-------------------------------------------------
:::Game Name::: Skate
-------------------------------------------------
:::GAME URL::: http://www.gamespot.com/xbox360/sports/skate/review.html
-------------------------------------------------
:::The Good:::
 Trick and control system is unique and a lot of fun.
 Good graphics and animation help make the game feel a bit more realistic.
 Decent voice acting and choice sound effects.
 Community features make sharing your exploits easy and fun.
-------------------------------------------------
:::The Bad:::
 Some challenges make demands that are a little too specific for the analog trick system.
 Online events often clump too many skaters into too small a space.
 Load times and menu animations often get in the way of your skating.
-------------------------------------------------
:::Date::: Sep 17, 2007
-------------------------------------------------
:::Scores::: 
GameSpot Score: 7.5
Critic Score: 8.6, 65 Review (s)
User Score: 8.7, 3,953 Vote (s)
-------------------------------------------------
:::Addition:::
Publisher: EA Games
Developer: EA Black Box
Genre: Skateboarding
Date: Sep 14, 2007
ESRB: Teen

-------------------------------------------------
:::Review:::
Skate's analog trick system is revolutionary for the genre, but the game surrounding those mechanics 
 isn't quite as good. 

  Plenty of skateboarding games have come and gone in the years since the long-running Tony Hawk 
 franchise reinvented the skateboarding game. Most failed because they simply attempted to duplicate 
 the arcadelike fast-moving gameplay of Activision's series. After running unopposed for years, 
 Activision's got some new competition in the form of Skate from Electronic Arts. At times, this 
 simulation-styled skating game feels like it was built from the ground up to be the anti-Tony Hawk, 
 and aside from both games taking place on skateboards, the two don't have a whole lot in common. 
 This is largely thanks to Skate's very cool control system, which puts all of the meaningful controls 
 on the controller's two analog sticks and triggers. It's an awesome system that makes tricks feel 
 more involved and entertaining. Unfortunately, you'll be applying this control scheme to a series 
 of challenges and goals that aren't quite as good.  

           If you mess this trick up, be prepared to see a color-coded list of the bones you've broken. 

  Skate puts your skater movement onto the left analog stick. The right analog stick controls how 
 you move and flip your skateboard to do tricks. For a simple ollie, you hold down on the stick 
 to crouch then snap it up to jump into the air. Kickflips and heelflips are accomplished if you 
 come up slightly left or right of center. Shuvits happen when you hit down to crouch, then roll 
 the stick around to the side and up to the top. These are the basic tricks, but they get significantly 
 more complicated. The triggers are used for your left and right hands, so when you're in the air, 
 you can use these buttons to perform grabs. Once you've grabbed onto the board, you can tweak it 
 around with the right stick for different types of grabs. It's an instantly intuitive system with 
 the depth to keep you going for some time, but it isn't perfect. A lot of the tricks are done in 
 extremely similar ways. So when some goals call for specific tricks, like a Nollie 360 Flip, you 
 might find yourself attempting the trick again and again, only to have some other trick come out. 
 This gets totally frustrating in spots, especially in S. K. A. T. E. competitions, where you have to 
 duplicate someone else's trick exactly to stay in the game.  

  Grinding in Skate is as simple as lining yourself up with a rail or curb, getting airborne, and 
 landing on the grindable edge. Well, it sounds simple on paper, anyway. In practice, you'll have 
 to really work to line yourself up because the default camera is a low, off-to-the-side angle meant 
 to duplicate the look of a dude following you on his own board, holding a video camera the whole 
 time. Your skater is large on the screen, meaning he'll block a lot of your view; he doesn't seem 
 to become transparent often enough to let you get a clear view of the action at all times. Also, 
 Skate is very big on timing. The height of your ollies or other tricks is dependent on how long 
 you crouch and how fast you snap the stick up. It'll take some time before you're hitting every 
 rail, flipping in and out, or landing in manuals all over the place. The whole system is also purely 
 skill-based. You don't receive skater statistic boosts, unlock new tricks, or the like. Everything 
 is available right off the bat. The only stat that increases is your own personal skill with the 
 sticks.  

  There's a loose story to Skate's career mode. It opens with you getting slammed by a bus and going 
 in for surgery. This justifies the way you can reconfigure your skater's face and body type in 
 the typical EA style of analog sliders. Once you're back on your feet, you're out to get noticed, 
 so it's time to start recording footage and winning events. The different goals in the game give 
 you some variety, but you'll have to get good at all of them if you want to get to the top. Because 
 you're trying to get covered by two different skateboarding magazines, you'll have to complete 
 a lot of photo goals, which ask you to perform specific tasks on specific objects. Some of the 
 tasks are simple, like reaching certain point scores, while others will demand that you pull off 
 longer grinds, flip specific tricks into grinds, or land in manuals. You'll also encounter multiskater 
 competitions, such as timed battles for the most points, best trick contests, or slalomlike downhill 
 races. There are also free-form footage goals, where you're given a set of tasks that must be performed 
 within 30 seconds. The catch is that you can do these anywhere, so half of the process is figuring 
 out which part of the city is conducive to your task. Some of them require you to skate in no-skate 
 zones, which are patrolled by security guards who will push you over if they catch you. Some require 
 you to do huge grinds, do a lot of spins, remain in the air for 10 seconds, and so on. The film 
 goals are probably the trickiest ones in the entire game.  

  As you make your way through the game, you'll open up additional skate spots within the city, including 
 such indoor locations as the Plan B Warehouse and the X Games Stadium. Aside from entering these 
 indoor locations, you can skate around the city without seeing a loading screen. But if you decide 
 to warp right to a location, you'll see some somewhat lengthy load screens. The distance that you 
 can warp without loading also seems a little random. Some goals have you skate long rails or cover 
 what doesn't seem like that much ground, but if you try to warp back to the other side of the goal, 
 it'll stop and load. When you're stuck on a goal and trying it again and again, the loading becomes 
 really grating, as do the unskippable menu animations that pop up when you fail a film goal. This 
 all sounds like small stuff, but it really gets magnified when you're stuck trying the same thing 
 over and over.  

  In addition to the career mode, you can play several multiplayer events, such as jam, which is 
 a timed session that is won by the highest scorer. For these events, the city gets broken down 
 into smaller areas. A couple of jam locations are in fairly small areas, like residential-sized 
 pools. When the game sticks you into these spots and there are six players in the game, it just 
 becomes chaos. This is because there isn't enough room to skate and you're left constantly bumping 
 into other skaters, which isn't much fun at all. You can also play S. K. A. T. E., get into best trick 
 contests, races, and so on. The online performance can be a little spotty and seems to really depend 
 on the connection speeds of the other players, as well as your own. This means that one player 
 with a slow connection speed can bring the whole game down. In a game that's so focused on accurate 
 timing, it's pretty lame to randomly drop into slow motion. But when it's all working, it's decent. 

  There is also a community aspect to Skate. You can use a replay editor to capture video footage 
 of your performances or snap screenshots at any point and share them publicly. These can then be 
 viewed through a menu in the game or through the game's Web site, which is nice because the person 
 you want to show your skating exploits to doesn't need a copy of the game to see them. These items 
 can be rated and commented on, which is a sharp idea that expands on the sorts of things that EA 
 has done in the past with Burnout or some of its sports games. The only catch is that, as of this 
 writing, the Web site is sluggish and pretty buggy, making it hard to navigate, as well as see 
 the best footage.  

  Visually, Skate has a realistic look to it that fits with the overall atmosphere of the game. The 
 skaters look good and the animation is great, though a few of the up-close talking segments that 
 show polygonal versions of real-life skaters look a little weird. It all runs at a solid speed 
 that really makes you feel like you're booking when you're in some of the downhill races.  

  Like other sports games, Skate is filled with plenty of sponsored equipment and other product 
 placement. For the most part, it feels fine; getting sponsored by board and shoe companies is an 
 integral part of the game's career mode and that part never feels too salesy. But it crosses the 
 line in a few spots, like whenever you meet a pro skater. It shows that skater skating a line, 
 doing some nice tricks, but then it also zooms up to give you a very deliberate view of his skateboard, 
 trucks, wheels, and shoes, flashing the sponsor logos on the screen all the while. Also, there's 
 a weird bit of reverse product placement in the game because EA and Adidas teamed up to produce 
 some limited-edition shoes. These are introduced and advertised in the game, complete with promotion 
 codes that get you $50 off on them when you beat the skaters that endorse them. It's awfully blatant, 
 but it's actually pretty unique. It helps that the shoes are sort of rad. The game also downloads 
 new ads for billboards and other surfaces as you play, though there aren't enough different ads, 
 resulting in some cases where you'll see the same stupid billboard 10 times as you skate up a single 
 street.  

           After you edit your replay, you can put it online for others to view and rate.      

 
  The soundtrack is a really weird mix of music that doesn't actually play through most of the game. 
 On the default settings, music is ambient. This means that whenever you get close to a skate-friendly 
 spot, where skaters might gather and actually have a radio, you'll start to faintly hear music 
 coming from the direction of the spot. If you like, you can set it to directly play the music, 
 but most of the soundtrack is a little sketchy, and the way the game opens with Booker T &amp; 
 The MG's "Green Onions"  every single time  you load up the game makes you feel like you're turning 
 on some awful Jim Belushi movie rather than getting ready to play a realistic skateboarding game. 

  Aside from the weird soundtrack, the in-game audio is really great. There are lots of great skateboarding 
 noises, especially the way the wheels skid when you do powerslides or land hard and turn. The game 
 also has something like color commentary, which comes from the invisible kid that's "holding" the 
 in-game camera. He'll call out to other pros as you pass by, congratulate you on good trick lines, 
 comment when you stack and break some bones, or impatiently whine when you set the controller down 
 then walk away. His presence is pretty good and gives the game some personality.  

  While Skate has a handful of issues that hold it back, it has an absolute ton of potential. It's 
 a great first start for what hopefully will become a regular franchise. With some more refinement 
 and a few more things to do, this could probably be the best skateboarding game around. It's definitely 
 worth playing, if only to get your hands on the trick system, but if you're stingy with your money, 
 you could probably get enough out of it with a rental.

UserName: Murj
Rating: 7.5
Date: Mar 19, 2009 3:33 pm PT
Review:  As next gen gaming cam around, it wasn't just the graphics that became revolutionised. The way 
 games are played has changed and that couldn't be more true for EA's Skate.
  
  In Skate you control a skateboarder who has just come out of hospital after suffering a horrific 
 accident while skating. Magically fixed by your doctors, you naturally go back to what nearly killed 
 you in the first place. Your goal is to make a name for yourself in the world of skateboarding, 
 which is set in lovely San Vanelona. San Van is a big, big city comprised of four main parts. Each 
 part of the city has it's own theme whether it's big hills or plazas. As well as skating everywhere 
 (which is great to do because venturing upon your own private spot and continuously trying to own 
 it is great fun) , San Van offers a subway system which lets you travel to any part of the city 
 for free. Otherwise in your backpack you can select the map to hop to any part of San Van you'd 
 like. This might eventually become your main means of transport if you don't like skating up hills.
 
  
  Advancing in this game means winning all the contests, owning spots and getting footage. By doing 
 all this you attract the attention of sponsors. This advances the game, unlocks new items and gives 
 you extra cash bonuses if you wear and use the merchandise supplied by your sponsor if you win 
 challenges, events or own spots.
  
  The heart of Skate is in it's control system where you use your left and right analog stick, combined 
 with the left and right trigger for the bulk of the controls. Your left stick directs you, while 
 your right stick controls the board. Different rotations and flicks of right stick will allow you 
 to perform different tricks, or tweak your grab moves if you're already using a trigger. Although 
 the feel is far more realistic than the Tony Hawk series, it still feels a bit exaggerated which 
 in all fairness does make the game better.
  
  Manuals and grinds are also possible with the analog sticks. By slowly leaning backwards or forwards 
 on your right analog stick, you can perform manuals. Just be careful manualing down hills. Grinds 
 are as easy as lining yourself up to the rail and ollying onto them. By holding your right stick 
 in a certain direction, you can control what sort of grind you'd like to pull off. 
  
  As with most games, you'd expect the difficulty to gradually increase as you play. This is the 
 same with Skate however, it really does crank it up. Which is where the problems start. Because 
 many challenges have specific requirements and because many tricks are similar to eachother; the 
 challenges can become quite tricky. There are no stats either, so the only thing that can get you 
 past each challenge is by practising. Practice makes perfect so they say; this should be on the 
 back of the game. If you have the time devoted to playing this game then you will be rewarded. 
 However if you do not have the luxury of playing your 360 as much as you'd like to then this game 
 may become a chore.
  
  After a while where I couldn't complete challenges I just started finding my own private spots 
 to skate at. Allow me to say this. Trying to skate the perfect line over and over again if just 
 as much fun as (if not even more fun than) completing the story. Owning in-game spots are cool 
 but when you find your own private spot it's that much sweeter. Best part is, once you've done 
 your line or had a massive bail or even something amazingly stupid you want other people to see 
 then you can edit and upload your replay to Xbox Live. Other people will be able to see you owning 
 your private spot, getting wrecked by cars or whatever. However, even this becomes a chore after 
 a while; so if you get bored of this and can't finish the story then the game can become stale 
 pretty quickly.
  
  Online play is also pretty good with different races and events for you to play, ranked and unranked 
 alike. Skate definitely has one of the tightest online communities around, although it's one of 
 the smallest.
  
  EA Skate is an interesting step in a new direction for the skateboarding genre, one which I'd love 
 to see develop. If you have enough time on your hands to practice and master this game then I'm 
 sure you'll have nothing but good times. But if like many people you simply don't have the time 
 then completing this game may seem like a distant dream.

UserName: mjstokes85
Rating: 9.5
Date: Feb 6, 2009 1:28 am PT
Review:  I am not a real skater, although, i do love to watch, and am fascinated by real skateboarding. 
 There is an art to it, an addictive quality that when you set out to do a trick, you must do it, 
 no matter how many times you fail. Skate captures that so well. Real skating is not about nailing 
 a trick first time, it's about falling off your board 40 times, getting closer and closer to perfecting 
 that trick, then finally doing it, and feeling a huge sense of accomplishment. That is what skateboarding 
 is, and that is what skate is.
  
  Back in the day i was a Tony Hawks fan, i loved the early games, 1,2,3 and 4, but as time went 
 on, the game lost it's way. It just wasn't fun anymore. Skate brings the fun back. The use of the 
 analogue stick to do tricks is a simple, yet superb concept. It makes mastering the harder tricks 
 very tough. But that is skating! The hard tricks are, well, hard.
  
  The story in the game is predictable, your rise to skating fame from a nobody, but it is done well. 
 The challenges are varied, some easier than others, some are very hard, but that is where you require 
 patience. If you have no patience you can forget completing the story mode of this game and just 
 hit up the free skate instead.
  
  There is plenty to do, plenty of hot skating spots that can be unlocked (and trust me, the further 
 you get through the story, the better the unlocks) .
  
  The graphics in Skate are superb, the menus are solid and the sounds are particularly impressive.
 
  
  What is bad about skate? Well it is hard to find too much wrong, but the frame rate can sometimes 
 drop, and the game will stutter, but this for me has been rare. It can get frustrating at times 
 to do challenges, but for me that is part of the fun.
  
  Make sure you use your sessions marker, an excellent feature that allows you to virtually "save" 
 a spot you were stood in and instantly go back to it. This is very handy when for example you are 
 trying to grind a rail on some steps and there is no way back up to the top other than a long trip 
 around the back of a building. The session marker can be set at the top of the steps so if you 
 bail you can instantly go back to the top and try again.
  
  Skate is a game you need to play over and over to perfect. You WILL eventually be able to nail 
 those hard tricks, it takes time, practice and LOTS of patience.
  
  I can not comment on the online play as i am not a gold xbox live subscriber, but i am sure it 
 is just as much, if not more fun than single player.
  
  Skate is a masterpiece of modern gaming, anyone remotely interested in skating should play this 
 game!
  
  9.5/10

UserName: Pwnd56
Rating: 10
Date: Jan 16, 2009 11:03 am PT
Review:  I don't think I have much to say about this game, you have to get it for yourself, but I will try. 
 Tony Hawk has been the skating behemoth for many years, and it took just one EA game to take it 
 down. Skate is the realistic experience that both gamers and skaters alike have been waiting for! 
 Instead of pressing some stupid button combo to get a hardflip, you have to do it yourself, with 
 the revolutionary "flick it" controls. To get an ollie (jump for skating game newbies) you simply 
 hold the right analog stick down, and flick it up as fast as you can. You also have to flick it 
 opposite for nollie (front bend jump for skating game newbies) , and in many different directions 
 for flips. You also must just barely push the stick up or down for a nose/manual. This is hard 
 at the start, but in a while, you will get it. This game makes you feel freaking awesome after 
 a simple combo, unlike TH. In TH, you could land a 900 mctwist, and be like, "meh, what do I have 
 to do next," when, in skate, if you landed a blunt grind on a high ledge, and jumped off with a 
 hardflip, you would be like, "Oh, my gosh, I can't believe I pulled that off!" Besides the skating 
 mechanics, which are all the game is really about, it has good graphics, a good soundtrack, and 
 completely awesome levels!! Also, there is this thing that you get in career mode if you bail hard 
 enough, called Hall of Meat, which will show the bones you break. This game is currently owning 
 the sports games, incase you don't know, and it is definately the best skating game ever, even 
 if there is an annoying cameraman that folllows you all the time, and yaps all the time, it is 
 worth your money.

  I was hoping this game would be similar to the great '' Tony Hawk's Pro skater 2 '' on the PS2

 game.

 this game to anyone.

UserName: iamnessie
Rating: 8.5
Date: Jan 11, 2009 5:47 pm PT
Review:  Skate definitely changes skateboarding games and put the nail in Tony Hawk's coffin.
  
  It starts out with a your skater getting hit by a bus. Then a great FMV with all of the pros in 
 the game in different roles (my favorite is Chris Haslam online shopping) all being shown while 
 you're being taken to the hospital.
  After you arrive the nurse asks you to enter all of your info into a T-Mobile Sidekick in the first 
 of many blatant products placements.
  
  The story is pretty generic for a skating game: you have challenges, contests, photo shoots, etc.
 
  But you don't really play skating and sports games for the story do you?
  
  Graphics are okay. 
  Everything looks nice from far but up close... not so much. Bushes and trees 
 are actually flat, you can't see your reflection in glass, and the 'make everything shiny' rule 
 applies here. 
  Your character looks good but not any of the people in the surrounding world. There are only about 
 8 different people models in the worlds, so get used to looking at the same people.
  The map is another thing. Pathways and areas show up on it that aren't actually there. So if you 
 see a long path, there could be actually be a wall or bush.
  
  i enjoyed most of the soundtrack. The menu loading music is a muzac piano version of other songs, 
 "Give It To Me Baby" by Rick James and NWA's "Express Yourself" are 2 examples. "Express Yourself" 
 was actually in Tony Hawk 4 if anyone remembers.
  The filmer has great comments on when you get injured an after awhile it's the same old stuff over 
 and over. But before it gets old, he does have a lot of different things to say depending on the 
 situation.
  
  Gameplay:
  the trick system, Flick It is what's really important in this game. 
  It works out perfectly 
 but it does take a long time to get used to and is nowhere as simple as other skate games. 
  One big problem is you long for the ability to get off your board like in the last 5 Tony Hawk 
 games. You get caught in the middle of areas that can be impossible to get out of. It's really 
 annoying and is nothing like the realism they're trying to portray.
  They did try making a realistic game which means you can fall 100 feet without crashing. Physics 
 are pretty realistic. If you're going fast, you can easily lose control and fly into a wall.
  
  This game reminds me alot of a new millenium version of Rockstar's Thrasher: Skate and Destroy. 
 i loved that game just because of the realism of the tricks.
  If realism without a 50 trick combo sounds good to you, try it.
  This is indeed a realistic sports 
 game like Madden rather than a Blitz.

UserName: ssf4gnarlybrown
Rating: 9.5
Date: Dec 22, 2008 3:37 pm PT
Review:  Skate is one of the most amazing things since sliced bread. I don't know what that means but i 
 heard one of my teachers say it the other day. Anyways, Skate revolutionized the way skateboarding 
 video games should be made. In career mode, you start out as a character that recently got injured 
 and had lots of surgery. Your character skates in a place called San Vanelona, which is a skateboarding 
 mecca. You first begin actually skating like your character doesn't know how to skate (because 
 of the injury) and you must learn all the basics again. After that, you start getting challenges 
 that you must complete in order to get further in the game. You slowly work your way up to become 
 a pro skater and become one of the legends of San Vanelona. 
  
  The creators of Skate also invented the Flick-It system, in which you use your right analog stick 
 to make the board flip. For example, if you are skating regular footed in the game and flick it 
 down and up to the right, you will do a heelflip. This is much simpler and more realistic than 
 in Tony Hawk where you have to push A then press X and move your stick to the right just to do 
 a heelflip.
  
  The only problems that i see with this game that aren't being changed for Skate 2 are that it's 
 somewhat difficult to get used to and when the game loads it takes awhile. The Flick-It system 
 is undoubtedly more realistic than Tony Hawk's gameplay, but it can be difficult to get used to. 
 In career mode, you must do some tasks that require you to do a specific trick like in Paul Rodriguez's 
 sponsorship challenge. You must do a nollie tre flip (360 flip) to a grind on a hubba. Luckily, 
 if you just press select and move down to the Trickbook in your backpack, you can see exactly how 
 to do tricks. In Skate, you can't get off your board, you can't move objects around, you can't 
 be a girl, and you can't do handplants, bonelesses, no complys, fingerflips, hippie jumps (hippie 
 flips are in Skate but they are very hard to do) , and some grabs. However, all of these aspects 
 have been added to Skate 2 which is being released January 21 of 2009. I have also heard that the 
 slow loading problem has been fixed for Skate 2 as well but i haven't heard of an official confirmation 
 on that yet. 
  
  Despite these problems, Skate was one of the best games of late 2007 and all of 2008 in my opinion. 
 It is extremely addictive once you get used to it. I play it all the time and i'm still not bored 
 with it, even though i can't wait for Skate 2 to come out. If you haven't played the game yet and 
 you have XBOX Live, download the demo. If you like the game and can't wait until January 21st, 
 then buy Skate, beat it, and buy Skate 2 on the 21st. If you don't have XBOX Live then i would 
 recommend renting it from your local video rental store or waiting until Skate 2 comes out. Whichever 
 case applies to you, i am sure that you will not regret it.

UserName: antipunt1
Rating: 8
Date: Nov 21, 2008 11:12 pm PT
Review:  Skate, for all its bad things, does many many good things. For once, it has awesome presentation. 
 It has great graphics, sleek menu/map, and YES fast travel. The animations and character design 
 is solid. Make no mistake, this is a very PRETTY game.
  
  And for the gameplay, I was astounded. I expected the analog controls to be some sort of a gimmick, 
 but they actually worked rather well. It was like... well. REAL skating. Very freaking hard. But 
 I could feel that people who were good at this game had to have good spatial perception and practice 
 similar to.. well.. real skating.
  
  This, however, is not a perfect game, take note. For one, I can imagine the controls being kind 
 of intimidating for new players. This game actually takes practice to get good at, and I can imagine 
 that alone being a turn off for many. Next off, this is, after all, just a skateboarding game with 
 a so-so story. Nothing 'epic' is expected in this territory.
  
  With that said though, after being so used to Tony Hawk storylines, I was VERY pleased to see skate 
 with its cool character presentation/voice acting, not to mention an actually involved story-style/pacing. 
 It felt.. well.. WELL put together. This wasn't some slop-job that I expected it to be.
  
  All in all, after a while, this game just got real fun. Multiplayer, single player, you name it. 
 Pulling off those 'simple compared to hawk' yet involving tricks were oh-so-satisfying. In short, 
 a skating game done right. VERY right. Beats any Tony Hawk game that I've ever seen. However, the 
 victory is not really a 'landslide' if you know what I mean.
  
  If Skate 2 can fix some of those issues (ex: running into people all the time, not being able to 
 walk off your board, making those kickflips/shove its not so dam similar) , if could potentially 
 knock Tony Hawk OUTTA the water

 mode revolves around a series of challenges including: Photo Challenges, Video Challenges as well 
 as Competitions. Although very well thought out the story mode may seem difficult to some because 
 of the going back and forth to find the locations of the various challenges. It all just takes 
 getting used to . The graphics are very nice and well animated, which take the game play to a whole 
 other level. Overall this game is Excellent I give it a 10.0 simply because it captures the essence 
 of skateboarding extremely well.

 2.

  Love the realistic Controls and physics, so much better than tony hawk.
  
  Game-play is great 
 and just add's such a wonderful idea to skateboarding games.
  
  Great music mixed with great graphics also give great back-up for a game with good game-play.
 
  
  I like how you don't have stats in this game to gradually increase. Your skill gets better based 
 on you learning new tricks and the old saying, try, try again.
  
  
  THE BAD
  
  
  There are Some things that might seem like they are small annoyances. But in truth they end up 
 really stall the game from being perfect.
  
  I absolutely HATE that yo can't get off your board in the game, I mean think about it, if you want 
 to get over a curb you have to ollie it every time, which may not seem that bad but if you see 
 an awesome 12 stair and the only way to get to it is ollie the curb then some how miraculously 
 ollie UP the set of stairs, that gets really annoying it makes it extremely hard to set up for 
 a lot of things.
  
  Also traffic and people SUCK, the areas that are the funnest to skate, are the ones that have the 
 most people to get in the way, I mean that is going with the realism theme. but actually if I saw 
 a guy going full speed to hit a set of stairs I'd jump out of the way, these people in the game 
 are just FEARLESS! They won't move for ANYTHING. You'll find yourself really frustrated after running 
 into people 25 times in the same area.
  
  The next thing is how hard the learning curve is. I mean with a game that changes what your use 
 to playing 100%. That is expected, but afer you finally stop hitting the A button on accident to 
 try and ollie (For us tony hawk fans.) then you realize that the controls are SO SENSITIVE! getting 
 a trey flip (360 flip) seems like just luck for the longest time. for skate 2 they need to give 
 you just a LITTLE bit more give, because if you don't get the flick EXACTLY right (for harder tricks 
 anyways) then you end up only doing a kickflip, or you end up doing a completely different trick 
 than you wanted to.
  
  
  OVER-ALL
  
  
  This is till an amazing games but I guess the faults of this are are pretty common for a game taking 
 it to a whole new level like this does. so I'm confident in saying I cannot wait for skate 2!

Review:  Skate, in my opinion, is a game that seemed to sneak under the radar a little bit. Most of that 
 is probably because a lot of people were still hooked on the Tony Hawk series. Although those games 
 are good, i honestly believe that Skate is the best skateboarding game out there right now. Don't 
 get me wrong, I enjoy an afternoon with my Playstation 1 and Pro Skater 2 as much as anybody else, 
 but those games were and still are to easy. By easy, of course, I'm talking about actually doing 
 the tricks. All it took usually, even for complicated tricks, was to memorize a combination of 
 2 to 3 buttons. That got old for me. While the analog system isn't perfect, it's certainly better, 
 in my eyes. At first, the system is hard to get used to, and it gets hard towards the end, but 
 its still much better i think. 
  
  Also, the map is great as well. The 3 parts or districts to the city was a very good idea. It keeps 
 things a little more interesting. Plus i love the fact that you can just roll up to a legendary 
 skater and challenge his and your skills in a game of SKATE. That might be my favorite part of 
 the game.
  
  Overall, this is an excellent game that, love it or hate it, will keep you entertained for many 
 hours.

::::::
UserName: Sess1on
Rating: 8
Date: Oct 6, 2008 12:24 pm PT
Review:  Tony Hawk games have ruled the genre since it's inception. Many incarnations have sprung up over 
 the years and dwindled away in the shadow of the ever popular Hawk series. Up until now. Intro 
 Skate. EA's prized Hawk-killer. And hot damn is it a welcomed breath of fresh air in the genre, 
 filled with both style AND substance. 
  
  Unlike the Hawk games, Skate's gameplay focuses on realism. You feel like you're actually skateboarding 
 when playing. And not only that, you feel like you're in an actual skate video with someone constantly 
 following you around, capturing your every move in a massive sandbox, and highly stylized free-roaming 
 city filled with every skateable piece imaginable.
  
  The art direction and style of Skate is typical for an EA game, which is a good thing. The soundtrack, 
 generally, has a well compiled playlist for those who don't use there own music. Customization, 
 while something that's not nearly as in depth as it could be, is great feature that no skating 
 game should be without. The story is nothing special, but then who plays a skateboarding game for 
 the story anyway? And of course, the revolutionary new control system is undoubtedly addicting 
 and fun to use.
  
  Though Skate isn't without its flaws. While fun and addicting, the game can become incredibly frustrating, 
 and not to mention annoying at times. The revolutionary new control system can be hard to imitate, 
 especially in a game of S. K. A. T. E. Doing the same trick twice takes practice. 
  
  The A. I. in Skate is horrific. It's almost like no one on the development team bothered to go to 
 a real skate park to see how traffic in the place works. Here's a hint; people don't just drop 
 in or skate what they please whenever. There's a waiting system. Otherwise, people run into each 
 other, constantly. Now, it's understandable that the player will break this rule. It IS a game 
 after all. But that doens't mean the NPCs shouldn't abide by this rule.
  
  Skate's camera man and narrator is one of the most annoying things in the game, simply put. It's 
 a feature that could been done away with entirely. I feel bad for those who played through with 
 his obnoxious voice blabber away the whole time.
  
  One aspect, as mentioned earlier, is the sheer size of the skateable environment. Like similar 
 large sandbox games, this one shares the same universal flaw; not taking proper advantage of all 
 of it. Sometimes I find myself in an area or on a path I never knew existed that's fun to skate 
 and wonder why it's not used for anything more than just being there. A lot of great places in 
 the city exist that could be used for S. K. A. T. E. and various other online game modes but aren't. 
 
  
  Flaws aside, Skate is a solid game. And for it only being the first, the series has a promising 
 future. Let's just hope it doesn't follow the same fate as the Hawk series, which I'm hoping comes 
 back with a bang. Because, as you know, competition is good for us; the gamers.

UserName: Sodney
Rating: 9
Date: Aug 31, 2008 1:03 pm PT
Review:  Skate is a game that is great for fans of skateboarding. It really captures the fun and frustration 
 of skateboarding, which is a good thing for fans of skateboarding but gamers in general might get 
 too frustrated at times.
  
  The graphics are great, the skaters are detailed and really look like the real pro skaters. The 
 movements of the skater also looks good.
  
  The sound in this game is some of the best I have ever heard. 
  
  The game has a fun story 
 that makes you want to play more. The story is kind of typical, get coverage and become a pro but 
 it is still very fun. The game also takes a while to complete. I spent approximately 15 hours to 
 complete the story but the replay value is infinite.
  
  There are a lot of cool sponsors in the game. You get a deck sponsor, truck sponsor, shoe sponsor 
 and a wheel sponsor. The cool thing is that you make the choice.
  
  Skate is definitely a must buy for anyone that enjoy real skateboarding. It is truly the most realistic 
 skateboarding game ever made. General gamers might not enjoy the frustration in the game but skateboarding 
 is supposed to be frustrating. If you enjoy the tony hawk games you really should try this one 
 out.

UserName: Large_Soda
Rating: 6.5
Date: Aug 25, 2008 10:30 am PT
Review:  Typically used as a quick getaway from committing a crime like shoplifting, or vandalism, skateboarding 
 has also become synonymous with videogames too. With Tony Hawk paving the road with 9 games in 
 their series, EA is now trying to capitalize on the market with their debut series Skate.
  
  There are many things to like about Skate on the surface, things like an inventive new analog 
 controls and more realistic moves for the criminals to attempt. You won't be able to perform a 
 900-silly-mcflip-a-la-douche in this game, no sir.
  
  One of the cute things I noticed in Skate immediately was how it made me feel like I was picking 
 up a skateboard for the first time. I could barely perform any tricks and I fell a lot. That trend 
 continued for while and in all honesty hasn't stopped. 
  
  And that is what I hate about Skate, it is geared to those that want to learn, to achieve, to follow 
 the creed "if at first you don't success, try, try again". Well that isn't me. I never pursued 
 skateboarding in real life, because it was too hard and now I'm doing the same thing in Skate.... giving 
 up.
  
  One of the beauties of Tony Hawk is that it lets you be better than great, immediately and when 
 you fail it ends up being funny. Anytime I failed in Skate I wanted to break my controller.
  
  I suppose this review can be read as me "sucking" at this game and fair enough, but I would 
 expect that answer after donating several hours of my life to the game, not the tutorial stuff. 
 From the word GO this game's learning curve is drastically high and that goes against everything 
 a quitter stands for.

UserName: VentyLight
Rating: 9.5
Date: Aug 18, 2008 9:18 pm PT
Review:  Skate by EA is a great new game in the skateboarding genre. Using the new flickit control scheme, 
 you can skate in ways that you never could in Tony Hawk.
  
  The gameplay is very true to life. You start out small and you get more and more coverage to become 
 an icon skater. You take photos, videos, compete in jams and best trick contests or you can just 
 be mellow and skate around the huge landscape known as san vanelona. The things that can be skated 
 in this game are not like tony hawk where you can grind a roller coaster or ride a pirate ship, 
 no in skate. you have to actually skate things that could be skated in real life like curbs, handrails 
 and more.
  
  The graphics in this game i thought were top notch with a little buggy bails but other than that 
 you shouold not be dissapointed. As well, the audio has a great mix of contact with different materials 
 on the ground, ramps, and rails and good voice acting seeing that the ones who are doing the talking 
 are pro skaters.
  
  Now most people say that the flickit control makes the game to hard to complete certain tasks. 
 Thats why you have to practice just like in real skateboarding. The more you practice, the more 
 you will do that tre flip over and over.
  
  So for those of you tony hawk fans out there, get ready because skate 2 is only around 6 months 
 away with new additions like handplants and you can get off of your board. 
  
  Skate is easily the best game i have purchased for my 360 so far. Great job EA and i cant wait 
 for Skate 2

UserName: IZZO71
Rating: 8
Date: Aug 17, 2008 8:28 pm PT
Review:  Before I say anything, I will say skate is far from perfect. However, it is a breath of fresh air 
 that rarely comes around in video games. For too long has the skateboarding genre been corrupted 
 by those horrible tony hawk games and man are they bad. In proving grounds Ive landing on a rail 
 with my head before and somehow managed to grind it?!?
  Skate isn't a perfect skateboarding simulation ( I can do flips off 2 foot high ramps) , but it is 
 certainly light years closer than tony hawk. Just everything from the flip tricks to the grinding 
 feels authentic and like you are actually skating.
  A lot of my friends mention the camera and that it is hard for them to align themselves with rails 
 because the camera is low and off to the right. However I never really had a problem with it so 
 it is what it is.
  The graphics on the game are quite nice. The colors are very bright and the lighting is very good. 
 The textures on the ground and on objects are not really all that impressive; but the shine effect 
 that is added to the rails and the polished granite steps and floors when the lighting hits them 
 makes up for it. 
  I am glad to say that most of the flaws in this game are being fixed in the second game. The nagging 
 want to get off your skateboard will finally go away as you can now leave your skateboard in the 
 second game. Also the horrible falling animations will be replaced by your character actually bracing 
 themselves and a sense of self preservation. I also hope they tweak the flip stick a little bit. 
 A lot of times in skate when I want to do a 360 hard flip, it will end up making me do an Ollie. 
 This doesn't happen often but with the tricks being the most important part of the game, I would 
 like to see the controls as perfect as possible.

UserName: xbox360-reviews
Rating: 9
Date: Jul 24, 2008 6:00 am PT
Review:  I was never really a fan of the tony hawks games, because i had thug 1 and 2 on xbox, but i didn't 
 really like them. I always hoped that there would be another skateboarding game that would take 
 over and be more realistic. So when i heard there was a new skateboarding came coming out called 
 skate, i was immediately excited and i saw the trailer right away, and i was even more excited. 
 The storymode of skate is not amazing but its acceptable. You play the role of a skater who has 
 had an accident on a set of starirs and you have to make it back to the top, doing challenges to 
 earn sponsors, and thats basically it. You get to create your own character, so you can make the 
 character looklike you or make a completely random one. The first time i played skate i actually 
 had to think, am i playing a game?, because the graphics of the environments are very detailed, 
 and the effort that ea have put into the gameplay is very good and reflects the realism of real 
 skateboarding. The main thing that sets skate apart from tony hawks is the control scheme which 
 is called the flickit control, and it has a very innovative feel to it. So you use the right anolugue 
 stick to carry out the tricks in your arsenal, and although it can be tricky, when you have mastered 
 it, the tricks become very satisfying. All good skaters have a skate vid right?, so ea actually 
 pushed my expectations and included a feature called the skate reel, and this lets you create your 
 own clips of your character or a pro if you wish so. you can also share this with friends online 
 and any of your photos that you have taken of the skater in action. The only thing really that 
 slightly dissapointed me about this game is that there is no offline split screen freeroam, instead 
 there is a game mode called s. k. a. t. e, where you do tricks and if your firiend doesn't make the 
 trick on his first and only attempt he gets a letter. The online makes up for it though because 
 you sort of get this freeraom thing but its still only one player, and s. k. a. t. e, and races. There 
 is also a mode where you see who can get the most points in a pool. So for a first attempt this 
 game deserves credit, and who cares if you can't snap your board, or get off your board, or do 
 a darkslide, or skate in nightime, its whats there that counts, and its fantastic. P. s the mega 
 ramp and xgames are very well implemented into this game and they are a good reward for completeing 
 the game.

Review:  Skate. is simply the most realistic skateboarding game ever. Tony Hawk can't compare to this realistic 
 an unique skateboarding experience. The analog "flickit" controls make you feel like your really 
 skating. They are fluid and very real. The graphics are very realistic and the skating animations 
 are superb. The wrecks, though, are very unrealistic and annoying. But it isn't as unrealistic 
 as project 8 with the skaters bouncing all over the place. Though that is fun a little.
  What also makes it very much like actual skating is the sounds. The sound as you hit the pavement 
 is so real that you might feel like your really in the game. The kick flip, heel flip, and all 
 the other tricks look just like their real like counterparts. This game is a must have for all 
 hardcore skating fans.

Date: Jul 18, 2008 10:47 pm PT
Review:  Set in a vast, vibrant, sunny skater paradise that never rains, snows, thunders, or, even has nightfall, 
 Skate takes away the gimmicky cities in past skateboard games (can you guess which?) , that always 
 somehow seem to feature perfectly placed ramps in random places, and brings a new, exciting edge 
 into skating games: realism.
  
  Skate is the 'simulation' to Tony Hawk's 'arcade' style, that throws away the silliness, and smacks 
 you in the face with a harsh dose of reality. Gone are the days of 80,000 point combos, and in 
 are the days of being hopeful to land a kickflip into a grind. With this change, also brings a 
 good deal of satisfaction on landing such things, and makes landing long lines and impressive air 
 even more rewarding. But of course, not landing your tricks will introduce you to the painful looking 
 ragdoll physics, which can make every wipeout something to laugh or cringe at.
  
  The controls are something that halt a new player instantly. Being a skateboard game, anyone who's 
 ever played a skateboard game before this know it down pat, with buttons being the main use. Skate 
 throws out all you ever knew about skateboarding controls, and introduces an innovative new way 
 to play; the analog stick. Strange, new and awkward at first, repeated playing will warm you up 
 to it, and you'll wonder how you ever lived without it. It's a dynamic system, of course not without 
 its flaws, but a very interesting take on controls.
  
  The graphics follow the next-gen formula of gritty but vibrant, dirty but real. The camera is awkward 
 at first, but 30 minutes into the game, and you're already used to it. Sound is top notch, and 
 bails are bone crunching.
  
  This is one of those games that deserves it's place in your library. It's just something that's 
 very hard to get sick of, and being such a massive game, it'll take you months to even get a taste 
 of what can fully be unlocked and explored in this game. 
::::::

::::::
UserName: TFrieden0928
Rating: 8.5
Date: Jul 16, 2008 10:42 am PT
Review:  NOTE TO READERS: I've been beating around the bush with most of my reviews because they deserve 
 the time and effort to explain my experience with the game, But its very different with sports. 
 I'm gonna get straight towards the point, and not fiddling around with it, just because there isnt 
 too much to explain. The review is lengthy but not as my others. enjoy.
  
  SKATE:
  
  Skateboarding was and never will be an intergrated part of my life, I've never got into the whole 
 idea of breaking your bones over a stupid surfboard on wheels, but I dug the Tony Hawk Franchise, 
 and I love Great videogames, so purchasing this game wasn't a real struggle, even though I didn't 
 know what to expect. Honestly, the game is phenomanal, its a new innovation of the genre, as well 
 as a good start. But its still very flawed, but the experience is no where near broken. In past 
 skateboarding titles, you will spend most of your time mashing buttons. Like seen in the TH series, 
 but those mechanics are thrown out the window and EA has made a control scheme that is innovative 
 and fun, that absorbs you into the experience, and in the role of an actual skater. When you bomb 
 a hill, you'll feel it, when you perform your flips and grabs you'll have to achieve it, and so 
 on. Its not just tapping buttons and performing tricks out the boom, you actually have to get good 
 with it. There is a sense of accomplishment that I felt everytime i landed something. And thats 
 a feeling that is unexpected, the whole game is challenging, but that makes it more of a satisfying 
 achievement. The controls are the most crucial part of the game, as it is also very complex. The 
 right stick is used for your board, and the left stick is used for your body. To perfom ollies 
 you hold down the right stick and flick it straight up, by doing variations of flicking, you perfom 
 various flips. while in the air you rotate your body using the left stick, it takes a ton of practice, 
 and lots of patience cuz the game doesn't let you get off easy. Netting high scores is a combination 
 of both, rotating and the type of flip or flips, you can also enter manuals as you land, by slightly 
 tilting the stick up or down, creating a combo. Grabs are split between your right and left hands, 
 and they are associated with the obvious bumper, you can rotate, and flip using the left stick, 
 and the right stick variates your grab. Grinds are much harder to perform, because of it timing, 
 but everything will fall into place and you'll soon be dishing out comboes and achieving high scores. 
 Just like in real skateboarding, you have to practice to get good. Everything is laid out in the 
 begining with no stat enchancements or new trick aquireing, the only obstacles blocking your sucess 
 is your abilities with the controls, and reality itself.
  
  Career mode is the most best part of the game, and probaly the mode you'll be playing in the long 
 run. Its decently long, and will take up to about 30hrs to fully experience it, but its well worth 
 it. For a skateboarding title. Just like the first TH underground, EA stole the idea, or borrowed 
 the "obvious" idea of what the story is about. You are a low down skater trying to reach fame and 
 fortune, scoring magazine covers, pics, film, events, sponsors along the way. The story kicks off 
 in a hilarious cutscene, leading to reconstructive surgery, and everything ties in to start your 
 journey. The game is thankfully not bound by generic levels, but is in a very big city, it'll take 
 at least 10 minutes to skate from end to end. The world is very detailed, and you'll skate in a 
 wide range of locales and areas, such as bowls. skate parks, etc. while going to different parts 
 of town like the suburbs, the old city, downtown. etc. to get fame and money, you complete events 
 and challenges to get on exposed on either of two magazines. these challenges are fun but they 
 get a tadbit dull and have problems. Some events make you do a specific trick, but it is very hard 
 to due to the likeness of all the tricks motions, its horrible. some might even quit the game entirely. 
 but other events are very cool, such as the X-games and meeting a crapload of pros, and skate jams. 
 Best trick contest and s. k. a. t. e, not so much. You can also purchase clothes, assescories, shoes 
 and the create the look of your skater. Its much more advance than tony hawk, but too bad you cant 
 add your face.
  
  As for the visual and sound department, skate fairs well there too. The game's graphics are unbelieveble 
 comparing them to the Tony Hawk series. The world is well crafted and detailed, and the models 
 and their clothes are very much realstic, you can see the vintage details on the jeans, shoes etc. 
 And everything lights up well too. The camera is a tadbit annoying, but its zoomed in on the lower 
 body, giving a up close and personal look, but its sometimes hard to see the road ahead of you. 
 The music and sound effects are very good too. Artists and bans like nirvana, dr. dre, n. w. a are 
 all in the game, and there is nothing better than the sounds of your board. The voice work is solid, 
 and the framerate is smooth.
  
  Online, Freeskate, and replay modes are all welcome additions, online is solid, not the best but 
 its worth a try. The real worthy extra is the replay editor, find something thats deserves to be 
 displayed to the world? upload it youtube style, and save anything you do, rate videos, watch em, 
 its all possible.
  
  Conclusion: Skate is a must own title for hardcore skateboarding fans, and a good playthrough for 
 gamers. Its one of those games where it doesnt change the industry, but it improves its own genre 
 greatly. Its gonna be hard playing Tony hawk now. But the game is flawed. You cannot get off your 
 board, (yes, really!) the story has no branches, challenges and events are sometimes repetive and 
 plagued, and the controls are too alike to perfom various tricks, i still cant get that 360 flip! 
 but all problems be damned, Skate is a great experience.

UserName: Ressdude
Rating: 8.5
Date: Jul 13, 2008 2:17 am PT
Review:  Skate is one of the better skater games out there. It has good graphics and a fun story mode where 
 the objective is to get as many mags and front covers as possible. The most interesting thing in 
 skate is its control system. Where instead of button mashing in previous games such as Tony hawks 
 you must use the right and left analogue sticks for the primary controls. The left stick controls 
 your general movement and some tricks but the right stick is the hub of many of the tricks. For 
 example ollieing is a lot more fun to do by flicking the right stick perfectly than say tapping 
 the A button. Players are allowed to customise there characters to a certain degree, you can select 
 from hundreds of real make clothes, shoes, skateboards and all other skating accessories. 
  
  However, skate does have it's problems, It can be very frustrating when you need to get past 
 a flight of stairs but you can't get off your board so you have to go miles round to find a slope 
 or ramp. Also doing some of the advanced tricks can be difficult because they can be very close 
 to other trick gestures. The sound is generally good but can sometimes be a bit off put.
  
  All in all I find skate a game that will keep you playing for hours. It may have just a few things 
 that will get you mad but all in all a great game.

UserName: djburnzy1
Rating: 9
Date: Jul 8, 2008 6:43 am PT
Review:  Bringing to the table completely different game play to those familiar with the tony hawk series, 
 skate delivers, big time. With what seems as an endless supply of challenges ranging from death 
 races to photo shoots in combination with flawless graphical tricks and gnarly goory collisions 
 with street lamps, cars and even pedestrians. Skate is one of those games you feel as though your 
 hands have literally been glued to the controller.
  
  Beginning with what looks like the opening scenes to a movie, skate brings you into it's world 
 letting you fully customize your character from head to toe and even muck around with his clothes 
 and deck. Sadly there is no grip tape customization. Which I frowned at. Although skate picks up 
 with its vast range of somewhat stylish clothing.
  
  As far as game play fairs it took me a while to pick up on the conventional style of the game itself. 
 My fingers were fixed to the idea that grind was triangle and triangle was y. So that took a while 
 to get used to. Although once you get the basics down skate begins to feel really natural and simple. 
 
  
  One thing that really got me going with this game is the fact that the skater was missing the ability 
 to WALK. I mean i know the game is called skate but could you at LEAST take the time to add a little 
 tweaking so that this player could walk instead of having to skate everywhere. 
  
  Online side of things was fairly enjoyable. Although frankly I'm nowhere as good as some of those 
 players online. It seems those online achievements will have to wait a while. 
  
  The problem with some skating games is that sometimes they miss prizes for good efforts. Like i 
 get stuck on some of the videos in this game you have to do. i. e do like a 3000 combo and total 
 20s air with 6 grabs, and once I've finally completed it after an hour due to collisions with stupid 
 computer controlled random skaters i find myself cursing at what you actually get from all the 
 work put into it. If that makes any sense to anyone you deserve a medal.
  
  Although this may be the case you do get something that seems to be worth all the hard work in 
 the end and that of course is the X games stadium. (A massive ramp leading into a absolutely huge 
 half pipe with various grinds etc.) Also various other parks that you unlock serve great value 
 when trying to do videos.
  
  All in all, skate is an excellent trademark of skating game superiority. To all the tony hawk fans, 
 this is so much better. To all the haters, you'd be surprised and to all the fans of skate... keep 
 skate'n and see you online. (hopefully)
  
  peace out!

Review:  A new passage to a skating game aside from the year after year Tony Hawk series, Skate. has surpassed 
 the realism of any skate game before, but is it a good thing it is more real, read my review to 
 see!
  
  Gameplay - 8.5
  The gameplay is this game is really thrilling, you'll get used to the controls after an hour and 
 once you are use to the controls you'll get better, the best thing about this game is when your 
 finish a trick you feel like you actually did in real for example in past Tony Hawk series, doing 
 I don't know a double kick flip in Skate. is like doing a one million combo, it feels sweet, that 
 what I love about this game, the only thing I hate is that its so easy to bail and you can't get 
 off your board which kinda irritated me at first but I got used to it.
  
  Graphics - 9.0
  The graphics are well done, some parts of the city look unreal but that pretty much the only spots 
 and the glow of the sun is amazing, the only thing I would change is that it would can from night 
 time to day time instead of just being day all the time, but that is mostly it as well.
  
  Sound - 8.8
  The music in the game are extreme and very good, the sounds of your board moving 
 over the sidewalk is very realistic as well, when you crash into cars you could hear your skin 
 slide a cross the glass.
  
  Story - 8.5
  The story is very well done, its about your created skater building up your fame by doing challenges 
 with pros and other stuff, the only thing I would change is that in the game missions pop up after 
 a while, so you'll have to wait for awhile. The story is pretty long, which I enjoyed.
  
  Replay Value - 8.0
  The replay is very high, just because you can skate around and have some 
 freedom, but there will be nothing really to do after you finish everything in story mode, unless 
 you try to do achievements, which took awhile for me, but overall you could play for awhile after 
 you finish the story.
  
  Overall - 9.0
  Overall the game is very well done, and I really enjoyed it, I still play it to this day, and I 
 finished the story, and now I'm waiting for Fall 2008 to get the sequel to this game "Skate 2" 
 and I heard it will be improved, but for now get this game unless you want to get the sequel which 
 is coming out soon.

 mode is fun but missing something. Maybe its the whole work your way up. Or maybe im just so used 
 to Tony Hawk games. The whole game though is basically about the core of skateboarding. No skills 
 to get higher and no special tricks. Even though the right thumb stick does all the moves, it sometimes 
 feels like there isnt that many tricks. You also cant get off your board which again leads me to 
 say this game is all about skateboarding but it wouldnt hurt to be able to climb somewhere you 
 would like to skate on. Even though skate has a few flaws or thing left out, its still a really 
 good game. The game does have possibly the best replay editor in a game. The only problem though 
 is you dont have so many camera angles. The game feels real and unlike Tony Hawk where as you can 
 do 2 backflips 3 900's and 15 kickflips and land skate is a lot harder depending on who you talk 
 to. Skate grows on you and eventually you learn to love it. But I guess thats personal taste. Skate 
 feels good and has a fair amount of things to buy. Shirts, pants, shoes, boards, hats, wheels, 
 trucks, and various accessories. Unlike Tony Hawk where you can skate around in your underwear 
 skate is more serious and realistic which appeals to real skaters. Skate is a solid game that is 
 atleast worth a rent. If you love Skate then good news is there is going to be a sequel. There 
 is no downloadable content which may disapoint some but most of the time its all overpriced anyway. 
 If you dont feel like buying or renting it then there is a demo off Market place that lets you 
 have a taste of what skate has to offer. It cant hurt to try.

Review:  ok first off ill say im pretty biased here because im a skateboarder myself. i can be a pretty 
 harsh critic aswell and im quite picky at that.
  also i have a deep running hatred for the slackers at EA and their multiple flops (for me anyway) 
 like need for speed and their attempts at 007 recreation. ive been a long time player of the tony 
 hawk series ever since THPS1 and its always been my escape during those wet skateless days, but 
 there has always been something missing. in the games i always loved to play realistically but 
 the series could never do that for me. skate however does exactly what the tony hawk series could 
 not.

  i wont even bother with graphics, it's pretty much norm for games these days to be flashy.
  
 
  (Sound)

 is the fact the soundtrack only plays in key areas of skating, which kind of resulted in me just 
 hitting shuffle on itunes. it was a nice concept but it didn't work for me.

 boiled down a little too serious. that was expected. (Difficulty)

 goals but it wasn't crippling at the same time, so pretty balanced.

 a sequel comes out or my xbox breaks. it's just a fun and addictive little package.

 of a few large zones, all with unique skatespots, be it stairs, handrails, slopes, sketchy suburban 
 areas or monuments that were just created subconsciously for skaters. the game world is the best 
 aspect of the game, with surroundings to suit any of your skate rat cravings. along with the flick 
 it controls, the game play is truly a unique one. overall id say this game is especially appealing 
 to skateboarders or anyone who enjoys extreme sports really. it's as much a simulation as it is 
 a game, at least in comparison to the rest of the market. i hate to say it, but EA actually did 
 a good job with a game for once instead of sticking their massive f**k-up shaped foot in the project 
 and duplicating the same thing over and over until the market is drowning in bad nostalgia. 
  
  fingers crossed i haven't spoke to soon.

 a mega over-hyped game, it disapoints. The pretty graphics aren't enough to make up for the stale 
 chunky gameplay and the nasty mechanics. It's a pretty good step away from the Tony Hawk Series, 
 but still not a very good game.

UserName: StreetSurfer
Rating: 9
Date: Apr 13, 2008 7:04 pm PT
Review:  I just got this game recently along with my new Xbox 360. First off, i would like to say that this 
 truly is the Tony hawk Skate killer. The flick control is genius and the graphics are amazing. 
 Though there are some glitches here and there, EA will probably fix those in SKATE 2. But anyways, 
 right now we're focusing on SKATE. The whole career mode isn't as creative as Tony Hawk but it 
 is realistic. You basically have 2 real life skate magazines. And you have to do challenges to 
 work your way up and get coverages on those magazines by doing photo shoots and videos to get sponsored. 
 But choose wisely. You can do any sponsor challenge you want but you can only choose one of them. 
 And that sponsor will stay with you throughout the whole career mode. So it's not like you can 
 quit skating for one company and go to another. You will have sponsors for obviously the board. 
 Then you have sponsors for other things like shoes, trucks, wheels, clothing, etc. Along the way 
 you will get to do pro challenges starring Rob Dyrdek (and Big Black) , Paul Rodriguez (P-Rod) , 
 Mike Caroll, Chris Haslam, and Danny Way to name a few. After getting all these major coverages, 
 you get invited to such places like Danny Way's compound, the Plan B Warehouse, and the X-Games 
 the grand daddy of them all! The flickit control system is very nice. Almost all your tricks are 
 done on the right stick. To ollie, you have to pull the stick down and flickit straight up. For 
 a kickflip, you pull the stick down and flickit to the right, or left if you're regular. It is 
 truly amazing and a fresh breath from the button mashing days of Tony Hawk. Not to bash on the 
 Tony Hawk series because he is truly the one that set the standards of Skate games. SKATE just 
 basically took that and made it 10 times better and more modernized to fit the 2nd gen consoles. 
 SKATE. reel is a cool feature that adds to the overall of the game. Skate. reel is basically taking 
 videos that you got to edit and record on your game and upload it to the ea skate website for every 
 one to enjoy and rate. The only downside is the flickit control. As i said before, the flickit 
 system is revolutionary and fun. But the pro challenges that you do are sometimes just way too 
 specific, making your experience really annoying. Like sometimes you have to do a 360 flip to a 
 grind, you may end up doing a 360 shuvit because the flick controls are really similar. So it may 
 take you 15 tries to do a single challenge. But hey that's like real life right? All those cool 
 tricks you see in skate videos aren't always perfect, they just edit out the imperfections. So 
 sometimes it will take pro skaters 100 tries to work out a perfect grind or a perfect flip. Speaking 
 of grinds, there are also no grind buttons in SKATE. instead, you have to align yourself with the 
 rail and ollie or flip onto it like you'll do in real life. The left stick is your body that's 
 how you control how you land on the rail. Another con of SKATE is that there is no option to get 
 off your board and walk. It may seem like a small con but sometimes when you just don't want to 
 skate onto another side to just ollie of a flight of stairs you can't just get off your board to 
 walk up those stairs then ollie of it. SKATE is also missing some tricks like the no-comply, boneless, 
 impossible, and there are not much substantial lip tricks. I'm sure when SKATE 2 comes out in 2009, 
 it will fix these downsides. All in all, SKATE is a very fun game that will have you playing for 
 weeks and maybe even months because of the wide area (called San Vanelona) and the different kinds 
 of flick combos you can do. Definitely worth the 60 bux. 
::::::

::::::
UserName: Amar93
Rating: 6
Date: Mar 30, 2008 4:35 pm PT
Review:  It's hard not to compare Skate with the Tony Hawk series because the Tony Hawk series has been 
 the only skateboarding game available up until now. EA released Skate back in September of 2007 
 to compete the popular Tony Hawk franchise.
  
  Skate features the brand new Flick-It controls which makes the game way more realistic than the 
 Tony Hawk games. An Ollie is done simply by moving the right stick down, and then flicking it up, 
 hence the Flick-It name. The longer you are able to hold the right stick down, you'll get more 
 air as you flick it back up. It's more realistic than Tony Hawk's way, which is done by pressing 
 A. 
  
  Grinding is fairly simple. It's as easy as landing on the rail. Simply flick the stick up, and 
 land on the rail to do a grind. If you wanted to do a kickflip to a grind in Tony Hawk, you would 
 have to press A, then press X and flick the left stick left, and then press Y to grind. Whereas 
 in Skate, you move the stick down, flick it diagonally and land.
  
  The game opens up with a long movie, and you can't skip it. Your character is skating around until 
 a bus hits him. You are then put in an ambulance, and it introduces all of the skateboarders, some 
 of which you might not know unless you really follow the sport, and they play some roles. Then 
 it opens up with a customization option which allows you to create your skater.
  
  You'll get a wide variety of shirts, shoes, hats, and pants from different brand names to customize 
 your characters with. You'll also get a variety of board graphics, trucks, and wheels to customize 
 your board as well. The only downside is that the body customization is very poor. You'll get a 
 limited number of hairstyles and facial hair to choose from. So while the clothing has lots of 
 things to choose from, don't expect to make your character look exactly like you if that's what 
 you're aiming for.
  
  After you finish making your skater, you'll be taken to a short tutorial which will explain how 
 the whole Flick-It system works. Once you finish, you'll get a few challenges which are also tutorials. 
 Paul Rodriguez will teach you about nollies, Jason Dill will teach you manuals, and so on. You'll 
 also get to play a quick game of S. K. A. T. E which is similar to horse in basketball. Copy the trick 
 and land it. If you bail, you get a letter, and if they bail, they get a letter. Unless if it's 
 their turn, then it switches to you setting the trick. You'll then have to follow the same guy 
 to the elementary school to finish up with the tutorials. You'll follow a few skaters in the game, 
 and that is the most frustrating challenge because they won't just skate to the destination. They'll 
 swerve between cars, and take other routes and make it seem as if they don't want you to follow 
 them.
  
  The whole point of the game is to get noticed by the two magazines in the game, The Skateboard 
 Mag, and Thrasher. You start off as just some skater, and as you continue to do goals, you'll end 
 up making a name for yourself and get sponsors and even get invited to the X-Games.
  
  The whole sponsor thing is a great feature. As you get coverage in the magazines, you will eventually 
 get contacted by various sponsors. They'll want to sponsor you and have you wear their product. 
 The best part about it is not only that your sponsors gear is free to you, but you get paid for 
 using their product. So any event that you do that pays you, you'll get a bonus for your board, 
 trucks, wheels, and shoe sponsors.
  
  While all that may sound great, Skate is a very frustrating game. You'll often get challenges that 
 give you very poor directions and you'll end up replaying the same challenge over and over and 
 over again. Most of the challenges will make you want to claw your eyes out. You also get a nifty 
 little trick book which shows you how to do a particular flip trick, grind, or grab trick. They'll 
 show you how to do it for both stances, but it's always hard to do most. You'll flick the right 
 stick the same way that they showed you and they'll call it a different name. This is extremely 
 frustrating during the challenges where they want you to do an advanced flip trick into a grind 
 or something. 
  
  The game also has trouble differentiating between a frontside and a backside grind. If you land 
 in a grind and lower the right stick, they'll call it a backside. However, if you were to do it 
 again, they would call it a frontside. This, along with the tricks mentioned in the previous paragraph, 
 will definitely frustrate you if you are doing a challenge asking you to do a backside or a frontside 
 grind.
  
  To make the game more realistic, they added several spots known in the game as No-Skate-Zones. 
 There is at least one security guard patrolling the No-Skate-Zone and he'll chase you if he sees 
 you. If you get caught, you'll have to cough up $50. But the bad part is that most of the No-Skate-Zones 
 are really good spots to skate. But note that you'll have a lower chance of getting caught in a 
 big No-Skate-Zone than you will in a small zone.
  
  Skate will have challenges known as Jams. Jams are events in which skaters must do tricks to gain 
 the most points. But they mostly cram you in an area where you are guaranteed to hit someone. Along 
 with Jams, they also have races which really are not that fun. You have to go down a big street 
 or some other area hitting as many checkpoints as you can and being the first to the finish line. 
 You don't necessarily have to hit all the checkpoints, but it's highly recommended as you'll get 
 more time. You'll lose by either being in 2nd place or lower, or running out of time. 
  
  There is an Own the Spot feature which has you beating a preset score on an obstacle. These spots 
 are scattered all around the city, and since the whole map is open to you from the start, you should 
 be able to find all of them without even playing through the storyline. The only places that are 
 locked are the skate parks, but other than that, everything is open.
  
  Online is a pretty fun feature in Skate. There is a Skate. Reel which allows you to upload your 
 footage or photos onto the web for people to look at and rate. It's a really cool feature which 
 allows you to show off some of your best runs. You can also customize how slow you want the movie 
 to run, change the camera angles and the lighting. You basically get to mess around with a whole 
 bunch of stuff in the game.
  
  You'll also have online Jam Sessions, Own the Spot competitions, Best Trick, and races. If you 
 play one of the four events in the Trick events area, you'll gain experience which will raise your 
 rank. You start with nothing and you'll eventually go to Amateur, then Pro, then Icon. Once you 
 reach Icon status, you can't gain a higher rank. You can gain more experience points, but you won't 
 obtain a higher rank. The same applies for the Race events. To gain more experience, you'll have 
 to win the event, and if you place last, you'll get the least amount of experience points.
  
  Overall Skate is much better than most of the newer Tony Hawk games. It's more realistic, has 
 better control, and even has online. But the challenges just get frustrating and it's hard to land 
 the exact trick you want. And unlike Tony Hawk, you don't get better by assigning points to your 
 attributes, your skater will get better as you get better with the game, making it that much more 
 realistic.

Review:  Skate is a very unique, new skateboarding game that redifines anything in the skateboarding genre. 
 It is a nice change from all of the boring and repetative tony hawk games that haven't introduced 
 anything new in the series for a long time. The analog controls take a little bit of time to get 
 used to, but feel way better in the end and you will notice that it is a pleasant change. As you 
 advance through this game, you will be taught new tricks instead of just having to know them from 
 the start. If you are an owner of tony hawk's project 8 and a fan of the series, I would advise 
 you go exchange it right now and but yourself a copy of skate, you will be not only pleased at 
 your choice, but also refreshed. This game would appeal to people of all ages, as it is both fun 
 and a little bit challenging (but not too hard) and you can also pick your favorite skate companies 
 as your sponsors for those who like some better then others.

UserName: meconate
Rating: 9.5
Date: Mar 10, 2008 2:55 am PT
Review:  If your a fan of the Tony Hawk skateboarding games but your getting tired of the same old repetativeness 
 and unrealism that they now have to offer, it's time to move on and buy yourself SKATE.
  
  SKATE is not only the most realistic skateboarding game you'll ever come across, but the most fun 
 at that. Instead of adding stupid features like 'Nail-the-trick' that was seen in Tony's Project 
 8, SKATE keeps close to realism and pays close attention to gravity and physics making each trick 
 look so smooth. The only thing on SKATE that can be annoying at times is the whole trick system. 
 Although it works so well with the fact that you flick your right analog stick to do fliptricks, 
 use the left analog stick for your body movement and your Left and Right triggers for your Left 
 and Right hands, you'll sometimes find yourself getting stressed over landing certain tricks like 
 the annoying 360 flip where you have to swirl your right analog around and go straight up and... 
 and... well, it's just plain annoying at times. However, so is trying to land a trick in real life. 
 Practice as much as you can on the game, and you'll find yourself on the cover of magazines in 
 no time. 
  
  SKATE has lots to offer in skateboarding that the Tony Hawk series couldn't and never will.
