UserName: xXChronopolis
Rating: 9.5
Date: Feb 14, 2008 5:25 pm PT
Review:  EA redesigns skateboarding games with Skate. They do an incredible job at it too. All gamespot 
 can do is rag on it because why? who cares. The point is that this is the overall the best skating 
 game to date and I dont think anything will be surpassing it soon. 
  
  The flick system they use beats pressing a random assortment of buttons by far. It was about time 
 someone came up with using that as the main means of performing tricks and manuals and grinds, 
 etc. Kudos to the THPS series for somewhat introducing that in Project 8 and Proving Grounds but 
 EA has perfected this. 
  
  Not only does this game have a unique one-of-a-kind control system but the storyline and challenges 
 are not bad to boot. The challenges are not too hard but they will have you busy for awhile. The 
 soundtrack is a bit weird but that can be easily fixed by plugging your ipod in or playing music 
 from your hard drive. Even after beating all of the story and all of the challenges, i find myself 
 coming back to this game whenever I am bored. 
  
  If you are a skateboarder or a fan of skateboarding games. Check this game out.

UserName: PaladinJoo
Rating: 7.5
Date: Feb 7, 2008 7:45 pm PT
Review:  ... so it is a good thing that EA got that mechanic right in this game. For a rookie franchise, 
 this is actually a rather good first effort. 
  
  In .skate, you'll play as a skater working their way up the from unknown to sponsored skater to 
 skate legend. The game plays out in a sort of open ended city, where you'll be skating around completing 
 objectives like collecting skate footage and still pictures along with "Owning" special areas around 
 the city and facing other skaters in various skating challenges. Yes... the only focus of the game 
 is skating, and although I am often skeptical of games set in a single setting, for the type of 
 objectives and gameplay you're expected to execute in this game, it works wonderfully. 
  
  However, the "story" linking these activities together is pretty much non-existent, which is fine 
 for a skating game except that it TRIES to exist, and just fails with hokey dialogue and pseudo-slang 
 coupled with annoying characters and drab cutscenes that drag the overall presentation of what 
 is a really decent looking next gen title down. Still, with good character models and unique lighting 
 effects including use of several filters gives the game an overall visual design that is unique, 
 yet familiar at the same time.
  
  And the visual design is the only thing familiar about the skating in this game, because unlike 
 the Tony Hawk franchise, EA has opted for an entirely different, analog stick centric control scheme. 
 You'll be flicking the right stick to ollie and perform flip tricks, and using the triggers to 
 perform grabs. The game's controls are intuitive, but the learning curve behind the stick controls 
 are STEEP, and after hours of playing, don't expect to have learned to execute anything more than 
 a kickflip, shuvit, and other variations with any sort of regularity. The flips are all unlocked 
 at the very beginning of the game, it's just up to YOU to learn how to execute them, making a level 
 of challenge that's both a boon, and a hindrance. On one hand, it's all on you, not your character 
 or equiptment, to actually learn this games brand of skating, but on the other, if you're not nailing 
 those tricks with any sort of regularity, you're going to get very very frustrated, and that's 
 not any fun.
  
  .skate is a good first offering for this young franchise. Though it has it's flaws, it's definitely 
 got potential to be a rival to the crumbling Tony Hawk juggernaut. It gets a 7.5.

UserName: hillelslovak
Rating: 9
Date: Feb 2, 2008 9:17 pm PT
Review:  Ive grown tired of the Tony Hawk games, its just getting a little much. I wanted to play a game 
 that is pretty realistic. And when I wished for it, EA delivered. Skate has so many good features, 
 great graphics, good online, and its just plain realistic and fun to play.
  
  Gameplay- The gameplay is excellent. The manner in which you perform trick is similar to the fight 
 night boxing games, utilizing the control stick primarily. It works flawlessly, and it makes you 
 feel that you've accomplished something when you pull off a hard trick, unlike the mindless button 
 mashing of the Tony Hawk games.
  
  Graphics/Sound-Both are great. This game has excellent graphics, excellent lighting and good character 
 models. The sound is good as well. The soundtrack is a little strange (Rick James and Cheap Trick??) . 
 The skating and enviromental sounds are great.
  
  Fun/value-The story mode is pretty long, and all of it is fun. The online play is good. An excellent 
 addition is the replay editor. Since the game work on real physics, you can do just about anything 
 if you fall off your board and do some crazy flips, hit your balls on a pole, etc. 
  
  Skate is a refreshing change of pace focusing more on realistic skating, and is one of the must 
 have sports titles of the year.

::::::
UserName: -kazoku-
Rating: 9
Date: Feb 1, 2008 6:39 pm PT
Review:  by former 
  
  It's time to celebrate. "Why?" you ask? The last time something of this magnitude ripped through 
 the gaming universe we were all still worried about the Y2K bug and the end of the world being 
 brought about by our excessive reliance on electronics. The world was in turmoil, which is why 
 Tony Hawk Pro Skater was such a welcome sight.
  
  Yes, 1999 was a great year for skaters who were also gamers, gamers who were skaters, posers who 
 learned 'skate' speak by playing Tony Hawk, and everyone else got their hands on the revolutionary 
 sim. In recent years, however, the series has suffered somewhat from what seems like a lack of 
 purpose or sense of direction, which brings us back to the reason for the celebration: EA's skate.
 
  
  EA's skate is a revolutionary take on a genre the Tony Hawk series has had a monopoly on for almost 
 a decade. Skate follows the story of a skater who is befriended by a videographer after a near 
 fatal accident. This accident excuses the avatar customization you'll be able to do once you get 
 done watching the hilarious intro starring all the professional skaters featured in the game. No 
 worries, though, that's pretty much all you need to know about the story. It's basically nonexistent 
 from here on out.
  
  For those of you that need it, though, I'll go ahead and lay out the game's main objective. You're 
 trying to get coverage in two real world skate magazines, Thrasher and Skateboard Mag. Your ultimate 
 goal is to earn a cover shot on both of these magazines and skate in the X Games. If you choose 
 to you can avoid all that. The game is pretty enjoyable just skating around the fictitious, and 
 ridiculously large San Vanelona.
  
  The city has four major areas each with its own unique feel. You'll start off in the Suburbs. Lots 
 of houses, back allies, hidden pools and the like. There are a lot of rewards for the diligent 
 here. Then there's the Res. If you like the idea of bombing hills and becoming roadkill, the Res 
 is for you. Old Town is home to a lot of unique areas that lend themselves to anyone creative enough 
 to visualize that off-the-wall line. And, finally, Downtown, with its rails a plenty for grinding 
 goodness. There are also areas that are off-limits to skaters so watch out for security guards. 
 Like I said, just skating San Vanelona can be a blast
  
  That's not to say that skate is absolutely unstructured either. There are plenty of goal-oriented 
 tasks to complete, should you so desire. It's just as much fun to skate around aimlessly and look 
 for places to put together a fluid line, which, thanks to your trusty videographer and skate's 
 community features, you can then upload to the skate website to be viewed by others. (More on that 
 momentarily.)
  
  Skate's trick system has got to be the most revolutionary, intuitive and innovative system yet, 
 as it strikes a perfect balance between risk and reward that most games in this genre never touch. 
 To "ollie", simply pull down on the right analog stick and 'flickit' (don't laugh, that's EA's 
 official term) upward. To perform a kickflip or heelflip, after pulling down on the right joystick, 
 simply flickit upwards slightly to the left or right, depending on your stance. More complicated 
 tricks, such as a nollie 360 hardflip, require more complicated motions.
  
  The great thing about this system is that all of the tricks are available right from the beginning 
 of the game. This means that the only thing holding back the player is his or her skill level. 
 Throw in grinds, manuals, grabs, and the ability to string all of these together seamlessly (if 
 you've got the chops) and you have one robust trick system.
  
  Now, the trick system is great but if the game didn't challenge you it'd be a terrible waste. Nothing 
 to fear there, as some of the games challenges are certain to result in at least a few airborne 
 gamepads.
  
  The different gameplay modes are great, offering a lot of variety. First, there's Deathrace, an 
 event that's exactly like it sounds. Then there are the Best Trick competitions. Players here are 
 tasked with landing the highest scoring trick at a specific location within the allotted time period. 
 Jam lets players loose in a larger area, such as a pool, or even the X Games street course. The 
 player with the highest total score at the end of the event wins.
  
  Spot Race is an online exclusive challenge that requires players with performing specific tasks 
 at certain points on a path to the finish line. There are also "spots" to "own". These are specific 
 areas that may either be difficult to get to or just plain perfect for performing tricks on. The 
 spots you've found are archived in your "Spot Bible", which also keeps track of the high score 
 for each of the spots you've discovered. And lastly is S. K. A. T. E., which is just like H. O. R. S. E. 
 except with a skateboard. 
  
  All of these event types can be enjoyed online. The only downside is the lag which can be quite 
 bothersome considering a big part of landing and stringing together tricks is timing. Maybe they'll 
 work that out in the sequel.
  
  One of the most amazing features has to be the video editor. The game is constantly recording what 
 you're doing and archives up to the last 40 seconds of gameplay. That means that if you've just 
 done something completely out of hand, you can go to the pause menu, select the replay editor, 
 and piece together your own skate video. Now, it would be cool enough if all the fun stopped right 
 there. However, EA has set up a website titled "skate Reel" where you can post up to three of your 
 best videos. You can also upload up to six photos. You don't even have to bother using a PC, you 
 can check both your videos and everyone else's right from your 360 or PS3.
  
  We could easily go on about the intricacies of the gameplay but we'd be overlooking this game's 
 stunning graphics and physics engine. EA's Black Box was so careful about fine tuning the physics 
 that you'd barely notice they're there. And that's a compliment. Both the skateboard and its rider 
 behave exactly as you think they would, which comes into play when trying to keep momentum in a 
 pool or setting up for flipping into or out of a grind. This game also has amazing sound design 
 as anyone who has played it can attest to. Add to that the near photorealistic graphics and added 
 effects like motion blur and the experience becomes very immersive.
  
  There are a few gripes I have with the game. First handplants are absent along with the ability 
 to choose a female skater. I'd also have loved the ability to place a photographer in a specific 
 area for more dramatic shots during the replays and photos. These things aren't deal-breakers though, 
 not by a longshot. I hope to see these additions in the sequel.
  
  If you haven't played skate yet because of disenfranchisement due to the latest installments in 
 the Tony Hawk series, fear not. This is nothing like it. Personally, I would recommend this game 
 to everyone who loves either skating, videogames, or both. Pick it up. You won't be disappointed.

UserName: DAENF0RCER13
Rating: 8.5
Date: Jan 22, 2008 7:16 pm PT
Review:  Skate has now got me rid of button mashing tricks and combos from the Tony Hawk games. Skate's 
 different. You don't just play it, you feel it. No more buttons to do tricks (except grabs) . Instead, 
 you use the thumbsticks to control your movements. The trick system is revolutionary. You flick 
 the right thumbstick a certain way and it does a flip trick. It may take time to get used to it, 
 but once you get it, you'll be skating like the pros (not literally) . 
  
  The skating enviornment is just downright awesome. You're in a place called San Vanelona and boy 
 is this place HUGE!!! A lot of places to skate from the suburbs, the city, or a skate park. There's 
 just a lot to do. The transportation fits right into the game. You can take a subway, open up your 
 map and select a location, or just do it the old fashioned way, skate there. Whatever fits your 
 style. Many pro skaters to choose from. Some of them I've never heard of. Of course, you can create 
 your own skater. A good amount of customizations. From clothes, accessories, all that stuff. Although 
 it could have done a bit of tuning. 
  
  The replay editor fits in perfectly. You can change camera angles, change the shading, change the 
 beginning and the end, the speed of the replay, go forward or backward, and take photos. Replays 
 that you've saved and photos you've taken can be published online for others to view and rate. 
 
  
  Now the only problems in this game is the load times and the online play. The load times are just 
 horribly long. It can take up to 30 to 45 seconds just to start a career or go back to where you 
 left off. You know what, it takes about that long just to start almost anything. It's just ridiculous. 
 Now for the online play. It's alright sometimes, but it can get laggy, even if you have a good 
 connection. Although waiting for the game to start is kinda bad. Players are sent to a small place 
 to skate in before the game starts so there's not that much freedom. Plus for some reason, I don't 
 know why, I got one of the online achievements where I'm an Icon trickster or something like that 
 and I only played 2 games. I guess i got it cuz i played one of the best tricksters in the game, 
 I dont know.
  
  Buy or Rent?
  If your a skateboarder, or love skating, or just looking for a good individual sports game, this 
 game is for you. So it would be a definite buy. Lots of replay and a good amount of achievements 
 to get. I would only rent it if I needed something to pass my time to wait for a new game or something 
 of the sort.
  
  Graphics- 8/10
  The graphics are alright, but nothing special. The skating will take you deeper into the game.
 
  
  Controls- 7/10
  Although the controls are revolutionary to a skating game, it can take quite a while to get used 
 to. Especially if you've transitioned from the Tony Hawk series to Skate. What I recommend you 
 would do is if you have access to Xbox Live, download the demo. It'll take you straight to the 
 tutorial where you can learn the controls of Skate and it gives you a half hour to skate one of 
 the many places in San Vanelona.
  
  Gameplay- 10/10
  So many places to skate, so little time. San Vanelona will practically have you traveling around 
 every single area in San Vanelona. 
  
  Story- 6/10
  Though I didn't explain the story earlier, lemme sum it up for you. You get in an accident, you 
 recover, and from then on you try to make a name for yourself in the skateboarding world. So basically 
 the story is like the same as in T. H. U. G. Sorta.
  
  Replay- 7/10
  Though the city is big, the replay is not. Once you've done every single challenge in the game's 
 story, there's not that much to do except skate, which can sometimes get repetitive. Online play 
 wouldn't really be an option for replay as it is kinda broken sometimes, but hey, it never hurts 
 to try.

Review:  Has we know the Tony Hawk series have come way before the new game Skate. But now its time for 
 change. Skate is a revolutionary game, that puts you in the hands of yourself. You start out by 
 creating your character, and doing some training to learn and understand the controls. After you 
 finish your training you are free to go and explore the entire map. It is a huge map with an amazing 
 amount of spots to skate. You can also try missions, which are extremely fun but also very hard 
 at times. The online mode, is quite fun after getting used to. There is a free skate mode, death 
 race mode, spot battle, and a game of S. K. A. T. E. A game of S. K. A. T. E works exactly like it does 
 in the real world. Overall skate is a must have for skateboard fans, or for people who skate. Please 
 take into consideration that this game, will take many hours to learn and master, so do not get 
 irradiated, or annoyed with it.

::::::
UserName: mrfidget
Rating: 8
Date: Jan 14, 2008 7:26 pm PT
Review:  Skate is the first competitor that the Tony Hawk games have had in a long time. The Tony Hawk series 
 has probably had such a monopoly because other developers were afraid that their game wouldn't 
 stand up to a giant like Tony Hawk.
  But then EA made Skate.
  Skates controls, which are very different from Tony Hawks, consist of using the right stick to 
 simulate the movements a skater would actually make in real life. The physics are very realistic, 
 but it's weird how your character will fall limp off of his board after tapping a wall.
  Another huge part in the game is the bailing. You can just sit there spending hours bailing off 
 of a huge spot trying to break as many bones as possible. And, if you make a good bail, you can 
 watch the replay from different angles, or in slow motion. And if you think it's worth it, you 
 can submit it to the "Skate. Reel" where others are able to rate and watch your videos. The downside 
 is there aren't enough slots to put all the replays you want. Also, if you break at least one bone, 
 a chart will pop up showing a skeleton that represents which bones you sprained, bruised, or broke.
 
  The "Flickit" control scheme isn't all good, though. While playing "S. K. A. T. E." (which is H. O. R. S. E. 
 with skating tricks) , you will have to do exact tricks, but alot of the time your thumb will slip 
 the tiniest millimeter and your character won; t do the trick you want him to.
  The online play is okay, but it will get boring after awhile. While doing Jams online, the area 
 will usually be too crowded and you will often creash into other skaters.
  Overall, I think this game is worth a rent. Despite its downfalls it provides a fresh, new skating 
 expirience unlike the dial-a-trick style of Tony Hawk.

UserName: papa59roach

Date: Jan 11, 2008 2:09 pm PT
Review:  Skate. is an awesomeee game. At first, it will seem very awkward. especially if ur a tony hawk 
 veteran, like me :P. but after you get used to it, this game is wayy better than tony hawk. The 
 career mode or whatever it is called is pretty lame, thats why i gave this game 9.5 instead of 
 10. the challenges just arent very creative and theres really not much to it. some of the races 
 and competitions are pretty fun, though. The skating itself is what makes this game so great. You'll 
 spend hours simply, as the game's title would imply, skating. when you find a place for a kool 
 bail, you'll want to bail over and over and watch the replay. when you find a kool rail, youll 
 want to grind it over and over and watch the replay. when you find a place where you can get some 
 air, you'll want to nail out every trick and watch the replayy. the graphics are amazingg. and 
 the ragdoll (ish) physics make every bail fun to watch on the replayyy. overall, skate. is a great 
 game worth getting, whether you skate or not. :D

UserName: MasterJesterAra
Rating: 9
Date: Jan 10, 2008 9:21 am PT
Review:  This game has a different learning curve depending on who is playing it. All those people who said 
 that it was horrible and deserved a one out of ten. I dought they have ever skated before. The 
 game flows and i love the fact that you can't just manual everywhere and make a trick line that 
 is like 200 tricks long and get 19,879,858,752,544,648,947,345 points like you can in TH.
  
  When I first started playing it was weird but then again it is revolutionary so what do you 
 expect. I have always wanted a game to give reasonable points, not the stupid 75 digit scores but 
 i thought it was a little low in Skate. I was only getting no more then 500 points. Then i started 
 to catch on, the more complicated the trick and the better you pull it off the more points you 
 get. It doesn't take 50 tricks to get a 3X multiplier just a well placed kickflip 360 to a 5-0 
 and a 360 flip out. Sound hard.... because it should be.
  
  Anyone who talks about there not being good enough spots, you need to play the game more. When 
 you go out skating in the world you don't just automatically know where to go to skate and have 
 the most fun. Me and my friend went to a lot of places and having limited transportation that was 
 usually schools and other just weird stuff we could find to skate. Granted i haven't played the 
 most recent TH games but come on, how much of that stuff is put there just so that you can do really 
 insane tricks not because it would really be their in real life. Skate as far as i can tell is 
 put together in an all to real way and if forces you to think and use the environment. Also when 
 you do the Pro Challenges and the "own the spot" challenges you learn where new spots and and what 
 to look for, and not only that new moves. It takes a lot of tries because its not just a matter 
 of button combinations its actually getting your feet in the right place at the right time. Go 
 try that on a skateboard and then come back to the game and tell me the game is harder then doing 
 it in real life.... (Unless of course you already skate a lot and can do a lot of the stuff already) ... Also 
 with that go play TH and tell me how much of that you have EVER seen done in real life. I would 
 really like to know.
  
  All in all i love Skate and the way that it put together its trick system and point system. I also 
 like the fact that your not all super human and you can't just spend points to upgrade yourself. 
 You have to get better by playing and practicing. Some people say that it has a really bad collision 
 system. I think your not paying enough attention. In real life there isn't a big area were you 
 can miss the rail for the most part but still somehow end up on it, you are either on time or face 
 planting into the pavement. I think thats what makes skateboarding such an adrenaline rush. You 
 don't ever really know what is going to happen.

UserName: goldenrome
Rating: 9.5
Date: Jan 5, 2008 12:16 pm PT
Review:  OK, perhaps my intoduction is a bit of a lie, but it's deceptive about the rest of the game. It's 
 all very unique and competely different to anything I've ever seen before. 
  The problem is, we've only seen Tony Hawk's before, it's totally owned the genre for quite a while 
 and skate. is the first contender. 
  How does it measure up? Well, the first thing to mention is obvious- tthe control scheme. It's 
 quite honestly, flawed, yet fantastic. It's so much more natural than Tony Hawk's and flows nicely, 
 it's all very dynamic. The problems? Well, the problems come from the actaul game, instead of the 
 control mechanic. The problem is that many task will as you to do very specific tricks. On Tony 
 Hawk's it isn't any problem, press a certain combination, but on skate. it's hard to define things 
 like an ollie and a manual, and it can get very frustrating when the game expects you to do something 
 so specific. 
  The most irritating game mode confronts you directly with this problem. The game mode "skate." 
 is like horse. Usually you would think it would be a highest trick face-off, but on this you have 
 to copy the trick done before you- a near impossible task, especially at later stages in the game 
 when the computer plays flawlessly. 
  However the rest of the game is simply amazing. The main idea is get coverage from Thrasher and 
 Skateboard Mag and eventually own the X-Games. You'll go around skating contests and races (made 
 more fun by the fact that half the city is downhill) , and create videos at your choice of location.
 
  And that's the second best bit of skate. Many games have attempted success by making it free-roaming. 
 Almost ALL have failed. But in skate. it works so well. The amazing thing is that an amazing combination 
 of tricks can be conjured up from a simple street curb, anything is your tool. It may sound clich, 
 but you really can be cretive. And people have thier own favourite spots, and you can spend hours 
 just trying to find good skating spots
  You'll often find an oppurtinity and spend ten minutes trying to pull that single oppurtunity off 
 just right. 
  Skate. succeeds in so many ways, yet trips over itself is so many others, yet despite the career 
 and tasks not matching the control scheme, and the control scheme not being as 'pick-up-and-play' 
 and Tony Hawk's this is an amazing new venture into the genre, and let's just hope there's a sequel 
 with bigger brand names (maybe like vans and quicksilver) , reasonable tasks and the same sense 
 of curiosity that this original has created.

 and it being great. I'm sure EA will improve on these things in the next installment. Pick this 
 game up if you want to check out a skate simulation and the trick stick. It is defeinitely worth 
 it, but don't expect to be blown away unless you are a big fan of skating.

UserName: Tillekaratne
Rating: 7.5
Date: Dec 20, 2007 4:25 am PT
Review:  I didn't like this game at first. I used to be into skateboarding years and years ago, but soon 
 grew out of it. However, since then I've still enjoyed playing skating games; mostly Tony Hawk's. 
 My brother skates, so he bought this game after spending hours and hours on the demo of it, flicking 
 away at the controls. I had a go, but couldn't get used to it - it just seemed far too complicated.
 
  
  Though when I had some spare time I gave it a go, and after about two or three hours I became quite 
 impressed. The "flick-it" system does have some flaws, but overall, it's a really good idea, and 
 EA have executed it pretty well. After spending enough time on it, you can aim to do most of the 
 tricks that you want. Grab tricks are also well done, and so are the grinds. The grinds add a big 
 variation, as you usually end up doing a different grind from the one you want.
  
  The graphics on the player are fantastic. They look really good, and so does the board. The environment, 
 however, is pretty rubbish. Most buildings look terrible, and the less said about the traffic, 
 the better. Simply, I've seen cars better animated and better presented back on the original PlayStation. 
 They truly are dreadful.
  
  But if the graphics don't bother you and you are already into skating, I'd go for it, but I wouldn't 
 pay full-price for it.

UserName: tg1413
Rating: 8.5
Date: Dec 15, 2007 8:14 am PT
Review:  Well I must just say to begin with, despite it's flaws, Skate is just such an improvement on Tony 
 Hawk. There's just one thing lacking: the story .
  
  So the game starts off with a great beginning, well not exactly a beginning but a fun cutscene 
 thats actually real, and not part of the game. Anyway, you go through this to create your character, 
 there aren't many options there, apart from the hair, clothes, and accessories. Then you get into 
 the real game. If you've played the demo a lot like I did, then you can skip the tutorials and 
 get straight in. If you haven't... well then you'll have to do the tutorials anyway, or skip if 
 you're really confident. The first thing you notice is the fabulous graphics and the fluid animation. 
 Wow, they're awesome. Your skater looks so realistic and so does the world around them, the textures, 
 the lighting, everything. But the other thing is the new skate flickit system. This is just great. 
 Instead of button bashing, you have to flick your right analog stick to control the tricks you're 
 doing. This means that you have to actually think about your tricks, instead of just pressing a 
 button. The great thing about this, is that it's really satisfying pulling off a hard trick, and 
 any trick really. And you have to be precise about it, unlike on tony hawks where your character 
 would perform a trick, say a grind, with no problem at all, even if the distance and angle were 
 so unrealistic, and in real life, the trick would fail completely.
  
  But now to the bad bit. You get into your story of getting all of the pages in Skateboard and Thrasher 
 magazines, while this is challenging, it's just dull. You just have to complete different (when 
 i say different, the challenges are actually the same) challenges: photos, videos and jams and 
 best trick contests. But all of these are the same, and its just repetitive and annoying completing 
 them. And in the end, you just don't want to do them anymore. However, on the way there are the 
 good old fun pro lessons, which are a little bit different. You also have to complete different 
 challenges to gain sponsors, which is a good break from the usual challenges.
  
  Really, everything in this game is awesome, apart from the dull repetitive challenges, but if you're 
 willing to put them aside, you've got a great game.

Review:  Missions: Now as I was saying the missions do get quite repetitive especially the filming and photography 
 ones. The problem is you don't do them you don't unlock the interesting challenges (which are usually 
 gap this, get this amount of points etc.) which therefore means no progressing through the game 
 and what is the point in that. Apart from missions there is plenty of other stuff to do for instance 
 just explore the world freely looking for new spots or even mixing them up and making your own 
 spots!
  
  Create-A-Character: The create a character was a bit of a let down after things like fight night 
 by EA and I know this sounds cheesy but tiger wood's and more had greatly detailed create a characters. 
 This however has about ten if that hairstyles not much customizable in the face or body. Lots of 
 clothes and things like that but once you've got a sponsor on your board wheels shoes and trucks 
 if you aren't wearing that company's trainers for instance the sponsorship relationship goes red 
 and you don't get money off of them for using there equipment. (Duh!)
  
  Multiplayer: Multiplayer on this game online is great. You must choose between levels though it 
 won't just stream the whole thing but truely it is massive. Online you have a series of modes my 
 personal favourite is freestyle. Just go around the level trying things you haven't done before 
 or want to show friends in a private server or the world in a public server. There is also spot 
 challenge mode where you're given a spot, the person with most points after I think 3 rounds wins. 
 Offline multiplayer isn't so good as there is no freestyle just S. K. A. T. E. mode also know as horse.
 
  Or spot challenge so I just hope you ain't like me and don't mind challenging all the time!
  
  Controls: The new controls in this game are amazing the flick-it is revolutionary (hence why 
 a chose the game a revolutionary!) X / SQUARE or A / X is push RT / R2 or LT / L2 is grab with 
 different hands then you use the right stick which is also used for also etc. to tweak it into 
 some form of grab. They work well with the game and are easy to get used to the basics but if you 
 are a skilled gamer its easy to pick up the advanced controls too!
  
  Skate. Reel: Now this new skate. reel thing they have done is genius even though the editing tools 
 are probably some of this simplest around. You are give 30 seconds of clip to edit with screen 
 effects slow mo speed up and a simple trimming tool. The one thing missing from it that would have 
 been easy to put on soundtrack and a bit more time for recording. That is easy solutions they could 
 have changed. One other thing I wouldn't mind would be like a master editing suite where you could 
 take clips you've saved put them into one large video with a good soundtrack of your choosing, 
 possibly even off of your hard drive.
  
  Overall: Overall it is a great game and if this is what it's like in its first year I cannot wait 
 for years to come as Tony Hawk has had 9 years to perfect it but then Skate. comes in on its first 
 year and completely laughs in Tony Hawk's face.
  Tony Hawk you should be ashamed.
  While Skate. is like -LOL- PWNED YA FACE!!!

UserName: bojocon40
Rating: 8.5
Date: Dec 7, 2007 6:51 am PT
Review:  As we all know there has been a big named star called Tony Hawk that has laid waste to all skateboard 
 game clones. Luckily Tony can't touch this game. Why? Because it's a different view on skating. 
 Instead of combos and doing revert to manuals all the time you will now be looking for the perfect 
 line. That is what this game isa perfect line. But the line doesn't go out far enough.
  
  You start off as an unknown skater that gets hit by a bus and has to be taken to the hospital for 
 major surgery. That's when the game kicks in. You start off by creating a character. Creating a 
 character feels put together well. It feels like a less intense version of the Tiger Woods customization 
 options. You can either not go in deep or go all out. You can pull all the stops from how big your 
 skater is to size of the face. Then you go onto cloths and boards.
  
  This is where the fun starts. You get out of the hospital and taken on a tutorial. It's very simple 
 and it just teaches you the basics. You'll want to learn even more when the first tutorial ends. 
 The rest of the tutorials are spread out and are taught to you by pros in the game. During the 
 first tutorial it will also show you how to use the camera in the game. You can take pictures and 
 videos and upload them on the Internet and Xbox Live for everyone to see your mad skillsor your 
 horrible crashes.
  
  After the first tutorial you are let loose on the city which is nicely built. Pedestrians crowd 
 downtown. Cars drive by and honk horns when you get to close. You can also hear people talk on 
 their phones and to each other. The city really feels alive. I want to say it feels like a Need 
 For Speed sized city. By the end of this game you will still be finding new hidden places or some 
 bench that is in a back ally. 
  
  After the tutorial you can start taking on missions that range from you skating a line, competing 
 in competitions, competing in a game like horse called S. K. A. T. E., racing downhill and owning spots. 
 You do all these missions or events to get rep to get sponsors. You get up to 4 sponsors. You get 
 a shoe, deck, trucks and wheels sponsor. You can pick any sponsor from a pretty big list. But be 
 careful! You can only choose a sponsor once. After that it stays permanent. You can't go back and 
 change it.
  
  Basically your main goal is to get coverage so you can get sponsors so then you can go to the X 
 Games. That's right the famous X Games where you will compete in 2 events. You will compete in 
 Street and a huge "Mega Ramp". When they say mega they aren't kidding. That's pretty much the game. 
 There is no plot or twists. It's just you skating. Which is a good thing in my book. But it would 
 be nice to see some sort of plot as long as it's not like THUG or THAW.
  
  After you finish the game you are still left to skate. Which Skating in Skate pulls you in with 
 the "Flickit" controls. Yes it's one word. Basically it's what EA has been doing to almost all 
 the sports games. They integrated the right analog stick as your skateboard. Your left analog stick 
 is for steering you board. What makes this unique is that you actually have to learn the trick. 
 Some of these missions or events require precise landed tricks. You'll have learn all the tricks 
 and memorize them. I found this way more fun that just pressing a button. This also pans out in 
 game play. Say I want to grind a rail. I have to line up with the rail and Ollie at the right time 
 to land on the rail. You can land on the rail or you can shift you board around with the "flickit" 
 controls to do different grinds. . The controls in this game are demanding yet forgiving at the 
 same time. Like they say "Practice makes perfect." The controls also make it feel more like a sim 
 which is a good thing. 
  
  The camera angle scared me at first. It's down low at your skaters feet. It will feel weird at 
 first but you will adjust to like it. Just like the music. The music selection is a wide mix. From 
 classics to new songs. The weird thing is you never really hear the songs unless you put them on 
 soundtracks. The game automatically puts the music in ambiance mode. Which means the only way you 
 here the music is if you go to a popular skate area in town. The music also leads you to hidden 
 places.
  
  The sound effects are great! You hear your wheels go in between crack in the road. You can hear 
 your wheels screech to a stop when power sliding  you get the idea. Just every surface you can 
 think of your board going over you can hear it perfectly in this game.
  
  Multiplayer is a must now in almost all games. Multiplayer in Skate is great because you can just 
 skate with friends around the city or you can compete against one another. You can compete in S. K. A. T. E., 
 Own The Spot and much more. What's also cool is that you can go in and watch people skate if your 
 fingers are tired. It's kinda like Gotham TV from PGR but live.
  
  One HUGE downside to this game is the streaming billboard ads. There is nothing like seeing Small 
 Ville DVD and T-Mobile ads all over the place. You'll find yourself downloading a patch just to 
 put more ads on the billboards. Most of the ads are done right but when there is only two people 
 advertising at one time you see the same dang billboard every two seconds. 
  
  This is a good first installment of the game and I hope to see the game again. If you are tired 
 of Tony Hawk and need a new skate fix then look no further... Because Skate is here to stay.

UserName: Audio_Jihad
Rating: 8
Date: Nov 22, 2007 8:49 pm PT
Review:  I had no idea of the existence of skate until near the actual release of the game. I had gone to 
 talk to a family member about the newest addition to the Tony Hawk franchise (Proving Ground) that 
 was due to be released when he quickly snapped back that we wouldn't be playing Tony Hawk games 
 anymore, because Skate was due to be shipped and would give us the experience we'd always rant 
 on about getting.
  
  Skate revolves around the Flick-it system which can make those easy one button moves in Tony Hawk 
 much more difficult (and realistic) , but when properly landed going down a 6 set, can really be 
 satisfying.
  
  Plot-wise there isn't much there at all, just assorted tasks guided along by pro skaters and fictional 
 characters to get coverage in mags, film videos, or bomb hills in a race. There isn't an epic plot 
 with an explosive ending or anything like that, but it doesn't really need it as it doesn't seem 
 to be the point of the game. I would much rather look around for sick staircases and rails to hit 
 up (and as of this writing am still finding new spots) than deal with a storyline with flat characters 
 I won't care about.
  
  The whole city in the game looks quite good and has a good mix of color schemes, in the suburbs 
 you'll see a lot more color variety and more heavy green around than say old town, which has a 
 more toned down and, well, old look to it. The skating sounds are top notch and are quite close 
 to actually hopping on a board and doing a line.
  
  This being Electronic Arts' first venture into the skating world, the game does carry a few flaws. 
 The ability to get off your board seems to stick out. I can't count how many times I went down 
 a set of stairs and forgot to set the location marker to restart back at the top, causing me to 
 have to make a trek all the way to the nearest inclined plane to push up. Some people complained 
 about not being able to create a girl avatar, but it's humorously accurate seeing as not many girls 
 skate, and not many girls play video games. I do have a beef with the avatar system though as it 
 seems that no matter what kind of adjustments you make, your personal character will look just 
 like a friends character.
  
  I would definitely recommend this to anyone who feels the Tony Hawk series is too arcade, and to 
 any real skaters who are too lazy to go outside at the time.

Review:  I think its time for a new skateboarding game. The last other skateboarding game apart from the 
 TH series was simpsons skateboarding which i would rather not talk about.... 
  
  So Ea bring out this game called skate. (No prizes for guessing what genre it is....) 
  
  Skate 
 brings a new set of controls called Flickit. This is the main feature of the game that sets it 
 aside from TH. Basically you use both anologue sticks to do tricks, the left anologue controls 
 the person and the right anologue for the board. So the basic Ollie is just flicking back the controller 
 towards you and then drive it forwards. Then the Flicktrick is pulling bak and realesing it horizontally. 
 The only problem with this feature is that there are to many tricks that are so close to another 
 that you will end up pulling the wrong trick at least 30% at a time.
  
  There isn't much of a story line even though it is attempted. For example at the beginning of the 
 game there is a cutscene all the famous skateboarders (excluding tony hawk of cause) take you to 
 the hospital which sadly you cant skip to get straight to the game. The aim of the game i basically 
 to get all the sponsers and go to the xgames and be a champion.
  The map has got so many cool places to skate, just a shame the map is a bit too big to find all 
 of them. The good things about the story mode is that all the way through the game you never get 
 better, you dont get attribute points and all that jazz, meaning that it doesnt matter what player 
 you are it all comes down to skill. It a shame there is so much in game advertising, there isnt 
 a single street which doesn't say Adidas or D*C though the shoes look very good :D
  
  Onto the multiplayer.... and the first thing you notice is that you straight away get into the 
 game and play, the freeskate has got to be my favourite, just get upto 6 other players and play 
 any of the good spots in the game including the xgames mega ramp (awesome) and to danny way's mega 
 compound which is enormous..... There is also ranked matches so you can put your skills against 
 some of the best (and worst) players in the game....
  The other downside is the lag you can experience... sometimes you might get lucky and everything 
 runs smooth, or you could get be so laggy one second your on a ramp the next your eating dirt off 
 it.
  
  Extra's : Also on both singleplayer and multiplayer you can take pictures and photo's and upload 
 them to skate's website. then transfer them to youtube to get more pubicity. 
  
  To sum up this is a great start to the series and hopefully we will be seeing more soon. 
  
 
  Thx for reading, Elitedead

 skater in you (or the wannabe skater) . Great for fans of the Tony Hawk series or... just for skaters!

UserName: M0cha_Bear
Rating: 8.5
Date: Nov 8, 2007 1:13 pm PT
Review:  Skate is EAs first attempt at the skateboarding genre and it goes a diffrent route from Tony Hawk's 
 Pro Skater with a more skateboarding culture wrapped around the game. The gameplay is what everyone 
 talks about. It uses the right joystick to control the board and the left to control your body. 
 It makes for a really fluid and innovative take on skateboarding games, however to does take a 
 while to get used to. Doing certain tricks take time to get down due to having to be precise everytime 
 when preforming medium and advance tricks. Also the game is all about timing. It's key in landing 
 tricks, grinding and flip tricks... your timing is off by a few seconds you bail and hard. The 
 only true problem I had with the gameplay is you couldn't get off your board... at all... for any 
 reason. Which made it touch when you needed to off the street and on the sidewalk.
  
  The story itself is decent, you start off as a faceless and nameless guy who while taping a skate 
 video gets hit by a bus and goes through a long (and unskippable) process of getting to the hospital 
 to make your character, which is a bit limited on TRUE customization. The story then branches off 
 into basicly doing magazine photo shoot and videos. Which moves on to demos and competitions. Overall 
 the story is sorta shallow but it's better than most we've seen in the genre.
  
  The music is fantastic in th game, a perfect mix of well known artists, indie and exclusive tracks 
 done for the game. I personally loved rolling to Rick James' - Give it to Me Baby .
  
  All in all the game is fun to play but will take a while getting used to.

UserName: JFannn
Rating: 9
Date: Nov 5, 2007 5:26 pm PT
Review:  The first thing youll notice about skate is that the controls are completely unlike any skating 
 game youve ever played before. Whereas Tony Hawk games have always relied on button pressing sequences 
 and combos to perform tricks, skate essentially only requires the use of the analog sticks. The 
 right analog stick is mapped in a way that should feel familiar to anyone whos spent a good deal 
 of time on a skateboard. Pushing down on the right stick leans you back on the board while pushing 
 forward leans you forward, which in and of itself seems pretty simple. Tricks are performed by 
 combinations of forward and back movements, just like they are on a skateboard. For example, youll 
 pull down and then push up to about 9:00 on the right stick to do a kickflip (assuming youre in 
 normal stance) , or pull down and then slide the stick around to 3:00 to do a shuv-it. There are 
 of course fakie and nollie tricks as well with a grand total of 38 flip tricks you can perform. 
 Youll perform grabs as well with the triggers representing each hand and tweak them with the right 
 stick. Grinds and manuals will also become an essential part of your arsenal if you hope to make 
 it to the end of the game. Which are not controlled by just a button. You must ollie straight up 
 and hope that your board will line up with the curb. Once you get the hang of it, its easy, but 
 for beginners, you may get a little frustrated at first. And if you bail out, be ready to see a 
 color-coated skeleton with all the bones you've broken and bruised. Some gamers may be surprised 
 to hear that your character never increases or decreases in skill throughout the course of the 
 game. Instead youll just have to better master the unique controls to perform bigger and better 
 tricks. Once youve got the whole trickbook mastered youll be able to play with a great degree 
 of style, and thats when the video editor comes into play.
  
  
  At any time after pulling a cool trick (any time within 30 seconds...) , you can pause the game 
 and go into a replay editor in order to save your trick for posterity. The game touts Without 
 footage, its fiction, so youre able to upload up to three videos and five pictures to EAs skate 
 site in order to back up your message board claims to fame. It works well and does what it promises, 
 but there are some features that seem to be lacking a little. For example, minimal camera and speed 
 control can help to make some cool stuff, but not as much as full manual control could have.
  
  
  The camera in the game is another place where they're trying to be innovative. When your 
 riding, its not an over head view, its more like a skate video, almost like there's a dog trotting 
 along side you with a video camera on its head. The camera works great, for the most part. It adds 
 to the realism, but also, you may not be able to see things like curbs, which is important because 
 if you hit a curb your going down, or people! If you hit someone, you, and they, are going to get 
 a little banged up. But for the most part, the camera is really great, and does a lot for the realism 
 in the game. The realism presented in the game, while taking the genre in a whole new direction, 
 does hold it back in spots as well. There is a great degree of variety in the tricks, but theres 
 no customization and it seems like a number of staple tricks are missing. There will be plenty 
 of moments of frustration, as said earlier, when little obstacles like curbs or stairs get in your 
 way which makes us wish you could pick up the board and walk around. Additionally, the difficulty 
 in the learning curve likely means that this game isnt for everyone. As an aside, however, Ive 
 played this game with numerous friends who are certainly not hard-core gamers and literally everyone 
 has loved it and been able to do some level of tricks. As far as presentation, the graphics and 
 audio are both awesome. The sound of the wheels is like music to my ears and the city, the fictional 
 San Vanelona, is great. Its well designed so there are numerous types of areas that are pretty 
 much a street skaters dream. The character customization is rather limited and feels clunky, but 
 its passable and the amount of clothing and gear available is impressive  although youll buy 
 everything you want and still find yourself with TONS of cash left over. The online modes seem 
 a little light, but theres still fun to be had. The best of them is the freeskate mode, where 
 you can choose a zone and simply cruise around with your friends on Xbox Live. Youll see some 
 serious lag at times, but it seems to resolve itself fairly promptly by automatically changing 
 hosts. Overall, skate is more than worth checking out for any fan of skateboarding games. It wont 
 give you an experience like one youve had before, but its one you wont soon forget. You wont 
 be pulling off the crazy impossible stunts you may have in Tony Hawk, but its equally  if not 
 more  fun to pull off something really technically challenging in skate. With a little patience 
 and perseverance this game can provide a really great experience.

Review:  Skate is a very good game that blows Tony Hawk out of the water. The new control system of skate 
 is extremely good and flows very well and feels like your actually doing the trick and is much 
 better than pressing 6 buttons like in tony hawk to do a single kickflip. In skate career mode 
 you make and customize a character and then you just go out and basically free skate and do all 
 of these objectives that you are given. There are many types of objectives such as Video Shoot, 
 Photo Shoot (my favorite) , Pro Challenge, and Skate. You can also get sponsorships for things which 
 is sweet because you get more money from them if you put their stuff on your board. As you progress 
 along you get more places to skate like the X Games and Danny's megapark. The Multiplayer is pretty 
 good but is not very exciting. It seems to lag a lot which completely destroys the game because 
 Skate is all about lining yourself up and timing when you ollie. In Multiplayer you can play SKATE, 
 Best Trick, or race. Overall, skate is a very good game that anyone that any interest in skateboarding 
 should buy.

UserName: NBAmaster30
Rating: 8
Date: Nov 24, 2008 6:13 pm PT
Review:  Ever Since Tony Hawk Has Gotten into the video game industry we have be blessed with almost a new 
 Tony Hawk Skateboarding video game.. Tony Hawk however is not a realistic boarding game.. your 
 air is way high, your speed is off the charts and you can pull off crazy tricks easy.. We have 
 had a new tony hawk game for a while.. and we still got the same basic princibles in the game.. 
 You can't do most of what you do in the game cause its a video game.. Tony Hawk is starting to 
 dim and get old... Now there is a new kid in town.. EA has made Skate a realistic Skatebording 
 game, but does it dethrone the Skate god? or come up short..
  
  First off when you put down 60 bucks on skate you gotta know a few things first.. if your the kinda 
 guy who just wants to do insane tricks and have a more arcade feel.. then i doubt this is the game 
 for you.. Skate takes a realistic take on the skateboarding world.. so fans of skateboarding will 
 have to get this game.. almost every thing you do in the game is possible in real life.. So the 
 hardcore skaters will love this game and you will finally be able to get to play your true skateboarding 
 game.
  
  The story takes off when you are a humble skater who is fooling around town skatebording.. Till 
 you have to take on the dream to become a pro and have your name all over the place. This is nothing 
 too crazy or epic but it fits what the game is trying to say. To get higher in the skating community 
 you have to get Photo Shoots, Magazine covers, and video footage to get respect. One of the coolest 
 thing to earn respect is sponsers.. Just like i real life there comes a time in the game where 
 you have to sponser a company, all the big skateboarding names are here like baker, alien ware, 
 spitfire etc.. You can get a shoe deal with Nike, a Skateboarding deal with Baker, and get wheels 
 from Alien Ware.. You get added money if you skate for them plus everything you buy from the store 
 from that brand is free.. so pick wisely.. make sure you have a sponser with someone you like..
 
  
  In ths game you fully customize your character.. from skin tone to face, all that good stuff to 
 make your skater look cool.. They all are neat and you can have multiple skaters under your name 
 i believe so you can try out different things.. However unlike Tony Hawk you can't take a picture 
 of yourself and put it on your skater.. That would have been cool, but maybe we will have that 
 in later Skate Installments. Also your sponser play a big deal on what you wear.. Sign on a company 
 for a boarding contract and i think you should use that board, you get money bounuses for doing 
 so, plus you get all your sponser stuff for free.. soon you will have a sponser for your shoes, 
 wheels, etc.. In game advertising is a bit much if you hate things like that. I actually like it, 
 it gives you a realistic feel. Plus most of the brands are cool. Also what is very different from 
 this game to other skatebording games is how you do tricks.. most is used on the right annolog 
 stick. It gives it a more realistic feel and def. should be contined.. its more special then pressing 
 buttons to grab or flip tricks.. (if you ever seen the commercials you know what i mean) the grabs 
 are the shoulder buttons, and grinding is really neat too. depending on how your board lands depends 
 on the trick you do.. so its more realistic.. Although this is a cool way it might have been better 
 if they tweaked it a bit with adding some moves forgotten in the game. some have been in tony hawk 
 games.. like the pressure flip and inverts! however i think that EA will adress that and the next 
 skate will have both and more.. The control scheme is ambitous just like the game.. but it has 
 minior flaws that need tweaking. When you land a trick its alot more rewarding.. for some reason 
 when you do a crazy tony hawk trick you are left with no emotial feeling of what you did.. its 
 mostly button mashing.. but in Skate when you land a sick trick you have a great undescribable 
 feeling of accomplishment.. Its more realistic. i remember when i landed a trick in real skateboarding 
 you get a real sense of accomplishment.. although its not quite the level of excitement it still 
 feels good after you do a high or cool looking trick. Overall skate is a great new kid in town.. 
 and its alot better then the tony hawk game this year.. tony hawk is on the downside.. but skate 
 is the opposite and it can only get better.. that is the exciting part!
  
  Edit- After playing the game further i have been mistaken, the game is not as good as i have raved 
 it to be, basically it should have been good, I thought it was and assumed to much before i wrote 
 the review. Overall its still pretty fun and i had a great time playing the game. But i would only 
 recommend to the hardcore Skateboarders out there.. just drags too much, where it seems it would 
 be a great story that drives you to keep playing, i never got that drive.
  
  
  Breakdown
  Gameplay: the best realistic skateboard game ever.. however after the first few hours 
 it gets boring fast!
  Graphics: some of the textures (grass) look kinda cheap.. however overall the game looks decent
 
  Sound: Lots of different genres of music.. you will find one that you like.. plus the skatebording 
 noises are very realistic
  Value: If you can get past the boring missions, then you got a good value, for everyone else its 
 not
  Overall: A must buy for skating fans.. But for the average player its not that greatbr / 
  
 
  Final Score
  7.9

UserName: _SMYLEY_
Rating: 8.5
Date: Oct 27, 2007 2:17 pm PT
Review:  Being a skater and growing up with things like bigflips and bs/fs flips, it really was nice to 
 play a game that captured what it's like to skate. It really has that simulator feel to it, especially 
 with the style design and flik-it analog cotrols. They really have something in this entirely new 
 perspective, I only wish they took more of the simulation feel instead of the tony hawk backflip 
 mctwist to quarter mile long manual feel. They could have made the skater's style more believable 
 with more realistic landings (sketchy, clean, revert etc...) and the fact that the character lands 
 EVERYTHING he pops as long as it's timed right can verge a little on the yeah yeah so what side. 
 The greatest thing about this entire platform of skating is not only the camera-eye perspective, 
 but the feel of accomplishment: in tony hawk, the fact that you could do these super-unrealistic 
 maneuvers that made little sense left you with a need for the highest score while in skate, if 
 you just kickflip onto a ledge and shuv out you feel like you just did it inreal life. This entire 
 game leads you to the right goal for skateboarding; do something sick and then do it nollie. All-in-all, 
 the game is great and i can't wait for EA to improve everything in SKATE 2.

UserName: Striker1408
Rating: 9.5
Date: Oct 25, 2007 7:33 pm PT
Review:  Ever since the days of THPS, us gamers have had complaints.. and us skateboarders even more.. Way 
 back from why cant i manual to why cant there be just one world.. ... Simply put.. the skateboarding 
 genre, has been.. needless to say a weighted market.. with the exceptions of NES games.. and PS games 
 such as thrasher and grind session.. not only is EA Skate a breath of fresh air, and a new look 
 on a genre seemingly doomed to repetitiveness.. its an experience that really brings the gamer 
 into the game, and gives them the true feeling of skateboarding. The control scheme for this game 
 is what both skateboarders and gamers have been waiting for.. a more fluent feel, where you can 
 truly flow with the environment. Basically, the left stick controlling your body, and the right 
 your board/feet, and the triggers being your hands. This brilliant and simplistic design is joined 
 by the absence of a grind button... but why? because the developers at EA believe grinding should 
 be based on a button.. but on your aim at the object you desire to grind.. Along with a most genius 
 control scheme, is the most realistic physics ever created. [for a skateboarding game..] You wont 
 be seeing rooftop to rooftops over helicopters here.. and theres definitely no landing at breakneck 
 speeds, while your body is turned perpendicular to the direction your traveling. No, this has what 
 you expect out of a good physics engine. except.. one thing.. the bails in this game.. are somewhat.. embarrassing.. 
 i mean.. even if you fall from like.. a kickflip caught too late.. you fall on your face.. and your 
 body goes completely limp.. While we are talking about complaints. i must bring up the inability 
 to travel on foot. This, although not seeming to take much out of the gameplay, would have been 
 a more realistic addition, and at times, a better mode of transportation, such as when trying to 
 line up right.. The career mode has you starting as somewhat of an unknown skater from the dream 
 skate city of San Vanelona working his way to get sponsorships.. sound familiar?
  i know.. a little.. in the box thinking eh?
  i agree.. but truthfully, there isn't much more to 
 a skate career than that..
  what do you want, a love story involved? [ i can hear it now..-_-]
  anyway.. you do this by completing 
 video parts, and getting magazine covers in thrasher and the skateboard mag..
  one complaint.. there IS money in this game.. which i like.. but its COMPLETELY USELESS .. you only 
 need the initial $300 or however much.. and you really dont even need that..
  
  The Multiplayer mode is put together well, offering various categories such as ranked and unranked, 
 race and trick, and then the sub-game options..
  the on Live, the Sidekick theme is continued, and from the Live homepage, you can see top ranked 
 skaters, and top footy..
  the only complaint i have is the gameplay can get a little choppy..
  
  
  Altogether, EA Skate 
 is a MUST OWN for die hard THPS fans.. and, [sorry Tony] , but this game is by far the best skateboarding 
 game there is.. and i believe activision and neversoft are going to suffer major losses..
  this game provides anyone of any age and any style, to pick up a controller, and truly have the 
 feel of skateboarding, whether that be relaxing in a bowl, coasting down the massive hills, or 
 just playing a game of S. K. A. T. E. with their friends.....
  
  ENJOI!

UserName: BelaidKL
Rating: 8
Date: Oct 24, 2007 12:24 pm PT
Review:  Tony Hawks was a game which slowly, in my opinion, drifted away from the skate boarding genre. 
 Skate didnt seem like the type of game which would replace the Tony Hawks franchise but it quickly 
 proved me wrong. The trick system is fun and when you produce the tricks and land them its feels 
 like you've actually done it. The tricks are hard to do on purpose most of the time as I mostly 
 find my self flicking the left analog stick in many directions only timing when i do it. Graphics 
 are also good and the challenges are fun yet sometimes stressful.
  Now I move to the game its self. Characters are good and dont get in your way that often even Shingo 
 is hardly never around. Pedestrians are annoying though, you have a giant line then you kick flip 
 of a curb and a pedestrian makes you fall over. The cars can get annoying but in my opinion are 
 fun to ollie over or even manual down a hill into. But then theres the broken bones and all, something 
 which has no effect on the game. You brake your arm and yet you can do a christ air right after 
 it. Also its unrealistic, you smash your face of a curb and all you get is face plant, hardly, 
 but if you fall of a giant staircase you only get a broken wrist, hardly. But over all theres no 
 complaints its a fun, big realistic game, skate boarding wise and graphically. Just make things 
 mean something and dont let the trick system be too precise other wise i hope they make more of 
 the Skate games.

UserName: onlywhispers
Rating: 9.5
Date: Oct 19, 2007 2:24 am PT
Review:  Skate has rolled into stores. Thank God it has come. SHORT SUMMED UP REVIEW.
  
  Gameplay: This is most likely the most realistic skateboarding game to ever exist, most likely 
 the most realistic game ever. The flick it controls work wonderfully and are a great new way of 
 skating. There is a huge learning curve for this game, so huge, some people won't learn everything. 
 Just like real skating, it takes practice, and effort. Its hard, but afterwards, you get a sense 
 of accomplishment. The goals you are told to do range from the easy, to the plain out hard. Everything 
 in this game is about learning. You end up having your own style of skating. Everything works well 
 in this game with the exception that some tricks are to close to other tricks, which makes it difficult 
 to pull off some thing. 9/10
  
  Graphics: The graphics are amazingly good. The textures are smooth, and the skater details are 
 very well done. The city is full of objects and every object is detailed and greatly placed in 
 the enviroment. The city itself is beautiful. The animation on each skater is scary. Its dead on 
 to what you would see in a skate video, or some random skater down the street. Its amazingly good. 
 The camera is an issue, due to the Being followed by a filmer look. It just sometimes doesnt work. 
 9/10
  
  Sound: The city is full of life. So are the sounds. Cars wooshing by, skate boards flying off to 
 the side. Music fading in and out of each speaker. I was suprised of what this game was capable 
 of with sound. Its a great game to test out your surround sound. Sadly, the music is a little weak. 
 Theres a few good songs, but nothing you would love to skate too. Thank god for custom music. 8.5/10
 
  
  Overall: I am a fan of the tony hawk serious and Tony Hawk 1, 2, and 3 are amazing games. They 
 will be classics forever, but now its time for a new taste of skate. Since Tony Hawk Underground 
 Year after year Tony Hawk has grown into an immature style of skating (Jackass esque) , and rehashed 
 from year to year, and it is time to put down the board. Skate is the perfect game to replace Tony 
 Hawk, and give us a new style of Skateboarding. I can see skate becoming greater by Skate2. Hopefully 
 they will have flatland tricks, and handplants (RB would be a great use for a modifer button to 
 pull off those tricks.) . Revolutionary indeed.
  
  9.5

UserName: uklegendkiller
Rating: 8.5
Date: Oct 17, 2007 5:13 pm PT
Review:  After eight years of chart-topping Tony Hawk games - and dozens of pretenders to the throne that 
 aped the series' lightning-paced arcade action - only a complete reinvention of digital skateboarding 
 would be enough to topple Activision's groundbreaking series. And in EA's ambitious Skate, the 
 chairman of the board has finally met his match.
  
  While on first impressions Skate looks like a traditional Hawk game, what makes it a revelation 
 is its deep and intuitive controls; while skateboarding games normally see players hammering buttons 
 and direction
  pads to unleash tricks, all Skate's moves are unleashed using the controller sticks and triggers, 
 with player movement mapped to the left stick while the right controls how you flip your board. 
 As the game unfolds, holding down the right stick or nudging it in different directions allows 
 you to master dozens of tricks without memorising tedious, Mortal Kombat-style button combos, while 
 a gentle tap on the triggers also allows you to grab your board while in the air, making it a cinch 
 to perform hair-raising stunts and allowing players to think like a real sk8ter boi.
  
  Ham-fisted and impatient players will doubtless find the steep learning curve a chore - especially 
 as many of the tricks use similar nudges and flicks, making it easy to perform the wrong trick 
 at the wrong time -
  while the game's oddly mundane challenges and tedious loading times only
  serve to undermine 
 its dexterous achievements. But as the first entry in a series that's sure to run for years, Skate 
 takes giant steps in redefining console skateboarding and is a new benchmark for other genre titles 
 to aim for.

UserName: kente10
Rating: 10
Date: Oct 23, 2007 4:11 pm PT
Review:  SUMMARY :Skate is the new game from EA. It's more so a simulation than a videogame. (im not saying 
 its not fun, its just insanely real) Everything in this game is perfect. the graphics are perfect. 
 the animation is perfect. even the tiny details like the cracks in the road are perfect. Basically 
 take a Tony Hawk game, take out all the fake crap, add insane graphics, the ability to make movies 
 and snapshots, add a new control system and you get Skate.
  
  STORYLINE: The storyline is pretty much the same as any skating or sports game. Make some guy who's 
 a nobody, do missions, become a pro. as repetitive and unoriginal it may sound, its done perfectly. 
 the Koolest thing is how you can make videos and snapshots and edit them to make it look like a 
 real skate vid or pic. when you do this, a sponsor might like it and u can be added to their skate 
 team. GAMEPLAY: The gameplay in this game is phonomenal. Everytime you land a move, it feels like 
 your accomplishing it in real life. it just looks so real and the animation is so perfect. Another 
 good thing is the grinding system. the grinding is so perfect that it shouldnt be changed at all 
 in any way. instead of hitting a button and latching onto the nearest rail in sight, you have to 
 be lined up with that rail and you just have to land on it and you'll grind. it's pretty sweet. 
 The new flickit system is really awesome. But before you get use to it you'll have major trouble 
 cuz it can sometimes be a chore landing the trick u want. the most trouble is pulling off kickflips/heelflips 
 and varial tricks. other than that its easy to use. and its actually really not that bad. you'll 
 get used to it. The ONLY thing that i dont like about this game is the inability to get off your 
 board. i just wish you could walk around for a while instead of having to find ways to get up stairs. 
 Another thing about this game is the reality. for example, its extremely hard to quad flip but 
 it can be done cuz ive done it. Another thing is doing spins. i think a 540 is the biggest spin 
 i've ever gotten. Also, this game thinks a lot about a real person, meaning your character will 
 act as real as possible. you can't jump off a 50 foot building and stay on your board, no matter 
 how you land you'll fall... (unless your falling onto a ramp) . Last but not least is the traveling 
 system. their is no loading when your skatin aroun san vanelona so you dont gotta worry.
  
  Difficulty: I haven't beaten this game yet so i dont know how hard it can get... but im almost 
 done with it so bare wit me here. (i got this game a day ago. and its my first Xbox 360 game) Well 
 i know for a fact that it starts out really easy to pretty hard. you'll start out doing things 
 that only require 500 points and then you'll go onto things that require 3,000 points. (the tricks 
 dont get as much points as tony hawk games do) its really different on difficulty depending on 
 your skill.
  
  Overall: overall, this game is revolutionary and amazing! a 7.5 as a gamespot critic rating is 
 way to brutal. this game is so much better than any skating game i've ever played! (I have every 
 tony hawk game cept proving grounds) If you love skating, this is the first game you should get 
 for the 360 or PS3. Hope this help. now go buy the game.

UserName: wonderboy_46
Rating: 8
Date: Oct 11, 2007 3:58 pm PT
Review:  San Vanelona:
  
  EAs Skate. takes place in the fictional city of San Vanelona. Created from scratch just for the 
 game and with four distinct areas modelled on real-world cities, including; New York, Barcelona 
 and San Francisco. In terms of size, each of the four areas is roughly the same size as the entire 
 gameplay environment from Tony Hawks Project 8. This makes the scope for exploration simply 
 massive, although at first it feels very daunting just looking at the map screen. However, getting 
 around is easy enough thanks to a good map system and an extensive array of train stations, which 
 are basically quick spawn-points, around the city This is clearly a city with certain skate spots 
 rather than a place where everything has been designed to string runs together. In Skate. youll 
 find a huge network of streets and back-alleys which make it feel more city-like than any Tony 
 Hawk environment. In amongst the urban jungle youll find some obvious skate spots such as plazas 
 and squares, as well as some public skate parks. Youll also come across no-skate zones where 
 security guards will give chase if they see you skating in the area. The real golden trick opportunities 
 are found in these areas and the many less obvious places to skate in San Vanelona, such as the 
 slipway.
  
  Graphics:
  
  Having looked very lack-lustre in early builds, the finished version of Skate. is extremely well 
 presented. The environmental graphics are great, especially considering the scope of the city. 
 That said, some textures do seem better than others and its a bit of a mixed bag in that respect. 
 The character models for your skater and also the pedestrians and traffic are of a very high quality. 
 In replays you can see very fine detail, such as shirts rippling in the wind and damage to the 
 board itself. The only problem the game really has is that the framerate sometimes dips, especially 
 in the densely populated downtown area. Sound:
  
  The audio in Skate. does the job but isnt too spectacular. The skateboard sounds are nothing more 
 than functional but the music is very good. This isnt just because of the choice of songs but 
 also because music increases in volume near more interesting skate spots, which is a great help 
 when trying to find hidden areas.
  
  Single player career:
  
  If Skate. struggles in any area, then this is certainly it. It cannot be denied that the control 
 scheme is fantastic and is the very thing skaters have been crying out for in a skateboard game. 
 Using the analogue sticks to control your feet and the triggers to control your hands is ingenious. 
 However, the game around this central flickit control theme suffers from trying too much, too 
 soon.
  
  To begin with its great. Challenges (a structure borrowed from Tony Hawks) involve photo and video 
 shoots at skate spots and you see the resulting footage displayed, just as you did it, in magazines 
 like The Skateboard Magazine and Thrasher. However, as the game progresses these challenges 
 become too specific, asking for particular tricks on certain obstacles. At this point the control 
 scheme is just not refined enough for these tasks. Thats not to say theyre impossible, they can 
 be done, however, they become less to do with skill and more to do with luck as the game goes on.
 
  
  The other problem is that the game has racing in it. This just confused me completely. Why does 
 a game about professional skateboarding in 2007 need to revisit archaic and irrelevant themes from 
 the 70s? It makes no sense at all. Modern skating is about tricks and the deathraces feel totally 
 out of place and just get in the way of the rest of the game.
  
  Eventually you get sponsored by the companies of your choice and reach the X-Games, which thankfully 
 isnt too much of a let down. However there is still room for improvement here as well, particularly 
 in the format of the contests which dont really create the atmosphere of the real event.
  
  Skate. reel:
  
  This is the feature which allows the player to pause at anytime and edit 
 a 30 second clip of their gameplay as they see fit, before uploading the footage to Skate. reel, 
 which is basically a YouTube of clips from people playing the game. Screenshots can also be uploaded 
 and there are a variety of video effects and tools for both video and photos.
  
  Now this all sounds great and works really well in-game. However, as soon as you try to use the 
 Skate. reel website it all goes wrong. The site is just broken, refusing to log some users in while 
 allowing others access. Skate. TV, which is similar to Gotham TV in PGR3, is also very intermittent, 
 sometimes working fine and at other times being totally useless.
  
  Online play:
  
  The online features in Skate. revolve around Skate. Messenger, a tool which is completely pointless. 
 Its supposed to allow you to see who of your friends is online playing the game. Now, on PS3, which 
 doesnt have messaging within games and so on, this is a great idea. On the 360 however its completely 
 idiotic. Just use the Xbox Guide EA!
  
  When youre actually playing online and not messing about with the annoying Messenger it works 
 just about OK for the most part. Once youre in a game its great, but as with most EA games online, 
 the servers work on a very intermittent basis and youll often get disconnected from games that 
 youre actually hosting yourself, which certainly isnt good. There are also horrible lag problems 
 sometimes. The other issue online is that you cant use every location on the huge map, which makes 
 showing your friends great areas youve found very difficult.
  
  Overall:
  
  For a first attempt at a new genre, Skate. is fantastic. The control scheme has truly revolutionised 
 the genre and the depth of character customisation and exploration is quite frankly, awesome. However, 
 most of the single player challenges fall into the same traps as the Tony Hawk series. Some missions 
 are too much of a case of trial and error as the control scheme requires such extreme levels of 
 precision from the player. Overall though, this is a must-have for any skater and a great starting 
 point for what will surely become yet another EA franchise.
