UserName: arcelice
Rating: 8.5
Date: Oct 7, 2007 6:21 pm PT
Review:  Skate is a great game. By far, the most enjoyable skating experience I've ever seen in a skateboarding 
 video game. The controls are very innovative and make the game feel much more intuitive and rewarding. 
 When you pull off a great trick, even if it's by accident, you get a sense of accomplishment. The 
 fact that pulling off grinds is much harder is a good improvement over the Tony Hawk series. When 
 you kickflip out of that long grind, you just feel it.
  
  The only things that could be improved in this game are as follows.
  
  For one thing, the fact 
 that you have to constantly restart events when you mess up is ANNOYING. I don't know why EA expected 
 us to not want to instantly go back to the start when we don't do a trick right. How else would 
 we do it? There should be a button that similarly to the SSX series takes you right back to the 
 start of a trick.
  
  Another thing I would change about the game is the fact that sometimes what you have to do next 
 is unclear. There should be some way of telling which events are absolutely mandatory and which 
 aren't.
  
  The last thing I don't really like about the game is that there isn't splitscreen free-skating. 
 When I have friends over that don't know the control scheme very well, the only option we have 
 is to take turns in a single-player mode.
  
  Overall, Skate is a very great game that is innovative, intuitive, and just plain fun. I would 
 recommend it to anyone that enjoys skating games.

UserName: unigoono
Rating: 9.5
Date: Oct 7, 2007 9:51 am PT
Review:  Skate takes that great skateboard game we all knew and loved and tosses it out of the window. Trying 
 to do away with the whole button mashing experience that was Tony Hawk they have tried to inter 
 grade a new system where you control the skater, and you feel like you really control the skater. 
 \
  
  They did this with a new system called flick it. Instead of pressing a whole mass of combo buttons, 
 you use the right stick to do every single trick. You use the left stick to control the skater 
 himself, like leaning forward, backwards, and so on. The trigger buttons are then use for grabs, 
 and depending on which way you are pushing your trick you will do different grab tricks.
  
  Now this all comes together nicely and makes for one great game. The control system might seem 
 confusing at first, but given a few minuets you will have it down in no time, but at the same time 
 like real skateboarding it takes time, practice and skill to master good tricks.
  
  Not to talk about a movie editing tool they have. It is a good system but it lacks in some parts. 
 You only have so many angels you can watch from. You can't use stationary camera's. And they could 
 have more lens effects. You would think a game made by a lot of skateboarders would have tossed 
 in a fish eye lens. But it is only their first game and have room to improve for the next one.
 
  
  All in all this game is good and way worth the money. It will give Tony Hawk games a run for their 
 money.
  
  The graphics are superb. I wouldn't classify them as the best but I am sure they will last for 
 a good 5 years or so
  
  The sound is nicely done. The music is nothing new to the skateboarding game, but with skate you 
 can take it a step more and play your own music.
  
  The game play is over all good. It has a nice story, but lacks different styles of missions. In 
 the end while they are great missions you will find yourself doing what seems to be the same ones 
 over, just in different spots. The Difficulty can be hard for some people... but it is still easy 
 enough that if you spend 30 minuets you will learn how to play.
  
  Over all I give the game a 9.5. It has it's down sides, but it is new and has done well for a first 
 game.

::::::
UserName: D3R1N
Rating: 8.5
Date: Oct 1, 2007 10:49 am PT
Review:  Do my eyes deceive me? A skateboarding title that isn't part of the Tony Hawk franchise? Why yes... 
 yes it is! Surprisingly enough, EA has decided to tackle the market that has been dominated by 
 Activision and Tony Hawk for years and years. But the real question is, do they succeed at doing 
 so? Let's find out by taking an in-depth look at the game, appropriately titled Skate for the Xbox 
 360.
  
  The game opens with you, the main character, getting hit by a bus after completing a rather impressive 
 line on your skateboard. As a result, you're quickly transported to the emergency room, during 
 which time the pro skaters featured throughout the game are introduced in a neat little opening 
 sequence. Afterwards, a suggestion is made to have you undergo some heavy reconstructive surgery. 
 This is where Skate begins, prompting you to create your skater via an extraordinarily large amount 
 of customizable features. Unlike recent installments of the Tony Hawk series, Skate's create-a-skater 
 is without a doubt superior and really gives you a sense of being in the game once you're through.
 
  
  As for the gameplay mechanics, which are also the heart and soul of this title, a revolutionary 
 flickit trick system is used. What flickit means is basically that you must essentially move the 
 right analog stick around and flick it in a certain direction to perform certain tricks. This particular 
 trick system really manages to give you a fantastic sense of realism, although it does tend to 
 get a little demanding at times when you have to complete objectives that require an exceptional 
 amount of skill. Needless to say, the learning curve is a little steep, but I guess that just comes 
 with the territory. Keep in mind that the flickit system is only used for flip tricks; grabs are 
 executed via any combination of the left and right triggers, allowing you to tweak them by moving 
 the right analog stick in a particular direction.
  
  Skate's Career Mode isn't THAT much different from, oh let's say, Tony Hawk's Project 8. Luckily, 
 this is only true when dealing with the various objectives you must complete and locating those 
 who provide you with them. The objectives themselves are very unique, and will require you to do 
 anything from a typical Pro Challenge, during which a pro skater will require you to tear up a 
 particular spot in certain way, to various photo shoots located throughout the city of San Vanelona 
 where Skate is set. Successfully completing said objectives will net you reputation as a skater-on-the-rise 
 and will result in the acquisition of various sponsors. The problem with this, however, lies within 
 how quickly the objectives are thrown at you and the fast rate at which you begin you obtain these 
 sponsors. It's not necessarily a bad thing, but having such a large amount of things to do on your 
 plate at any given time can be a bit overwhelming.
  
  After obtaining the aforementioned sponsorships (board, wheels, shoes, trucks, in that order) , 
 you can visit any one of three skate shops to take advantage of the free gear they provide you 
 with. Your choices aren't limited to just your sponsors though, as you can purchase other stuff 
 with the money you earn, but the amount of money you can earn increases when you complete objectives 
 with your sponsors' stuff. Such a system also manages to give you the feel of being a future pro 
 skateboarder, which is another definite plus. On an additional note, if you're having trouble picking 
 out a board sponsor, sponsorship videos are available for viewing in any skate shop found throughout 
 San Van to help you choose. Photos from each one of your photo shoots can be viewed in these shops 
 as well, depending on what magazine you're currently shooting for. Pretty neat, huh?
  
  Aside from making your way through the ranks, flickin' it and all that jazz, Skate also incorporates 
 an innovative replay system that allows you essentially edit anything and everything to convert 
 it into the footy of your dreams. Said footage is filmed primarily by your loud-mouthed buddy, 
 who is responsible for the sometimes intolerable camera angle you're stuck with throughout the 
 entire game. Granted, this further adds to the game being as realistic as possible, but that doesn't 
 stop the camera from getting in the way of what you're trying to do every once in a while. The 
 sometimes funny and always entertaining stuff the cameraman says however more than makes up for 
 this flaw, and the ability to upload all footage taken to EA's skate. Reel to share with others 
 isn't too shabby either.
  
  Skate is quite exquisite in a graphical sense, but the immense amount of detail present seems to 
 drag the game down a bit, providing us with an excess of annoying load screens that really get 
 in the way of your skating. This especially goes for resetting your skater back to preset session 
 markers that allow you to essentially warp back to the spot you've chosen. Load times aside, the 
 character modeling IS nearly flawless and each part of San Vanelona is rendered beautifully, sometimes 
 prompting you to stop and take a look around every once in a while to admire such a thing.
  
  This particular title also provides us with a soundtrack unlike that of any other game currently 
 on the market, sampling a wide variety of music from all genres. If the music, or some of it, is 
 not to your liking, you can either turn it all off or customize your own personal playlist. You 
 can even set it so that music gets played at spots where it's generally very good to skate. Pretty 
 neat, huh? The voice acting is pretty solid too, featuring the voices of each one of the pro skaters 
 you'll encounter throughout Skate's relatively lengthy single player game. All of this in conjunction 
 with some really great skateboarding noises really make this title succeed in the sound department.
 
  
  Overall, EA's Skate sure gives the Tony Hawk series a run for its money, but the overly steep learning 
 curve of the flickit trick system and the difficulty it tends to cause at times take away from 
 the otherwise great experience it provides us with. On a positive note, the game really is innovative 
 and gives you an excellent sense of what it feels like to be a professional skateboarder. All in 
 all, I feel Skate's relatively lengthy single player campaign and online capabilities make it worthy 
 of at least a rental for any fan of the sport, providing you're up for a challenge. 
::::::

Review:  Let me start out by saying this game is amazing. It has done an amazing job at capturing the true 
 feel of skateboarding through its revolutionary controls. Just like in real life if you want to 
 to a vairleheel you do a combination of the moitions for a fs shuv and a heelflip. I also love 
 how the grinds are also about aproach. The way the controls work and reasons for it might be a 
 little a little hard for some non-skaters to understand but any skateboarder will be able to apreacate 
 how close it came to capturing the true feel of riding your board through a controler. They take 
 some geting use to but once you get the hang of it, pulling of tricks becomes a truely rewarding 
 experience. The city it is set in is amazing and a skate paradice, unlike the poorly designed levels 
 in the later tony hawk game which contain pracicly nothing an actual skater would skate; stuff 
 like randomly placed ramps in the midle of a dirt field. Also unlike Tony Hawk the goals in this 
 game pertain to actual skateboarding and do not consist of stuff like, catching escaped zoo animals, 
 vandolizing public propery, doing idiot vivi la bam type stuff, and other pointless things. The 
 default seting for the music is actualy quite good; you start to hear music as you get close to 
 good spots and it fades away as you leave. The pro line up is amazing and contains some the world's 
 most amazing skater such as Pj Ladd and Chris Haslem. Playing online with friends is fun; the only 
 downside being the ocasional lag. The game has a few minors errors that only a skater's eye could 
 catch but the all the good qualites outweigh the few bad one 100x. This game isn't for everybody 
 but if you skateboard, like video games the require skill, are up for a challenge, tired of tony 
 hawk's unrealism, or just like to try new things then this game is a must-buy.

UserName: dracula_16
Rating: 8
Date: Dec 3, 2008 5:12 am PT
Review:  Basically if you wanted to play a Skateboarding game for the last 7 or 8 years then your only choice 
 has been to play something in the Tony Hawk franchise. Those games might as well not even exist 
 anymore because Skate will have you wondering why you thought those Tony Hawk games were good to 
 begin with. Instead of absurd combos like a 900 double backflip you will be doing more realistic 
 moves in Skate.
  
  That's not to say that Skate is so realistic that it's boring -- it's only realistic to a point. 
 You'll still be able to fall 30 feet on your ass and skate away as if nothing happened. When you 
 take a really hard fall this Skeleton chart will appear and it will show you what kind of damage 
 you've done to yourself such as bruising, spraining or braking your bones. 
  
  You can even save screenshots and/or videos of your coolest moments and share them online via EA's 
 official Skate website. It's not however just a simple replay because you can edit your footage 
 however you see fit. You can use fast motion, slow motion, change up the camera angles, inverting 
 the colors, and much more. You'll probably want to use the replay feature because you'll inevitably 
 come across an awesome moment that you'll want to see again. 
  
  These awesome moments are made possible due to Skate's solid gameplay. Part of what makes Skate 
 as good as it is would be the controls. As opposed to Tony Hawk games' button mashing gameplay, 
 Skate has you using both analog sticks. The left stick controls your body and the right stick controls 
 your board. To do a basic trick like an ollie you'll have to hold the right analog stick down to 
 crouch and then flick it upwards to ollie. To do fliptricks you'll be doing combinations of holding 
 the right stick down and flicking it in different directions. For example, flicking the stick down 
 and then to the side will result in a Pop Shuvit. You can do manuals by holding the right stick 
 slightly up or down which will continue your string of tricks over flat ground. 
  
  You can also do grab tricks by using the left and right triggers in conjunction with the right 
 stick to pull off different grabs. In order to do a grind you'll have to ride towards a rail/ledge 
 at the correct angle, time your ollie correctly, and land on whatever rail/ledge you were moving 
 towards. There is no grind button. Grinding is definitely the most satisfying part of the game, 
 in my opinion 
  
  
  A large part of what you'll be doing in Skate is getting coverage so that you can appear on Thrasher 
 and The Skateboarding magazine. Challenges include "owning the spot" which is beating a pre-determined 
 score in a very small space (such as getting 2,000 points jumping down a staircase) , Film goals 
 that require you to do all the specified tricks within a short amount of time, and more. 
  
  Skate maintains a consistently smooth frame-rate, the environments are varied and the trick 
 animations are superb. Other skateboarding games have puppet-like animations in comparison. 
  
  To compliment the graphics is Skate's quality sound. The sound of your board coming to a screeching 
 halt after coming down a steep hill is excellent, along with all the other sound effects you'd 
 expect from a Skateboarding game. The Soundtrack is merely average. There are definitely some great 
 tracks like "Psycho Therapy" by the Ramones, "Raining Blood" by Slayer, "Hate Crew Deathroll" by 
 Children of Bodom and "Hustlin" by Rick Ross. Beyond those songs there are just generic rap and 
 rock songs that are forgettable.
  
  So should you buy Skate? that depends on how much you'll play offline because the online play is 
 almost not even worth mentioning because it lags so bad that it's unplayable. If you're the kind 
 of person that'll rush through Skate once and never play it again then no -- Skate isn't for you. 
 If you're the kind of person who'll spend a lot of time just exploring and recording footage of 
 yourself then yes, I think you'll enjoy it enough to warrant a purchase. Thanks for reading.

UserName: produceofperu
Rating: 8
Date: Sep 28, 2007 9:04 pm PT
Review:  Before I begin my review, to the people who have yet to play Skate; No matter HOW good you think 
 you'll be when you first play this game, you're just not prepared. And to be merely an okay skater, 
 you'll need to put in at least 4 or 5 hours of gameplay. That means just skating around the city 
 practicing, not necessarily completing goals. On to the review!
  
  As I previously stated in the Review Deck, Skate is a decent game in general, but an EXCELLENT 
 skateboarding game for fans of Tony Hawk or the actual sport. The single player career mode is 
 extremely challenging and rewarding. You'll sometimes find yourself trying to complete one goal 
 for an hour or more. Not to mention the fact that you have to ollie up on to every sidewalk or 
 small curb. Believe it or not, this WILL seriously try your patience. However, once you accomplish 
 set goals and get more familiar with the mechanics in the game, you'll definitely be feeling very 
 proud of yourself. The multiplayer mode in Skate, also known as Party Play, unlike the single player 
 mode, is extremmmely limited and gets very boring, very quickly. Your friends will most likely 
 just want to skate around the game and learn the basics (if they haven't already) , or just sesh 
 around SanVan for hours on end. Too bad! In Skate, not only is there NO sort of Free Skate mode, 
 but you are only able to play a game of S. K. A. T. E. or Own-The-Spot where you have a couple seconds 
 to nail a trick and your friend either has to copy it or land a better one. Basically just not 
 enough. Online play on the other hand, does feature a pretty fun Free Skate mode. Which is definitely 
 a good thing. Although there can be some slow downs. The graphics of the game are pretty damn good. 
 But they're not revolutionary. Not outside the genre anyway. The same goes for the control scheme. 
 It's a really good idea, but it's also (sad to say) really broken. Performing certain tricks requires 
 fingerstyle gymnastics (for grabs and such) and/or one amazingly accurate thumb (for advanced flip 
 tricks.)
  Overall, I DO believe that this game is more fun, challenging, rewarding, and way more realistic 
 than ANY game in the Tony Hawk series. But I still don't believe that it's a Tony Hawk Killer. 
 Only Skate's sequel (s) could prove me wrong. Now THERE'S something to get excited about!
  
  Happy Skating!

UserName: shadowblade99

Date: Sep 25, 2007 2:58 pm PT
Review:  So EA just thinks that it can walk right in and knock THPS over eh? Well it was a good attempt, 
 but Skate just doesn't have what it takes to dethrone the king. Skate has wonderful graphics, they 
 are very good looking. Great amounts of details, physics and animations are spot on, dramatic lighting 
 and darkening, colorful, and so on and so forth. But good graphics don't make a great game. The 
 musical score, sounds, and talking is top notch, something that EA is very good at, again this 
 doesn't make a game. It helps, but in this day in age when everything isn't about graphics and 
 controls anymore Skate falls short. There really aren't that many modes, something the THPS has 
 done very well is changing and adapting to the current trends of gamers. While this doesn't always 
 prove to be a good thing, Skate doesn't do much for the gamer looking for something new. It's got 
 the standard set of single player modes. The multi player, is well the same as past THPS games. 
 Where the game falls really short is the controls. using the second joy stick is a good idea. It's 
 never been done before, but there is a reason for that. The joystick is unreliable. You have to 
 do certain movements on the stick in order for your boarder to do a trick. This doesn't always 
 work that well, or at all for that matter. Another thing that holds back this game is the difficulty 
 of it all. I know it's supposed to be a realistic skater game, but it's really difficult, even 
 on easy to land many of the trick. After a while you just get frustrated or bored and you put or 
 throw your controller across the room. Plus because it's more realistic, it's not nearly as dramatic. 
 Therefore casual gamers will get rid of this game right fast. It's nice to have a new skating game 
 on the market, something that THPS has held forever. But this is one that I would have prefered 
 not to have played.

UserName: greatskate182
Rating: 8.5
Date: Sep 25, 2007 6:06 am PT
Review:  The Good: The game is very, very good. The mechanics, physics, and animations match so perfectly 
 real skateboarding. The city is huge and there are so many nooks, crannies, and hidden spots it 
 would take a lifetime to find all the lines to skate. The sense of speed you get when bombing a 
 hill is phenomenal. The developers even went as far as adding speed wobbles which shows the level 
 of intricacy. The trick system is great and, once you get the hang of it, not as impossible as 
 people make it seem. It is so fun to just cruise and hit a huge rail. You get a sense of accomplishment 
 from doing normal tricks (i. e. a kickflip backside lipslide actually takes some thinking) . The 
 video editor is a nice addition and is really fun to play around with if you just had a sweet run 
 or stunt. The ragdoll physics are fun and if you, like me, skate, you'll appreciate all the finer 
 details of this game.
  
  The Bad: First of all, the idea of this camera guy following you is cool, but the camera angle 
 can be troublesome. Most the time it's not a huge deal, but when trying to land on a narrower pathway 
 or rail it can be hard to line it up. The load times are long and frequent, but with a city so 
 massive and living, can you blame them? Pedestrians and other skaters only get in the way a few 
 times, but when they do (like during contests) it is annoying. People complain that the game is 
 too hard. Yes, the game is a little hard in some spots, but definitely not impossible. The biggest 
 gripe I have is the fact that you cannot leave your board. When I see a nice handrail that I am 
 dying to hit, in real life, I would be able to get off my board and walk to the top of the stairs. 
 In SKATE, however, you are forced to skate around the building in search of the rail. It does help 
 that you can set a start location and return there with the push of a couple buttons, but it gets 
 really annoying not being able to get off your board and climb some stairs, jump up onto a ledge, 
 etc.
  
  Overall: SKATE is a great looking and feeling game. Fans of the Tony Hawk series will enjoy the 
 change in scenery and gameplay, especially if theyve spent a good deal of time on a real skateboard. 
 There are some minor gameplay issues that are frustrating, but not game-killers in any regards. 
 SKATE offers skateboarders and gamers a chance to live out all their true-world skating fantasies. 
 The city is huge and alive and the spots are endless. And trust me, Ive been skating for five 
 years and SKATE (in its animations, physics, and mechanics) is so close to the real thing it is 
 amazing. Fans of skateboarding and alternative sports games will get a lot out of SKATE.

::::::
UserName: Barloc1337
Rating: 8
Date: Sep 24, 2007 7:27 pm PT
Review:  Skate is the new skateboarding franchise released by EA. Although the Tony Hawk series has owned 
 the whole skateboarding franchise, a new competitor has just arrived on the block, and is here 
 to do some damage. Skate does many things that are very new to the skateboarding game, and the 
 game is a really good building platform for EA. But with some minor things, the game doesn't quite 
 reach full potential, but it is a worthy adversary to the Tony Hawk games.
  
  So of course the big thing about Skate is the new control scheme. Unlike the Tony Hawk games which 
 use certain buttons to preform certain types of tricks, the controls in Skate mainly rest on the 
 right analog stick. For example performing an ollie is as easy as pulling the stick down, and pushing 
 it up. To do certain flip tricks, it is all in how you start or finish where the right stick ends 
 up. Push up and slightly to the left or right and you can preform heel and kickflips. This is a 
 revolutionary way of playing the skateboarding games, and most of the time works well. Where you 
 will run into problems is when certain challenges may require you to preform certain tricks in 
 the game. Since all the flips in the game are done with the right analog stick, sometimes the game 
 may be confused on which trick your trying to pull off. Mainly the instances happen when specific 
 tricks are necessary, otherwise you won't really notice any problems.
  
  Also with the controls, Tony Hawk has a button to preform grinds, but unlike that, Skate makes 
 it more realistic and makes you line yourself up with the edge or pole or whatever your grinding 
 on, and simply jumping on to it. You can then change the position of your board with the right 
 analog stick, and with the left, you can control how you get off the pole or edge. This is a much 
 more realistic approach, and most of the time works. Although the timing may take a little while 
 for you to develop, you'll soon get the hang of it and start pulling off great lines.
  
  The grabs and manuals are pretty simple. To do grabs you can press either the right trigger, or 
 left, or both to preform certain tricks. You can also tweak with the right analog stick while grabbing 
 to preform new grabs. Overall it is a little difficult to get the hang of, but once you do it is 
 pretty easy. Manuals are simply pulled off by pulling on the right analog stick slightly forward 
 or backward. You can then use these to connect your lines and preform very cool tricks. Overall 
 the entire control scheme has a few flaws, but is one of the most revolutionary control schemes 
 that the genre has ever seen.
  
  The game itself, or the story, is pretty standard, and doesn't really feature anything special. 
 You create your character, give him some clothes, and a board, and you start out as someone trying 
 to prove himself as a skater. So you will try and film yourself doing cool tricks and/or lines 
 and try and become a pro skater. You'll try and get sponsored by the many companies that are available 
 to you in this game. After getting that and becoming pro, you can compete in such events as the 
 X-games which does mean the mega ramp is in the game. So overall it is what you would expect from 
 a standard skating game.
  
  Although this game is new and innovative, this game has some minor flaws. The game's camera is 
 based on the fact that you have some guy with a video camera who is filming you, which leads to 
 a weird perspective of being behind the skater and down below his waist. This is cool, but does 
 lead into some vision problems, which will frustrate you when your racing, or just trying to pull 
 off something very cool. The skater doesn't become transparent in spots he should sometimes which 
 can lead to some bad things.
  
  The challenges in the game are interesting since the difficulty will bounce around from time to 
 time. The game seems very unbalanced this way since you'll run into some hard challenges in the 
 game in the middle of the story, unlike the difficulty just progressively getting harder. The game 
 will frustrate you this way but you will be able to complete the challenges, although some may 
 take longer than others.
  
  So overall Skate is a cool new idea. It has pretty much been built to be nothing like Tony Hawk, 
 and if there is anything that they've done, it's that. Skate takes a much more realistic approach 
 to the genre of skateboarding, and is a neat idea. I think that it would be cool to see this game 
 get expanded into a franchise, and try and tweak some things to make the game better. Skate is 
 a neat idea, and I recommend that everyone who is a fan of the Tony Hawk series, or just any player 
 for that matter check out this game. 
::::::

UserName: pigonthewing
Rating: 8
Date: Sep 24, 2007 6:41 am PT
Review:  I wanted to wait till I got fairly good at the game before reviewing it since for a game like this 
 its not fair to review it until you get a handle on the controls.
  
  This is a very hard game for your average gamer, also compounded when you know nothing about skateboarding. 
 I knew the basics like ollies, grabs, flip tricks, but i had never heard of a shuvit or a nollie 
 for example, so i had to learn some of the skate boarding lingo to sometimes even understand what 
 some of my goals would be. Such as a BS and a FS which i think is back side and front side.
  
  Now the controls are quite good. Some tricks are very hard to to and you will continue to do 
 tricks you didn't intend but with practice you will start to perform what you intend more and more 
 often. But it takes practice, a lot of practice.
  
  The world is quite large but no overly so, but for a game like this its perfect. There are many 
 types of areas for your style of game. Whether you like to grind or do lots of air.
  
  Just being able to go out and play on your own is fun. Also when you open up the x-games and the 
 mega compound you can start doing some absolutely crazy tricks which can be fun for awhile but 
 personally i like just skating the smaller parks and pools.
  
  Now issues i have with the game. The camera angle is annoying. Its hard to see directly in front 
 of you and not being able to look before you turn you often will crash into a person that you had 
 no idea was there. Whats funny is if your chased by a security guard the camera pans back a bit 
 and this would have been a perfect camera angle for the game. Or at least an optional view. Its 
 not a deal breaker but it can be a bit tedious sometimes.
  
  Next the loading times can be quite large. thankfully once your in the world you don't load unless 
 quickly jumping to a new area on the map.
  
  Another is you will have to attempt some tricks a number of times to accomplish. This didn't bother 
 me since i realize even in real life these guys have to attempt these tricks a number of times 
 before they get it. But it may bother some.
  
  Its a great game and I love to just mess around with from time to time.

UserName: king_midas123
Rating: 7.5
Date: Sep 23, 2007 4:04 pm PT
Review:  This game will probably have you dieing to try out it's controls first. When you do, it's a blast 
 and you will probably spend 1-2 hours trying out new stuff. After that, once you try to get into 
 career mode and get used to the controls; you're going to want to turn off the game and do something 
 else. First, career mode is just really boring. You spend pretty much the entire game shooting 
 for magazines to get famous. The pro challenges are intended to be fun, but they end up being just 
 frustrating. It seems like they tried to make a horrible career mode. Other than that, I can safely 
 say that the freeskate is the strong point of this game and is probably what you will spend most 
 of you time on. Online is also a lot of fun. I'd say it's worth a rent if you want to try it, but 
 if you absolutely love freeskate, I definetly recommend this game for you. Overall, skate is a 
 very good attempt for a better skating game, but I think if they franchise it, they'll fall downhill 
 for the Tony Hawk series to dominate once more.

UserName: Scuza2100
Rating: 7
Date: Jan 11, 2008 3:19 pm PT
Review:  When I first played the 1/2 hour demo of Skate, I was blown away. The gameplay mechanics were so 
 revolutionary, I immediately thought that this would instantly eclipse everything the Tony Hawk 
 franchise worked so hard to accomplish. On the release date, I went to the local retailer to buy 
 the game. They told me it had been moved back to the 13th. I was fine with that, so I waited patiently 
 and played the demo a few more times. On the 13th, I returned, and they told me I had to wait one 
 more day. I was fine with this, but they were definitely pushing the envelope. When the game finally 
 came out, I bought it immediately. I slapped the disc into my 360, and began playing. At the start, 
 the game was lots of fun. The Flick-it controls were so fun to use I thought I would never stop 
 playing the game. Then my guy advanced to Amateur. The game became nearly impossible. The challenges 
 were ridiculously hard, asking to do tasks far to specific for an analog stick trick control. I 
 struggled through, and made it to Pro. I'm currently sitting here with about 3 or 4 Pro-ranking 
 Challenges done, impossible to continue due to the game being to difficult. It became a vicious 
 circle: You can't complete challenges because you can't get any better, and since you can't get 
 any better, you can't complete challenges. The physics system also had a few glitches that are 
 funny, but interrupt what you really want: The realistic feel. Althought, the rest of the game 
 was good. The graphics tossed Tony out the window, and the base idea left Hawk in the dust. The 
 board performance customization was fun, but the player customization lacked that certain unamable 
 element that the recent Tony Hawk games had. Even though Skate outranks any Tony Hawk game I've 
 played, the unbelievably specific challenges and the lack of player motivation holds this game 
 back from achieving what it truly deserves.

Review:  Skate is a great game that shows Tony how skateboarding games should be made. This game is completely 
 amazing, and worth every penny. It is one of the most fun games I have ever played. The graphics 
 are great, the gameplay is innovative and awsome, and the value is top notch. If you blaze through 
 career, it should take you at least 9-10 hours. Then it will take you a lifetime to find, and skate 
 everything in SanVan. The frame rate holds up suprizingly well for a game of this size. There are 
 some glitches that can be frusterating, but as a previous hawker I know it has a lot less glitches 
 than the TH series. The single player achievements are great and not impossible to get, unlike 
 some games. Multiplayer is the only downfall to this game, it's ok but not that good. There are 
 many name brands in this game which make it even better, you can ride for brands like: destructo, 
 circa, lakai, plan b, and spitfire. In this game it is very rewarding pulling off simple tricks 
 like a varial kickflip to nosegrind. Also if you skate in real life you will like this game even 
 more. Skate is simply one of the best games you will ever ever play.

UserName: Penguin93
Rating: 9
Date: Sep 21, 2007 9:51 pm PT
Review:  Skate is the one game to give the Tony Hawk series some competition. And wow, it did a great job.
 
  
  Skate uses one of the best story's you can use for a skateboarding game. Getting Coverage, and 
 getting Sponsored. Getting Coverage is pretty mandatory for getting sponsored by the bigger skate 
 company's, so you will be shooting photos for The Skateboard Mag, and Thrasher. Along the way, 
 you will do Filming Challenges, Owning Spots, et cetera, in order to get Noticed by the Big company's 
 such as Almost, Zero, DC Shoes, Girl, &eacute; S, Independent, Spitfire, and so on.
  
  The new Flick-it system is where a good portion of Realism takes place, Flicking the Right Analog 
 stick in ways you would sort of flick your feet on a real Skateboard. It might take awhile to get 
 used to the Flick-it system, but once you get the hang of it, you will really enjoi it. (see what 
 i did there? i'm so clever.)
  
  Gameplay: After playing Skate, i can never go back to a Tony Hawk game, ever. Skate really brings 
 an awesome mixture of Fun, and Realism, the Flick-it system is great. So many Brands of Decks, 
 Trucks, Wheels, and Shoes. You can choose the Loose-ness/Tight-ness of you're Trucks, along with 
 the Hardness/Softness of you're Wheels. You can choose you're own Style, Normal, Loose, Aggressive. 
 Mike Carroll, Pat Duffy, Paul Rodriguez, Chris Cole, PJ Ladd, and tons of other great Pros are 
 in the game.
  
  Graphics: Skates Visuals, Level Design, and overall Graphics are Stunning. Character Design is 
 Incredible, San Venalona is Amazing. Frame-rate glitches tend to happen but Rarely. 1080p makes 
 everything even more Visually great.
  
  Sound: A Great selection of Music, such as The White Stripes, Nirvana, Valient Thor, Mot&ouml; rhead 
 , and so on. Great Voice acting for all characters. You can hear the wheels Spinning after popping 
 a trick while going fast, which i think it pretty cool.
  
  Skate will last you a very, very long time. There is much to do after beating the main story, and 
 Online play is pretty good.
  
  Cons: Well, every game has some cons. Not being able to get off you're board can be a pain, just 
 getting around can be so much easier if you could get off you're board. Local Multi-Player is fun, 
 but there is no Free-Skate mode for Local Multi-player, which really disappointing.
  
  I Highly Recommend Skate, weather you skate in reality or not, you will love skate.

UserName: death_zone
Rating: 8.5
Date: Sep 21, 2007 6:52 am PT
Review:  This Review Is Meant For A Single Player Only, Experience The Gameplay With The A. I
  
  (REVIEWING IN A SKIT STYLE)
  
  Today Ive got a chance to meet with one of the EA BlackBox 
 representatives to talk about his latest released game, Skate. Im surprised to hear his thoughts 
 about his own game. Check it out!
  
  D-Z: Tony Hawks games has been a long running series that Im sure, by now, most of the gamers 
 are getting sick and tired of playing it. Now, Electronic Arts is here to tell us exactly how hard 
 it is to be a pro skater in a realistic way. So tell me, how do you guys revolutionized this skating 
 genre?
  
  EA: Firstly, Skate is all about Next Gen, from the wheels to the world, you will feel fresh for 
 this entirely new skating game. So let me start off with the CONTROLS.
  
  We did mention that there are not going to be any button mashes, well, I guess we have lied to 
 most of our viewers and listeners. In fact, most of the time during gameplay, youll find yourself 
 mashing one, two, or perhaps three buttons just to get your skater to skate and brake. Dont be 
 surprise though, as youll be pressing or holding the button frequently when you are traveling 
 around San Vanelona. Also, both the Left and Right Triggers are used to grab the board with your 
 left and right hand. Pressing the B button while grabbing will actually let u do a trick or two. 
 So that is button mashing afterall.
  
  But trust me dude, it really feels good to skate. Oh wait, whats a GOOD for without a BAD 
 right? Ahah! We have invented a flickit control system, that err. actually dont work as perfect 
 as what we have planned for. The directions for pushing and pulling the right stick on certain 
 tricks are quite similar; therefore, its kinda hard to pull off some specific tricks which are 
 needed to be done in some of the many objectives. But overall, it feels smooth and responsive most 
 of the time. It just requires timing, practice and most importantly, I call it The Ultimate Test 
 For Patience. Its definitely a hundreds of trials and errors to get an objective right.
  
  D-Z: Woah! Im glad to hear that your thoughts are actually the same as mine. Thanks for revealing 
 the good and the bad part of your newly invented control scheme. So lets move on. Youve revolutionized 
 the controls, what about the PRESENTATION?
  
  EA: We are the first developers to develop a skating game that involves free roaming. Our city 
 is named after San Andreas and that is San Vanelona. Obviously in comparison of sizes and map scales, 
 GTA is way much more bigger than ours. But it feels big when you are skating, because a skateboard 
 travels much more slower than a car. So It takes a longer time to reach from one end to another.
 
  
  We also want the city to look like a breathing world. And with that, we have created about 6-7 
 different looks of cars and people. And with those numbers, can u imagine how will our city look 
 like? Haha
  
  We have also created many downhills and down slopes for the skaters to pick up speed. But it seems 
 that, Ive spend most of my time going uphills and skating up slopes trying to find my next objectives 
 that is located on the minimap. Ive noticed that theres also no balance when it comes to WHERE 
 TO GO, either you might focus too much on the minimap searching for your objectives, or you might 
 be working too much trying to fancy your skate skills which will eventually lead you into a wrong 
 turn. Not all objectives have multiple paths and ways to reach it. Another downside of our skate 
 game is definitely our camera System. DudeIt totally sucks, we did not provide any change of views 
 or camera, so like it or not, you have to stick with the low camera that is focusing mainly on 
 your skate deck. And I find that this is one of the issues that causes you to miss your timing 
 or evade any obstacles that is in front of you. But this usually counts as a factor when you are 
 trying to complete your objectives.
  
  D-Z: Nice one man! Looks like your presentation is not as good. Talking about objectives, can you 
 tell me how do your skater PROGRESS?
  
  EA: Sure, but there is nothiug much here. Youll start off by creating your skater using our CREATE-A-SKATER 
 mode which can only be found in the Career Mode. The Morphing of skaters only involves in the facial 
 and the body area. You wont be able to morph your hands, arms, legs, feet etc. Just know that 
 it is very limited and Morphing are not as deep as THQs Smackdown Vs RAW and its not even as 
 close to our own Godfather game. Then we have about 8-10 different types of hairstyle, and tons 
 of brands of clothing for you to hook your skater up with. But Im sorry that we could not get 
 any brands and sponsors for our pants section. EA can get all the license for everything, but I 
 wonder why not for the shorts and pants.. haha.. anyway weve only created a bunch of pants for you 
 to choose from.
  
  After that, you progress by doing the tasks assigned by the pro skaters hanging around the streets. 
 This will unlocked the skaters and the sponsors that they are using. Aside from that, you are required 
 to complete photo shoots and film shoots. It gets tougher and tougher as you progress. Seriously 
 dude, just have patience doing these objectives. Finally, the X-games, which is almost impossible 
 to beat.
  
  D-Z: To be honest, Ive lost a lot of my patience on this gameso it seems like the career mode 
 is actually repetitive huh? Hmmso care to share about the A. I?
  
  EA: A. I? You want to know about the A. I? Simplethe CPU controlled skaters loves skating with you. 
 So when you hang out on an area or just wondering around, they will tend to skate around there 
 and cause you to bump on them, this will definitely disrupt your goals and timing.
  
  Normal pedestrians arent aware of your presence when you are skating face to face with them. They 
 will only evade when you are inch away from knocking them down. Or if they got knocked down, they 
 will lie flat for about 8 seconds, and got up back. Just remember its mostly the same falling animations. 
 And all of them are weak.
  
  Security guards are definitely the strongest among all the A. I. They are fast, well actually not 
 that fast, but its their funny, stupid and clunky animations make them harder to be judge and evade. 
 And if they manage to push, or punch you, which I dont exactly know what they are actually doing, 
 you will be fined $50 and thrown out of the area you are skating.
  Basically, we dont do much in the A. I.
  
  D-Z: Maybe you can improve youre A. I system in 
 skate 2 next time. So any closing comments?
  
  EA: Of Course, since skate is a next gen game, dont worry about the graphics. I can assure that 
 u will enjoy the next gen visuals, sounds, and gameplay. The sounds are definitely realistic. You 
 wont believe your ears when you hear it. This is Skate, not Tony Hawks Game. If you ever played 
 Tony Hawk before and dislikes the gameplay style. You must definitely try this. It has the flavour 
 you are looking for years.
  Skate isnt something driven with a storyline. Its just a progression of your skater with many 
 frustrating objectives. But if you love to skate, or feel like skating. I recommend you to purchase 
 this game or at least give it a rent. Ive been playing it for almost 40 hours, and still havent 
 get sick and tired of it. Just be patience, and you will enjoy the most realistic skateboarding 
 game that has ever been created.
  
  D: Z: I agree, the gameplay is really satisfying. Though there's no achievements or story line, 
 but every trick and grind you pull off, feels like an achievement. And definitely it feels new 
 to the genre. And it feels fresh. Anyway Thanks for your time.
  
  EA: Anytime.

UserName: jtvance
Rating: 9
Date: Sep 20, 2007 10:47 pm PT
Review:  Skate. is a game that totally took me by surprise. I'm a long time fan of all extreme sports games, 
 and while I ride BMX and don't skate, I know a thing or two about it. Playing Skate. makes me want 
 to go buy a skateboard. It plays and feels like real skating. While some reviews have pointed out 
 things like difficulty and a steep learning curve as weaknesses, I believe that these are actually 
 the things that make Skate. so great. Everything feels like such an accomplishment. The people 
 that feel this way are likely the people who know nothing about the actual physical aspect of skateboarding. 
 However, these people obviously aren't EA's target audience as those are the same type of people 
 who think that real skateboarders can fly 100 feet in the air and do 10 back flips. The game really 
 only needs two things to be perfect in my opinion. The first one being the ability get off your 
 board and walk around, and the second being a favorite spots system that allows you to permanently 
 mark spots in your career mode that you love to skate. You could title each one and it could show 
 up on your map, and then you should be able to select that spot and go there instantaneously. I 
 understand it sounds a bit over the top, but with an environment so huge, they really need to work 
 more on making areas easily accessible. For instance, I shouldn't have to waist my time trying 
 to grind up a rail and then ollie onto a ledge to get to large gap or drop off. In real life I'd 
 just get off my board and walk up there. Here's how I'd rate the game...
  
  Environment/Level Design: 10
  
  The environment is utterly massive. I actually would go as 
 far as to say it rivals some of the GTA cities in size.
  
  Graphics: 9
  
  EA has trumped Tony Hawk graphically by far. The game appears to run on an engine similar to most 
 of the other EA sports games and actually ends working extremely well in this application.
  
  Sound: 10
  
  What more can you say? The sound effects of the board traveling across different 
 surfaces are amazing. It no longer sounds like your on a metal rail when grinding a wooden one 
 (I'm talking about you Tony Hawk) it even makes a smooth rolling metal sound when you shred the 
 giant steel full pipes.
  
  User Interface: 8
  
  The menu system has a great art style to it, but some certain functions can be tough to find due 
 to the way everything is presented. This is a minor issue though.
  
  Gameplay: 9
  
  This could easily be improved to a 10. Just add the option to get off your board and it's perfect. 
 I love that you actually have to pump back and forth when skating transition.
  
  Replay Value: 9
  
  The extreme level of detail and sheer size of the environments will have 
 you finding and skating new lines for months to come. Overall: 9
  
  Skate is a fantastic game that only needs minor improvements to be a true masterpiece. However, 
 it easily gives a huge breath of fresh air to the dying genre.

Rating: 7.5
Date: Oct 17, 2007 5:59 am PT
Review:  skate. is EAs attempt to take the title from Neversofts long standing king of skateboarding games. 
 They arranged everything with an ingenious trick interface and a vast living world with some unique 
 twists on the goals contained therein.
  
  First off, this game was received incredibly well by the gaming community when the demo was dropped 
 on the 360 through Xbox Live. Everyone waited for this game with baited breath and, unfortunately, 
 EA failed to deliver a suitable number of copies to stores for its opening weekend (which was also 
 delayed) . This proved to be a very inauspicious start to the games run on store shelves. This, 
 in and of itself, was a low point in the game because we would have expected a much smoother, and 
 larger scale release from an Electronic Arts title. They are, after all, one of the largest video 
 game studios in the world.
  
  The opening of the game is a little lengthy and cannot be skipped. It starts with your character, 
 clad in black clothes with a black hoodie, hood up so you cant see his face. After jumping down 
 a stair set hes plowed by a bus. Your character is then rushed to the hospital where you receive 
 reconstructive surgery. This leads into the games Create-Your-Skater interface which involves 
 the use of their now standard four axis sliders to model and mold your players face. There are 
 also some initial clothing options available and a few generic, not totally pleasing, hair styles 
 to use. I think now is as good a time as any to point out that you cannot create a female skater. 
 This wouldnt be a big gripe for me if the game did not feature other female skater characters 
 running around. But since you can see female skaters in the game and not get to create one, its 
 a bit of a turn off.
  
  Once you get into skate. you can immediately appreciate the depth of skill involved in playing 
 this game. The control scheme can take literally hours to master, and even then you still have 
 to feel out every individual piece of the environment because nothing ever plays the same way twice. 
 Even the slightest indiscretion in your timing can trigger a bail, or at the very least, a missed 
 trick which can ruin certain runs such as video challenges.
  EA dubbed their new control scheme flick it. The two sticks are utilized in a very unique manner. 
 The left stick controls your skaters body. This is used for turning while riding, spinning in 
 the air, and even pumping in and out of transitions on half-pipes and other similar structures. 
 The right stick controls the board, holding the right stick down and then flicking it up causes 
 your skater to Ollie. Varying angles of both the initial hold and flick will lead to various 
 flip tricks. Rolling it left or right instead of flicking causes shuv-its. Grinding is automatic, 
 accomplished only by the proper aim and timing when near a grindable edge. There are slight flick 
 it movements do achieve some of the more advanced grinds like Blunt Slides. Wall rides and various 
 transition transfers are also accomplished in this fashion, asking only for proper aiming or timing. 
 This can be a short coming at times because occasionally after a grind combo or other feat your 
 character will sometimes want to roll back the way you came rather than continue the way you wanted 
 to go. Also, some since timing is so unbelievably sensitive a slight miss on a rail or grindable 
 edge can also result in a bail. Your skater will try to wall ride the object instead of grinding 
 thus resulting in a face plant. Also, since it is no longer a Dial-A-Trick system, the small 
 size of the right stick can make flicking a daunting task. Since it is almost exclusively dependent 
 upon which way you flick and so many of the tricks require control movements which are too similar. 
 You will find yourself trying to do one trick, and then doing another. This is another low point 
 in the game and no matter how good you get with the controls you will still find yourself making 
 what feels like a rookie mistake from time to time.
  
  Your character has to roll through a massive fictional city called San Vanelona. This is a very 
 well constructed city with a nice metropolitan downtown, an old city not unlike some of the classic 
 cities in Europe, a suburban element with a community center skate park, and a ritzy sort of upscale 
 area complete with a nice art museum with some fun, skateable pieces in and around it. There are 
 many great places to skate with good lines of obstacles strung together just waiting for you to 
 find them. Couple this with the challenging play control scheme and most of the lines you find 
 and successfully ride feel very good. This game had the potential to be something great.
  
  On top of all of this the game has an active replay function running all the time. You can review, 
 edit and then upload footage to either your hard drive or the skate. Reel community website so 
 that other people can see, rate, and comment on your footage. The community is still in its Beta 
 phase so it acts up from time to time, but when it works correctly it is a very nice touch to the 
 game. You can even pause the replay and take a photo, which can be saved and uploaded the same 
 way as the replays. The only fly in the proverbial ointment here is that you can only upload 3 
 replays and 6 pictures. You can save 8 replays and 12 pics on the hard drive, but that's still 
 a little scant simply because every successful line or big trick feels so good you want to save 
 it. This means there may be some over-writting or compromises in what you do and don't save and/or 
 upload to the website. Also, the website is still really acting up as of this review. Once the 
 video us uploaded you can log in to their website and edit attributes such as title, search tags, 
 and even add a short description. Sadly, the beta website has major issues saving tags and descriptions.
 
  
  The challenges are the true low point of this game, often hindering the intuitive control scheme. 
 There are only a few types available. These are simply  Competitions, which (until the XGames 
 street comp) are nothing more than mishmash best trick contests which put all 4 competitors on 
 the same obstacle at the same time; Photos, which are like one man best trick contests with a predestined 
 spot and a set score to beat; Death Races, which should be self explanatory, downhill runs with 
 3 other skaters, first to the bottom wins; and Video Challenges, where you have a set series of 
 goals (grind distance, total grind distance, air time, powerslide, and so on) and/or a score to 
 beat within 30 seconds. There is also S. K. A. T. E., a mode in which you and a pro skater play a game 
 similar to basketballs H. O. R. S. E. and one of you does a trick which the other has to match. Completing 
 these tasks usually results in coverage in either Thrasher or Skateboard Magazine. With the coverage, 
 your goal is to earn better coverage in each magazine, moving from the smaller afterthought sections 
 in the back to, ultimately, a cover shot on both magazines. Coverage in each comes from separate 
 events so you can progress all the way to the cover of one and do nothing in the other. The game 
 culminates in an XGames Mega Ramp event after the Street Contest. Each of these modes has shortcomings 
 which can be frustrating at times.
  
  With the competitions being done in a Jam type format (everyone on the obstacle at once) this can 
 lead to a lot of frustrating run-ins with the AI when they obviously believe they can ride the 
 obstacle no matter who got there first. You will find yourself being wiped out by another skater. 
 Bowl jams put all the participants in a bowl, pool, or half-pipe at once but the score is cumulative 
 and you dont have to rely on landing one best trick to win. The first round of the XGames street 
 contest works the same way, letting you utilize the entire course instead of one piece.
  
  Photo Challenges do feel a lot like solo best trick runs. The photographer picks the obstacle and 
 usually just gives you a score goal. Some of them do call for slightly more specific things like 
 do a flip trick but the real challenge usually comes from tricking the spot successfully. The 
 photographers usually pick large gaps and interesting spots like that to do your stunt. These can 
 take several minutes to complete successfully and then some can be burned in a single shot.
  
  Death races are challenging but the AI doesnt seem to utilize any real short-cuts most of 
 the time. There is a time limit and you have to pass through set gates (ala slalom) to earn more 
 time. Provided you dont give yourself a concrete facial or kiss too many cars during these runs 
 you should do alright.
  
  Video Challenges may not be insanely unique but they are done in an original way. They give you 
 the goals (as mentioned before) and a 30 second time limit, but you can perform them anywhere you 
 want. If you think a video could best be performed in a pool or half-pipe you can go there and 
 then start filming. They give you the what and you provide the where. Dont let this fool you, 
 the footage challenges are, by far, the hardest things in the game. By the time you get near the 
 end of the films list score goals become almost impossible, demanding as much as 5,000 points be 
 scored in 30 seconds. And you cannot fall. Falling counts as an automatic failure on your part. 
 The worst part is that some of them arent as liberal on the where as theyd like you to think. 
 Some require you to remain in no skate zones for the duration of the video. These zones always 
 have a security guard on patrol who will tackle you if he catches you, thus again ending your footage. 
 Also, with the mechanics of grinding and similar acts being so sensitive to timing, accomplishing 
 most of the later ones in the time allotted feels more like sheer dumb luck than a demonstration 
 of skill. I often found myself in a certain area where I knew I could accomplish the goals and 
 then my run is ruined because I missed my timing on a rail by a split second so instead of grinding 
 a good chunk of a required total he doesnt even attempt to grind it or bails for seemingly no 
 reason. The touchy nature of the physics makes some of the videos a matter of chance rather than 
 ability.
  
  There are also Own the Spot challenges you discover along the way. Completing these doesnt add 
 to coverage with either magazine but once you get sponsors it does pay cash. You have to discover 
 these spots, usually by accident though the Spot Bible feature with your map can help to give 
 you some vague hints as to where to find these spots. Once you activate one (by finding it, duh) 
 it is written to your map and you can now Own the spot. This is another type of best trick deal 
 which requires you to score a set number of points on the obstacle. However, this event is not 
 timed and can be performed at your leisure. Once you own the spot you can go back and do it again, 
 the goal being to beat your previously posted best. Scores can be uploaded to the skate. community 
 thus adding more replay value to this title. This feature can also be used online or even in a 
 turn based game on one console. Its a nice touch; I just wish they could have used it towards 
 helping magazine coverage. I also noticed (after more intense playing) that some of the spots have 
 issues with actually detecting that you did the trick. There is one called Curvature which is a 
 decorative marble structure resembling a quarter pipe. The best way to win this one is to grind 
 the back of it. The problem is that sometimes, even after grinding most of the structure (if not 
 the whole thing) it doesn't actually count your score.
  
  S. K. A. T. E. contests are another nice little diversion which pay your skater cash but dont help 
 his coverage, because the flick it system has so many similar moves this contest becomes very 
 difficult and another function of pure dumb luck. The real problem with this is that the contests 
 only count flip tricks accomplished with the flick it system and any accompanying spin. Grinds 
 dont count and neither do even tweaked grabs, ruling the latter merely as an Ollie with any encompassed 
 spin you may have done. And with the flick it systems previously mentioned sensitivity, these 
 contests become increasingly difficult, both to match pro tricks and do your own without repeating 
 anything.
  
  Last, but not least, comes the Mega Ramp event. This is where some of the games oddest features 
 come to pass. You begin with a brisk run down the massive roll in ramp and then a launch over the 
 gap. However, you also have to do something as cool in the ending quarter pipe as you did over 
 the massive gap. If you push off too hard to drop in you miss the ramp, coming back into contact 
 with it somewhere near the transition, however you go faster doing that than if you roll down the 
 ramp the whole time. Then hitting the ramp itself is about timing your flick. Flick too soon you 
 will probably bail right there. If you dont hit it in time you will just bail when you hit the 
 flat atop the landing ramp. Then, while in the air, the control scheme shows its most sensitive 
 aspect. With all of the speed you amass in the run you have to land with almost laser guided precision. 
 The slightest deviation from a straight landing will end your run prematurely. Even the left stick 
 is sensitive, the slightest tweak to the left of right will start your character on a slow spin 
 which can help take you off center when you land. Also, when you spin it responds a bit like the 
 flick it system would. Letting off the left stick doesnt make you stop, you just slow down and 
 over rotate a bit, which often adds to the levels of frustration. Sadly, since you get a much greater 
 launch here than anywhere else in the game they give you enough rope to hang yourself. Often you 
 will think you can land a greater spin than is actually possile.
  
  Also, failure of any of these goals results in an obnoxious stylized video to bring the CHALLENGE 
 FAILED menu on screen. It may not seem too annoying the first couple of times you see it, but 
 this game hinders as much on trial and error as the Stuntman games (if not more so) and after you 
 see that animation 20 or 30 times in a row when you keep failing at something you know you can 
 do it gets grating and tiresome.
  
  On top of this the camera is a real weak spot. It is filmed like someone is following you on their 
 own board holding the camera a little above knee high. This is the traditional angle of skate videos 
 and is cool to watchbut its a real burden to gameplay. More often than not the camera puts you 
 directly between it and your intended obstacle thus ruining your timing. And, as discussed earlier, 
 this ruins the root of successful tricking. It should usually remain off center but during downhill 
 runs it gets behind you, thus blocking your view of any traffic or obstacle which could, potentially, 
 keep you out of first place. During the mega ramp it inexplicably rotates to the side of your character 
 both when you air off the ramp and when you hit the massive quarter pipe at the end. This makes 
 noticing a slight rotation on your part or a less than perfect landing incredibly difficult to 
 detect. All of this helps to needlessly complicate a game that already came out of the gate with 
 its own unique challenges and complications.
  
  On top of it's lofty online support for single player achievements the game also has some excellent 
 online play. There are multiple race events and trick events online. These usually just take single 
 player modes and make them online competitions. I spend most of my time in Spot Battle which is 
 a version of Own the Spot where players go in turn and everyone gets 3 turns. Best trick wins. 
 Spot jam and Best trick comps are not my cup of tea if only because you can have too many people 
 shoved into spots. Winning (or even scoring) in race or trick events scores experience points which 
 helps to determine a player's over-all rank online as much as simply winning a few runs. Most of 
 your fellow players online have been pretty cool, laid back, and void of trash talk. Often there 
 are at least moderate cheers of support when you do something cool and own the spot. This is a 
 nice bonus point to the online mode simply because most of my last experiences with online play 
 have involved acres of trash talk, insults, ridiculous blame casting, and other obnoxious traits. 
 This doesn't really affect my over all scores too much but it ensures that 9 times out of 10 I 
 don't really invest much time in most games' multiplayer modes.
  
  This game had some lofty ambitions. It had some very unique control ideas, and some beautiful elements 
 to the game that made it truly unique and at times enjoyable. However, the limited challenge variety, 
 coupled with the occasionally terribly sensitive flick it system, this game fell short of the 
 mark and I believe has failed to make the boys at Neversoft sweat about its release too much. I 
 only hope for a sequel, because taken at face value this game cant earn the coveted 10/10 score 
 (or even very close to it) . But, as a starting point, it shows some real potential for a great 
 seriesprovided the masterminds at EA Black Box stay the course and merely improve this game for 
 the next installment. Kudos to them for a dynamite first effort.

Rating: 9.5
Date: Sep 20, 2007 7:20 pm PT
Review:  First off id like to say im mostly dissapointed with gamespots review. It dogged on it more than 
 supported it. They rated Two Worlds with the same score, and Two Worlds really wasnt that great 
 at all. You can read my other review about that there. So, now i will give you my honest opinion 
 about SKATE. THIS GAME ROCKS!!!!! I've played skateboarding games since the dawn of them, from 
 Thrasher, the Tony Hawk series and Grind Session. These were all great. Until now, mainly because, 
 SKATE brings the enjoyment and difficulty of real skating home.... FINALLY. You have a giant city 
 to skate around, and if you're a skater, you will spot stuff you want to conquer. I found a huge 
 rail thats like 150 ft long and i kept trying to nail it again and again until i got it. Its realistic 
 properties are really comforting becaue when you have the skill to throw a 360 hardflip or a varial 
 kickflip every time, you know you can dominate in the game mode S. K. A. T. E.. There is so much to 
 learn and it takes practice. If you want a game thats easy to do a 900, play tony hawk. you want 
 a game that takes practice to throw what you want, SKATE is for you. There tons of challenges, 
 races, and plain fun to be had in this game. Now for the bad, which it really isnt that bad. Gamespot 
 was right about one thing, the camera angle kinda gets in the way. and its following techniques 
 are kinda funky. The online play sometimes gets lagy, but thats only cause people have crappy internet, 
 or they quit mid-game. Other than that there really isnt much else bad to say other than its a 
 game, and there will be bugs. Overall, its one of the best innovations of a skating video games 
 ever to be made. Period. Just as first person shooters these days take skill to be the best, you 
 will need skillz to throw down in SKATE. It makes it interesting and fun and theres tons to learn. 
 So, with that said, go break some bones and go SKATE!

UserName: kbshaffer
Rating: 9.5
Date: Sep 20, 2007 6:58 pm PT
Review:  What makes a good game for you? For me, a good game is one that I can pick up and play for 10 minutes, 
 or for 2 hours. A good game is one where the environment can capture your attention and hold it, 
 making the campaign a fun option, not a grueling grind. Unless you are in a hurry to get as many 
 sponsors and gear as possible, then the city of San Vanelona will surely distract you at every 
 corner, curb, bench, staircase, bleachers, statue... you get the picture. I have logged probably 
 close to 20 hours so far and I am only at the shoe sponsor (second sponsor) in career mode. This 
 is largely because having full access to all the tricks and most of the city to start out with 
 is so much entertainment right off the bat. Plus, if you are a skater who skates for fun and the 
 culture, then who needs sponsors anyway? I won't deny that free gear is always rad though.
  
  Kudos to EA for having the balls to make a game that takes time to learn, and is reasonably 
 difficult to play afterwards. For those of us that have been playing games since we were little 
 (for me, 16+ years!) its hard not to get excited when we don't succeed at something on the first 
 try. And if you are a wuss that gives up after failing at something once then you are the reason 
 most games are made to make sure they get approval from the mommy's boys of the world, AND, don't 
 bother buying this game, and please don't bother skewing the game rating with your lack of determination. 
 I'll end this just by saying it is worth 60 bucks. Go get it.

UserName: slayerver1
Rating: 9
Date: Sep 20, 2007 12:49 pm PT
Review:  The skateboarding genre of video games was pushed to a new level with the Tony Hawk series. It 
 made skateboarding popular again reaching out to a new audience. As the years go by, yearly installments 
 of the Tony Hawk games had become just another game in the series with not much improvements made 
 every game. This year, EA decides to take a crack of the skateboarding genre letting the Black 
 Box studio develop a completely new game called Skate. Skate takes a different approach to skateboarding 
 games and takes the genre to a whole new level with its innovative gameplay and controls. For any 
 skateboarding fan, Skate is probably the best game of the genre this year and highly recommended.
 
  
  Skate has arguably the best intro ever for an alternative sports game with you getting hit by a 
 bus and taken to the hospital by actual skaters with different roles. It is pretty funny seeing 
 pro skaters act completely different than their skater roles like Danny Way, Paul Rodriguez, and 
 MTV's new comedic duo Rob and Big. After recovering from surgery, you start your career customizing 
 your body, face, and outfit then going out to San Vanelona making a name for yourself and the skating 
 world. The career mode is basically completing goals to get in two skateboarding magazines and 
 then competing in the X Games to win a gold medal. These goals range from photo challenges, tasks 
 that pro skaters give you, contests, death races, and film challenges that can be done anywhere 
 in the open world Skate gives you. While making yourself known, you will get sponsors from many 
 of the skateboarding companies that offer different decks, outfits, trucks, and wheels to customize. 
 Certain spots of San Vanelona are no skating zones as security guards try to run you down. Some 
 of these challenges can be difficult requiring specific tricks to complete them and get frustrating 
 at times especially doing the wrong tricks to restarting like 50 times. Another frustrating aspect 
 of the single player is pedestrians getting in the way when pulling off combos. The session markers 
 are helpful especially it takes forever to go back to some place you have a hard time on. The career 
 mode in the end is pretty good putting your skateboarding skills to the test in every way that 
 the game gives you for tricks.
  
  The controls for Skate is the major reason the gameplay is innovative. Instead of pressing buttons 
 to do magical tricks in Tony Hawk, nearly all of the tricks can be done using the analog sticks 
 and triggers. The left stick is basically your body movement and the right stick is your board 
 movement. Ollies can be done by holding down the right stick then tilting up. Flip tricks are done 
 by flicking the right stick in different directions such as kickflips flicking right. The harder 
 flip tricks like the 360 flip require different rotations of the right stick and these harder tricks 
 are required especially for S. K. A. T. E. challenges, which is basically horse in this game. Nollies 
 are the opposite the ollies done the opposite way which adds another array of tricks at your disposal. 
 Grab tricks are done by the left and right triggers in the air. The face buttons are used for braking 
 and pushing. Grinding is as simple as olling to the rail similar to the SSX games. You can also 
 pull backflips, frontflips, and spins by tilting the left stick in the air. Skate's control system 
 is revolutionary for a skateboarding game and delivers more satisfaction towards nailing these 
 tricks in lines and combos than something like the Tony Hawk games especially skating on a megaramp.
 
  
  After the single player career mode is done with, there are multiplayer modes in this game. Party 
 play is basically the local multiplayer playing simliar modes to the single player like S. K. A. T. E, 
 contests, and Spot challenges. Online multiplayer is where it is at with a maximum of six players 
 playing different modes ranging from races to best trick events. The online aspect is a great demonstration 
 of the actual skateboarding lifestyle when players are pushed to the limit nailing huge combos. 
 The community aspect of Skate is also another great demonstration of actual skateboarding with 
 replays, photos of your moves, and actual video footage of your greatest feats. The Skate reel 
 is where it is at for watching your own footage and looking your at your photos as well as watching 
 other players' footage while rating them. There is also a spectator mode called Skate TV to check 
 out actual online sessions. The online portion of Skate is probably the best online execution for 
 a skateboarding ever specifically the community features.
  
  The graphics of Skate are great for this type of game actually looking like a next gen game. The 
 city of San Vanelona is huge for something like Skate with many obstacles for players to go crazy. 
 Each of the four sections of San Vanelona offer enough variety for the player to pull off moves. 
 The characters look good enough as well with the pro skaters being accurate to their real counterparts. 
 The presentation of Skate is executed well also remaining accurate to the skateboarding lifestyle.
 
  
  The sound in Skate is also great with decent voice overs by pro skaters and different characters. 
 The soundtrack can be executed better, but it is good enough. Listening to the same song on the 
 menu screen can get a little repetitive. The music only goes berserk when your multiplier is at 
 three times and certain hotspots of the city which is executed well too, but the music won't play 
 all the time while skating. The songs themselves are great for this type of game especially the 
 hip-hop. Blasting NWA's Express Yourself while skating never felt better. The sound effects for 
 the board are also accurate while doing flip tricks and landing.
  
  Skate is probably the best skateboarding game out this year. It represents the skateboarding lifestyle 
 accurately and delivers innovative controls. The online features are also amazing for this type 
 of game as playing with friends is really fun. The general satisfaction of nailing huge combos 
 is excellent especially when something sick happens even though the learning curve may be steep 
 for some players. Fans of skateboarding should buy this game and hopefully EA can make this to 
 a franchise with more in the future.

UserName: mattrix42
Rating: 9
Date: Sep 19, 2007 6:16 pm PT
Review:  First of all I have to say that I've been a massive Tony Hawk Pro Skater fan for years. Lately 
 the series had been getting a little stale (the last one I bought was THUG) but it took a game 
 like Skate to really open my eyes to how far away from skateboarding THPS had drifted. I used to 
 skate back in the day and I never remember grinding on cruise ship railings or shimmying across 
 balconies four stories in the air while wearing a clown suit. Everything about Skate feels so much 
 more authentic... the controls, the graphics, the audio, the tricks, the characters, the story. 
 The flick controls are revolutionary... simple to learn, hard to master, subtle in their complexity. 
 Skate has it's shortcomings... things which I'm sure will be added in subsequent versions like more 
 player customization options, a skate park editor, and a trick editor. However, E. A. did the right 
 thing by saving these extra features for the sequels and concentrating on delivering a solid foundation 
 for the core skateboarding experience... and in that sense they've exceeded my expectations. Goodbye 
 Tony... you had a great run but it had to come to an end some time. Skate has just made you obsolete.
