UserName: siteless_one
Rating: 9
Date: Sep 19, 2007 11:34 am PT
Review:  It's not too often i can realy say this: I love this game. If your like me you were playing the 
 demo for weeks befor the game came out. If your not like me, what the hell are you waiting for? 
 this game is, among other things, beauitful. the level design, although at time can be frustrating 
 is well planed out and unfolds like any other skating game. What stands out the most in this game 
 is the awsome array of styels a player can skate. It may seem that every one is landing the same 
 tricks the same ways but infact, i have never seen two people play this game the same as one another. 
 some may take to the streets and tare it up while others may search for the vast array of pools 
 and half pipes to grab some air. some players are fast and aggressive and still others take their 
 time to perfect the look and style of their skater. This video game is not just a nother sports 
 game that will fall by the way side. The players have spoken, they want more and more. The only 
 cridisism i may have with this game is that there is no flatland and you can not get off of your 
 board. So while you cant simply walk up stairs or recreate the most tech skater of all time, rodney 
 mullen, the game still falles nothing short of perfection (in a sports game) . Im sorry Game Spot, 
 but i have to dissagree with you guys on this one. I give this game an 9.0 because its just plane 
 fun, online or off. with a few minor improvments, the next instalment of skate may just be the 
 most fun you can have with a sports video game.

UserName: bacoker
Rating: 9
Date: Sep 18, 2007 10:26 pm PT
Review:  This game is by far and away the best skateboarding game to date. The biggest draw for me, having 
 skated for 12 years, is the realism. Unlike in the Tony Hawk series, you will not be doing any 
 out-of-control 540 flip to frontside noseblunt to backside tailslide to 360 hardflip to manual 
 out. In skate., you are pretty much stuck to doing tricks that can and have been done if real life 
 skating, with a few exceptions. The graphics are great, and the fictional city that you skate has 
 a combination of spots similar to some of the best spots to skate in real life, ie. Hubba Hideout, 
 Embacadero, Art Institute, Streets of San Fran etc. The controls take a little time to get used 
 to, but add to the realism of the game. The ability to film your tricks, edit footage, and upload 
 to the net is a great addition to the game. I didn't rate it a 10 because there are a few thing 
 I would like to see added, such as night skating, and being able to step off the board. Other than 
 a few minor flaws such as those, this game is great!

UserName: Rekunta
Rating: 7.5
Date: Sep 18, 2007 5:33 pm PT
Review:  I love and hate this game in equal measure. It is so frustrating on so many levels, yet is equally 
 amazing to the same degree.
  
  I'm a pessimist, so I'll start out with the negative. I posted this in the SKATE forum and it explains 
 what I feel is flawed:
  
  The complexity of this game which makes it so incredible and innovative is also what makes it so 
 ultimately frustrating. The commonality between some moves is so close it's almost fruitless to 
 try to differentiate them in execution. For example, the variant 360 kick flip and the 360 pop 
 shuvit are so similar that I've only got the variant 360 three times in a row. I don't fault the 
 game for this, it's a game design and hardware issue (tiny area for the analog to move) combined. 
 Also, certain trick motions overlap each other, so if you move the stick just a slight bit past 
 where you need to change direction for one move, it's too late. For, example, look at the 360 Pop 
 Shuvit (medium) versus the 360 flip (advanced) .
  
  Another thing that adds to the slighty imprecise nature of the stick controls is the pace of which 
 the game moves. It's always just a matter of seconds to act, and remembering all the different 
 variations (not to mention the corresponding control input depending on the foot placement while 
 grinding, not to mention balance) makes it incredibly difficult for me to even pull off one or 
 two moves. That's not mentioning keeping the board on the line after hopping to a different trick, 
 then proceeding to Ollie into the air, pull the trigger, and think of one hold, spin, or flip to 
 do. Usually my long chains come from rapid fumbling and doing whatever I can within the time allowed. 
 A cool replay no doubt, but far from gratifying game-play wise.
  
  Don't get the wrong impression, I think this game is amazing, innovative, and just plain fun in 
 so many ways but to be honest it's detracting from my overall enjoyment which is too bad, because 
 I really want to get proficient at this game since it's obvious how much depth SKATE has, yet it 
 almost feels unreachable. 
  
  One more thing to add to the above: the camera is a problem. it is WAY too low which makes it hard 
 to line up as the skater's body is impeding your ability to see where you're going, which also 
 applies to when you turn. It also flops around occasionally which is a serious flaw considering 
 the precise nature of the controller input required. It is also not adjustable, which would be 
 immensely helpful as your view would not be blocked.
  
  After all that negative, I'm too tired to explain the positive and this is way too long. Just play 
 the game to see it or read the millions of 10s on this site.
  
  A cool but flawed game. Be prepared to practice, and pray for that varial. 
::::::

UserName: astrotaylor
Rating: 9
Date: Sep 18, 2007 9:35 am PT
Review:  Skate starts off fun, asking only for simple tricks or combinations to continue your advancement. 
 Once you reach AM or Pro status the game begins to raise the bar and it can be a major pain to 
 accomplish the goals when you have to ollie on to a box, land in a manual, ollie a gap to another 
 box, and land in a manual again, then land the trick. Retrying a goal can be annoying if you've 
 traveled far enough from the starting location that it has to kick back to a loading screen. As 
 far as skateboarding games go, this has to be the most realistic I've ever seen or played. Once 
 you ignore the goals and just skate around town having fun, it quickly becomes one of the funnest 
 games I've been lucky enough to pick up. Got the last one on the shelf at the Anchorage, AK Best 
 Buy on release day!

UserName: frigginjoe
Rating: 8.5
Date: Sep 17, 2007 11:06 pm PT
Review:  Skate nails the skateboarding game by moving in the exact opposite direction of the Tony Hawk series 
 - focusing the gameplay on the feel and challenge of the skating itself.
  The open-ended world really lends to skateboarding, as the exploration and constant lookout for 
 environmental trick opportunities is a big part of street skating. The graphics are great, though 
 not without their faults. While the soundtrack is more of the same, the sound effects are dead 
 on and truly add to the feel of being on a board with the wheels screeching, chirping, humming 
 and clacking as you traverse over various textured grounds.
  The most appreciable aspect of Skate is that the challenge lies in timing, placement and location 
 rather than taking the fiction over the top ala Tony Hawk's Pro Skater. In doing this, it's thankfully 
 spaced itself apart from the aging Tony Hawk series, not to mention up the ante for future installations 
 of both series.

UserName: okcomputer666
Rating: 8
Date: Sep 17, 2007 8:44 pm PT
Review:  I've been waiting for a good skate boarding game to come out ever since I got burned out on Tony 
 Hawk after the first THUG game. I always enjoyed the gameplay of the Tony Hawk games, but it seemed 
 like the gameplay kept getting stretched thinner and thinner with each new game. After playing 
 the Skate demo to death I figured that Skate would be that game, and thankfully it is. I never 
 liked the super arcade like feel of the Tony Hawk games so it was really refreshing to be able 
 to play a game that focused more on reality rather than just pulling off million point combos. 
 While the gameplay of Skate is rather realistic it feels like it came at a price. While it's extremely 
 rewarding when you do pull off amazing lines and tricks, it gets very difficult to execute them 
 with any sense of procession. The pacing of the game doesn't help much either. After about two 
 or three hours of playing, the challenges went from fairly simple and straight forward to being 
 balls to the wall difficult. I went from simply having to grind three times to complete a challenge 
 to having to find 21 foot drops while having to score at least 1,500 points in 30 seconds. After 
 about 20 minutes of skating around trying to find a large enough drop, I spent at least another 
 hour trying to pull it off. I cannot tell you how many times I went flying into a light post. After 
 what seemed like an eternity of trying to pull off the jump I finally did..... only to get hit by 
 a car and having to start it all over again. Eventually, I finally completed the challenge which 
 unlocked about 10 other challenges. While that may sound harsh, it never got to the point where 
 I was frustrated enough to quit or smash the controller simply because it was always fun. While 
 it maybe a difficult game, it is always entertaining and you always feel like you are accomplishing 
 something. If you have the dexterity and the will power to hammer through the harder challenges, 
 you'll find a game that rewards your skill and determination. Or you can simply just free skate 
 which is always fun.

UserName: chocolatelepre
Rating: 9
Date: Sep 17, 2007 7:06 pm PT
Review:  simply put, this is what i have wanted tony hawk to attempt to make for years now. this game is 
 meant to appeal to skaters first, and the general public second. sure, it is easy enough to push 
 around doing tricks, but just like real skating, more difficult tricks require more time spent 
 on learning them. the filming is tough and frustrating at times, but have you ever tried to film 
 a real skate line? i can assure you it is way more frustrating. and when you finally have the control 
 to get a specific trick, the feeling of rolling away is almost as gratifying as the real thing. 
 the level is also a welcome change. when tony hawk's american wasteland promised a vast, seamless 
 level, this is what i envisioned. there are specific spots to skate, but the most fun comes from 
 cruising around, bombing hills, and doing insanely long lines. every object is skateable in some 
 way, and the only limitation is your imagination. kudos to ea for the line multiplier. it is much 
 more realistic for a couple of good tricks to come in a row rather than one long trick connected 
 by manuals, reverts, spraypainting and walking around. finally, the amount of support from the 
 skating community is superb. most of the times i get upset when companies cram as much advertising 
 into the game as possible. but in skate, it feels right. all the clothing, skateboards, and shoes 
 are real life items and its crazy that my digital skater can look so similar to how i look when 
 i skate. the long list of pros in the game is also impressive. i probably means nothing to you, 
 but seeing a legend like mark gonzalez or a relatively underground skater like jerry hsu is insane. 
 it really shows how much ea was focusing on the realism of the skate scene. the things the pros 
 and the filmer say are things me and my friends say when we skate. to sum it up, throw out your 
 latest copy of tony hawk and go pick this up.

UserName: punkdsk8erdude
Rating: 10
Date: Sep 17, 2007 2:21 pm PT
Review:  As a long time Tony Hawk fan, its saying a lot when I can say this game, regardless its a different 
 style of skateboarding game (sim rather than arcade) this is by far easily the best skateboarding 
 game ever, not to mention one of the best videogames i've ever owned.
  Graphics - incredible. Very, very realistic. Except for the plants. some of the plants aren't too 
 great.
  The customization - ok. Theres a great seletion of boards, trucks, and wheels, but the character 
 customization, aside from the body type creation, is'nt very good. I'm talking about choices of 
 hair and clothing. The clothes is a prettywide selection but the hair, is pathetic.
  The SKATING - holy crap where do i begin. in real life i love bombing hills. In this game, i love 
 bombing hills lol. It's so much fun to just actually skateboard, just riding the board is great 
 fun, not even doing tricks.
  I love when you loosen your trucks and you go down hill in the San Francisco style area The Res 
 and you see your board wobble under your feet.
  Its just great fun.
  Some of the bails are silly, but a lot of them are realistic as well.
  Look, all i can say is 
 play the game yourself. I can't put it in words how good this game is.
  However, i can say its not perfect.
  Let me just say what EA should do for skate 2 if there ever 
 is one which im sure there will be after the success of this amazing game.
  -the ability to get off your board.
  Im not talking tony hawk style parcour jumping around climbing 
 on buildings, im just talking about the ability to get off your skateboard, walk up a stair set, 
 get in position, drop your board and do what you wanna do. There are a lot of times i see a spot 
 i wanna skate, lets say a 12 stair or something, and i have to skate around it usually up some 
 sort of slope to get to the top to finally skate it. The session markers are useful, but you have 
 to get there in the first place lol. I think just being able to get off the board would be really 
 useful.
  -Have the skateboard break.
  In real life, there are pressure cracks, chipping, and breaking of the decks. Also, the wheels 
 get smaller over time as well.
  There is such a wide selection of boards and wheels and trucks, i think they should have the board 
 break realistically, so you have to buy a new one. I think they wheels should get really small, 
 and have that affect how well your board controls and skates and how fast etc etc so you feel obligated 
 to buy a new set every now and then, and i think your trucks should get flattened on from grinding 
 too much so you need a new pair. I think thats realistic, and it help promotes the great selection 
 the game provided. Its pointless to waste your hard earned cash in the game on a new deck because 
 you never see the bottom except when you buy it, and it never breaks. So whats the point? The wheels 
 you see, as well as the trucks so that makes sense.
  Also, talking about wheels, instead of having the tuning option of hardening/softening your wheels, 
 i dont think they should have that. Thats not realistic. They should have it so the wheels you 
 buy have the size, and also the duro (for those of you who dont really skate thats the level of 
 hardness, the higher the number, usually in the 90s or hundred, the harder the wheel.) so i think 
 that affects what wheels you buy. If you want hard wheels you buy hard wheels you want soft wheels 
 you buy soft wheels lol.
  That simple.
  So, with these 3 things, i think the game would be perfect. And it's only three things, so that 
 game is pretty much perfect lol.
  I love this game.
  Bought it the morning it came out, played it for 4 hours straight the day i got it, and have played 
 it about an hour each day since. =] I love this game, great job EA. I was originally gunna buy 
 the new tony hawk also, but after getting skate, theres no point. idc if one is a sim and one is 
 arcade, skate is just simply amazing.

Review:  Growing up, I always looked at skateboarding as a suburban, whiteboy activity that was laughed 
 upon as they buss their asses trying to be Tony Hawk... then Tony Hawk came out... After mastering 
 skate-or-die and 720, I thought that Tony Hawk was the Bee's Knees and nothing would change that. 
 I bought every Tony Hawk with the hope of making my own unique hoodlum amongst preppies and all 
 would be well... Never really got me that good but I was nice in the T. H. games and I mastered 
 most of the tricks and learned how to exploit the games with high score tactics and everything 
 was cool... All hail Christ Air... Then that all changed when I had a chance to befriend a guy 
 who was just skating by one day and I learned that skateboarding is indeed a culture and my ignorance 
 was no longer blissful... I began to see the little things like the importance of photo's and video 
 footage. The importance of truck stiffness and wheel softness... the fact that I ran into many 
 of great boarders and none of them can ollie flip in midair then convert to a christ-air and land. 
 None of them could grind a telephone line and drop that many feet onto flat surface and maintain 
 speed... I was upset... They weren't real skateboarders and the game was reality... then my views 
 change when I popped in skate... From the moment you touch the controller, your soul will become 
 that of your onscreen counterpart... every nook and cranny of this game speaks that of the culture 
 itself. Graphics are second to none... Gameplay is terrific... I love the fact that there are plenty 
 of real life pros in the game and they have been gradually been implemented.... They could have 
 plastered all of the features on the box but didn't when I ran into a few pros that I have grown 
 fond of watching xgames and such is a real treat... this game is a new cult classic for the ages... 
 A breakthrough... The same way we make our younger kinfolk laugh when we pop in Supermario Brothers, 
 This will have the same effect for tomorrow... The only thing that I would like to see in the next 
 one -- Have the skater be able to hop off the board and walk around.... Thats about it... Grab onto 
 cars for more speed and momentum...

UserName: timmyg15
Rating: 9
Date: Sep 17, 2007 9:51 am PT
Review:  I've been waiting for a game like this since the PlayStation2 launched. The Tony Hawk series had 
 a monopoly on the skateboarding genre in the ps2/xbox generation consoles, and i would rather play 
 'Thrasher: Skate and Destroy (1999) on ps1 over any tony hawk game released.
  
  Skate combines next gen graphics with next gen gameplay and the outcome is a highly enjoyable to 
 play skateboarding game. What sets Skate apart from most other skateboarding games *cough* tony 
 hawk series *cough* is its commitment to realism. The physics and the general pace of the game 
 are very real to life, maybe not 100% accurate, but close enough. Skate excels with graphics, gameplay, 
 control, sound effects, and sound track. Anyone who has tried skateboarding will appreciate the 
 control and realism of this game more than someone who has not. The controls may seem a little 
 difficult at first, but really just need some getting used to. As you get better you'll find pulling 
 off some difficult tricks very rewarding. And when you do you can save your replay, and even upload 
 it online! This game has a story and plenty of tasks for you to do, but in the beginning you'll 
 most likely just skate around and enjoy the gameplay.
  
  There are only a few things i do not like about this game. First, the camera can sometimes be annoying 
 and block you from seeing what you need to see. The game needs some additional camera view options. 
 Also, you cannot get off your skateboard and walk. Skate has open-ended gameplay similar to the 
 Grand Theft Auto series, in which you are placed in a fictional city and can wander and do as you 
 please, and sometimes it would be useful to be able to get off your board so you can reach some 
 difficult places. Lets not forget that this is the first release of most likely many games in this 
 series. The sequels to this game will most likely address and fix any bugs, and improve slightly 
 with each release. I would give this game an even better score if not for the fact that i know 
 they will release a sequel thats even better.

  Pro:
  Realistic, you can not grind 2 miles on a telephone wire
  
  Inovative, Flick it controls although 
 they can be difficult to use, still gives you a better feel for the trick your attempting
  
  Graphics, Wow...
  
  Cons (not nesessarily a bad thing, just areas to improve on a sequal)
 
  
  Goofy=Mongo?, For those of you who have selected goofy footed stance you will notice that your 
 skater constanly skates mongo. For those of you who do not skate this may not sound like that big 
 of a deal, but when youride one way and your seeing something different on the screen it does cause 
 some frustration and confusion
  
  Pedestrian, Way to many of them. Every 3-5 minutes I am fighting to stand up properly and carry 
 on my usual buisness. Seems like some of the better spots on the game has anywhere from 3-7 pedstrians 
 standing/walking through the center at all times.
  
  Camera Angles, it would be nice to have an adjustable camera. The one set angle is extremely close 
 and makes it difficult to see the area around you, and as most will notice occasionally the camera 
 will lose you.
  
  The abiltity to step off your board, not for random stupid combos, but for not having to ollie 
 over every insignificant crack just o get to were it is your going. It can also become very frustrating 
 looking for handi-cap accessable ramps so you can get to the staircase or ledge you want to skate.
 
  
  
  Overal EAs Skate is an extremely addictive game that can easily overthrow the Tony Hawk franchise, 
 it just needs a few kinks worked out of it.

UserName: destinhpark
Rating: 9.5
Date: Sep 16, 2007 12:54 pm PT
Review:  There's been countless Tony Hawk games coming out over the years, but all the recent ones, as we 
 all know, have sucked miserably.
  
  now, along with Tony Hawk's Proving Grounds, there's a new kid on the block. And his name, is skate.
 
  
  first of all, I'd like to note how extremely innovative and original skate.'s gameplay is. this 
 isn't any sort of button mashing grind session tony hawk deal. all of the flip tricks, ollies, 
 and spins are accomplished using the analog sticks. sounds weird, huh? it is at first. but once 
 you play through the tutorial a bit, you pick up the controls fairly easily. but as you keep playing, 
 you'll definitely notice that your flickit control skills are rising each time you play.
  
  the control in itself is a fun learning experience, and you'll feel like you're actually, gradually 
 getting somewhere in the game. this is a nice feeling, considering i haven't felt like this in 
 a game for a long, long time.
  
  moving on and more technically speaking, the games audio and visual aspects are beyond superb. 
 the sound effects when riding over cracks on a sidewalk, or grinding a curb alongside of a main 
 highway sound impeccable, thus it is a major addition to the overall experience you'll feel while 
 playing. the visuals are top-notch and include sharp character models and boards. the city is massive 
 and very nicely detailed, down to each little window, nook, and cranny you can skate through. and 
 this is what makes skate. so much fun. from the very start of the game, the entire city is yours 
 to explore, although you do get to unlock a few smaller locations on the way, mostly skateparks, 
 x-games, etc. but the main entire area that is San Velona is all yours to skate up. and there's 
 so many small areas to find, including sewage drains you can skate all the way down with various 
 rails and banks, tons and tons of various staircases, and much much more.
  
  the game certainly doesn't lack in content, as the single player will take you quite some time 
 to complete. and you unlock loads of extras along the way like secret characters and playable pros, 
 clothes, boards, videos, and beyond.
  
  after SP though, the game does contain a 6 player multiplayer suite which is surprisingly, very 
 deep. there's over 6 gametypes that include races, competitive trick modes, and of course, freeskate. 
 personally, i find freeskate the most fun because you can kind of just chill and skate around while 
 you socialize with everyone, and watch some real good players pull of insane tricks. it's a blast, 
 and what's even more of a blast is creating replay videos yourself.
  
  that's right. skate. contains a replay editor where you can create short videos after pulling off 
 a sick trick, or having a glorious bail. the editors contains options such as visual effects, which 
 there are about 5 of that mainly change the color scale on the screen, camera angles, and the overall 
 speed of motion the video is playing at. these options are a ton of fun to mess around with, and 
 you'll sometimes even feel like a professional when you create a great video, upload it online 
 and receive tons of reviews. other players can score your video on just how sick they really are, 
 and i find it fun to get a lot of great feedback.
  
  the overall feeling of skate. is generally very fresh, new and extremely satisfying. if you're 
 into skating, there's no way you should miss this game whatsoever. however, even if you've never 
 really been into skating, you should give skate. a try simply because of its originality and flavor. 
 skate.'s just one of those rare games that completely redefines a genre and nails it perfectly. 
 so as a skater, i say, go for it.

Review:  Every time i land a trick i feel as if im landing it in real life, the motions for the tricks just 
 add so much feel to the game, and the graphics are pretty impressive too, its not the same button 
 mashing fantasy world as tony hawk's games. The only thing that i don't find realistic in this 
 game, is how easy it is to do a manual for half a mile or more, as i've already done. The only 
 thing i don't like about the game, is sometimes you get stuck somewhere running into walls, and 
 you say to yourself damn i wish i could get off this board, and walk to that spot . Over all this 
 game is amazing, and is revolutionary to skateboarding games.

UserName: radioheadfan07
Rating: 9.5
Date: Sep 16, 2007 11:41 am PT
Review:  First of all, let me say this is my 1st review. Skate is extremely fun and refreshing from tony 
 hawk, but it has a few flaws that bring it down a bit.
  
  Graphics:
  
  Graphics are very nice, probobly one of the best ive seen on the 360. Everything looks really nice 
 except for the cars, which really dont matter.
  
  Controls:
  
  Controls are extremely unique and fun. Although, i do have some complaints. I think the flickit 
 system doesnt always recognize that well, it feels almost impossible to ollie without kickflipping 
 5 times before you actually get it right. But overall the controls are done extremely well.
  
  Gameplay:
  
  San Venelona is huge and right for any player, and its easy to loose 6 hours 
 in 1 sitting. The only complaint i really have about the city is (i know theyre here to try to 
 make it more realistic) the dam padestrians walking around can be extremely annoying when trying 
 to get a challenge done. While were talking about challenges, some of them are very hard, but once 
 you beat it you get a huge sense of accomplishment. Just skating around is very fun and, combined 
 with the organic control scheme, is a great experience. Voice acting is really nice, and seeing 
 all of the pro's gear and stuff is a really nice feature.
  
  Overall, Skate is an amazing game that everyone should have, a few flaws brought it down to 9.5, 
 otherwise i could have easily gave it a 10.
  
  Please, please go buy skate right now, its worth it, trust me!!

Rating: 9.5
Date: Sep 16, 2007 10:06 am PT
Review:  No need to get discourged by the first two letters of the game, hence EA. EA's Skate is as realistic 
 and innovating as a skateboarding game can be. Begining with a brand new control shchme that deals 
 mainy with the analog sticks, it has you in a satisfiying state of control over what your skater 
 does and how he does it. To sumerize it, the left analog stick controls you skaters body while 
 the right one controls his board. The buttons X and A are useed as you feet to push both left or 
 right as well as the triggers control you hands both left and right. Besides the very responsive 
 control scheme EA skate deals largley with realistic physiscs and a true to life sound system unlike 
 any other in a skate game. There are many little details in the game that make it very innovating. 
 Two examples would be how you grind and manual. To grind you would do as you would in real life 
 and jump on the rail, ledge ect.. to grind or slide. Also for manuals its all about find that sweet 
 spot on the analog. Beside the tech stufff, Skate puts you in a HUGE open city waiting to be skated 
 and backs it up with true next generation graphics and pyhsiscs. This games all about being part 
 of a magizine cover for thrasher and becoming a pro. You have to work for it. Ea skate does support 
 a fullly featured online aspect in this game, and even though when in game it can seem a bit on 
 the low FPS side, it has so many features involving so many things LOOK there is to MUCH to talk 
 about with this game in one review. STOP READING THIS AND GO TO YOUR LOCAL GAMEPOT, EB GAMES ECT.. 
 AND BUY THIS GAME. YOU WONT BE DISAPOINTED. O and this game KILLS tony hawk back to the stone age.

 reviewing something they don't understand. 2 of the main criticisms of the game is that there aren't 
 enough tricks, and the goals are too basic. The deal with the tricks is that yes they left tricks 
 out, BUT most of those tricks you don't even do in actual skatboarding. I can't remember the last 
 time i saw someone do a pressure flip, yet this guy claims that it's a street skating staple, obviously 
 this person knows nothing about skateboarding. To say you wish their were more tricks, fair enough, 
 we could always use more, more, more. But to elaborate about these multiple tricks as street skating 
 staples, is just to show your complete ignorance to the sport you are trying to discuss. And about 
 the objectives, it's kinda nice to play a game that the only point is not to just merely make it 
 from A to B to C. There is something more there that moves beyond Button Mashing and blowing through 
 objectives.

 it's funny how he says this right after he talks about the fact that you actually progress as a 
 player and not just as a number stat system. And yes, it is easy once you figure out the right 
 touch, EXACTLY like skateboarding, it's called muscle memory.

Review:  I have always played Tony Hawk when it comes to skating games on a console, and i was anxious to 
 see if i would really like this game, or if i would want to throw it at my tv and burn it. Tony 
 Hawk has always had that unrealistic feel, you don't push buttons to make your skater move, and 
 you must repeatedly button mash your way to new tricks. Also for Tony Hawk, the physics are very 
 unrealistic with what i call, 'moon gravity'.
  
  Skate has revolutionized all of the skating games. From its amazing physics, awesome graphics, 
 and a completely new and fresh attempt to controls. I highly reccomend this game to ANYONE that 
 is even Slightly interested in skateboarding. The difficulty factor does take an amount of time 
 to master but once you do you will love this game even more.

::::::
UserName: SSGDevilDog
Rating: 9
Date: Sep 15, 2007 11:45 am PT
Review:  I've heard many different games over the years being described as easy to learn, difficult to master. 
 skate without a doubt representative of that statement. The control scheme and realism make the 
 game a breath of fresh air for the skating game genre.
  
  First, and most important in a game like this, the controls. The flickit style of controls is an 
 innovative new take on how you control your body and the board. The right analog stick represents 
 your feet. Pull down and flick it up, and you'll perform a simple ollie. Pull it down and flick 
 it up and to the right, and you'll perform a flip trick. The left stick controls your body movement. 
 Push it to the left to rotate left, push to the right, rotate to the right. Pushing the left stick 
 up or down immediately after getting in the air and you'll initiate a flip. The triggers are your 
 grabs. It really is an excellent system. It really provides a more realistic feel to perform tricks.
 
  
  Graphically, the game is also excellent. The environment, which varies from suburbs to a downtown 
 area is very polished and really provides a distinctive feel for each of the gameworld's areas. 
 The animations are pretty fluid, although sometimes the physics can leave you scratching your head. 
 A few times, I've found myself slamming into a wall and bouncing right back around in the opposite 
 direction or finding myself attempting a grind on a short wall only to do a sort of hovering perpendicular 
 to the ground move. But it really doesn't happen that often, so it surely doesn't detract from 
 a great looking game.
  
  Sound is solid as well. The ambient sounds offer everything from the sounds of pedestrians talking 
 to the thumping of a radio playing music at the local skating hotspot. You can also choose to play 
 music constantly if you wish, although I found it more engrossing to choose the ambient playlist. 
 Not only does it give a more realistic soundtrack, but it also provides the ability to locate popular 
 skating areas by allowing you to hone in on the music that plays at such locations.
  
  Online play comes in either competitive modes or a free skate mode. I haven't had much experience 
 with the competitive modes as of yet, but the freeskate allows you to join a few friends and just 
 explore the city to find your own lines and pull of tricks as you feel fit. Connections are pretty 
 solid, although when lag happens, it can be frustrating.
  
  While you won't see the wacky, off-the-wall Tony Hawk style tricks of grinding across power lines 
 on your way to pulling that backflip grab move as you jump to a rooftop, skate really provides 
 an immersive experience. The challenge of pulling off a difficult trick using the flickit controls 
 really provides a sense of accomplishment lacking in other button mashing style skating games.
 
  
  All in all, skate provides an excellent fresh approach to a proven game genre. Tony Hawk has provided 
 some great fun over the last several years, but skate's more realistic approach to skating and 
 the ability to identify and capitalize on your own skating lines is a great experience. 
::::::

UserName: sonofares
Rating: 10
Date: Sep 14, 2007 9:09 pm PT
Review:  From the opening scenes in this game where we get to see the cast of pro skaters like Danny Way, 
 Mike Carroll, and even Mark Gonzales, I have been extremely impressed. I played the demo for this 
 game so I knew enough to know I had to get the game.......... but.......... it blows the demo in 
 the dust. I skateboarded for 16 years and got to the level of sponsored am. It was my life for 
 a long time growing up. I ate, slept, and breathed skating but as I got older (and larger) those 
 days and memories faded. The Tony Hawk games were fun and were cool in the sense you could do all 
 these crazy tricks but really for the most part wasn't realistic. And just like in the real skating 
 world where Danny Way came on the scene when Tony Hawk had been dominating the contests for years............. and 
 started taking over....... it looks like he's gonna take over the video game skate world. For one 
 thing, this is the most revolutionary game I've played in a very long time. This is much like a 
 skateboarding simulation. I've never played a game that actually gives you the feeling of doing 
 that activity as much as this game does. It actually gives me the same feeling I would get when 
 I used to skate and pop a big ollie to nose grind....... or a pop a huge ollie over a hip or a big 
 ollie grab or kickflip or whatever. The controls have been revolutionized and all the crazy button 
 mashing is done. If the Tony Hawk games are going to compete with this, they're gonna really have 
 to make some changes. If there's a single thing wrong with this game I haven't found it. From the 
 moment I popped it in my console I stayed in awe. It truly is awe-inspiring and has to be played 
 to be believed. I can't even believe they could make a game that controls so intuitively as this 
 game. It has really broken down the physics of skateboarding and matched that to our little XBOX 
 wireless controller. Much props to the creators of this incredible game. And thank you for allowing 
 me to have that feeling of skating again.

UserName: Alex071093
Rating: 8.5
Date: Sep 19, 2007 4:03 pm PT
Review:  In EA's skate the gameplay feels just right, using the sticks for tricks was a revolutionary idea. 
 In this game skating is just like it is when you're really doing it, its fun and you feel good 
 about yourself when you do something. Don't get me wrong, The Tony Hawk Series was fun but its 
 just not realistic when it comes to real world skateboarding, and since when does grinding make 
 you go faster? Skate is a relief from the Tony Hawk games. Finally theres a game that when you 
 play it you feel like you've accomplished something. Another thing that was a great idea was to 
 get rid of the grind button, why would you need to push a button to get on a rail? Tony Hawk games 
 were cool and theres always people that like them, I just thought that was'nt real world skateboarding, 
 They were fun for a while as far as story goes, but at last theres a game you can play and feel 
 like you're actually skating. Other than all the good things about this game, the music is pretty 
 O. K. it just doesnt completely fit in sometimes, and thats something that Activision is good at, 
 putting good music into a Tony Hawk game. Even though the gameplay feels natural through out the 
 game, in some challenges the sticks just arent enough to complete it without going into a hard 
 difficulty. Another (not so good) thing is the online multiplayer, sometimes a bunch of skaters 
 are put into a tight spot, and this leads to everybody ending up on the floor without getting a 
 solid trick down. This game is Pretty good for EA's first big step into the skateboarding genre, 
 even though it could use some tuning.

Review:  Where to begin... I used to skate years ago. I skated for about 3 or 4 years and LOVED it. I'm

 skating. Anyways on the the review:

 that doing the trick you actually wanted to do can be challenging. The memories this game brought 
 back was great. I used to watch a bunch of skate videos and loved listening to the music on the 
 skate videos like black sabbath, Iron maiden, the who, queen, the list goes on and on. Actually 
 skating as a child was what really got me into music as well. So popping on those old skating tunes 
 I used hear during my favorite skate videos while playing this game just hit me like a ton of bricks 
 with pure awesomeness and a rush of good ol' memories. ****ing ****!!! I'm sorry, I won't frolic 
 down memory lane anymore. Aw screw it. I'll just keep this as short and sweet as possible. Me being 
 a former skateboarder (went out and bought a skateboard again though because of this game) totally 
 appreciate this game for what it is. And I'm VERY sure anyone who has EVER skated before will appreciate 
 this game as well. I hear and see people knock this because it's hard and you have to keep re-trying 
 tricks. BOO HOO! You have to do that in real life and real life isn't easy in the beginning either!!!

 done for me and skateboarding games in general very much, but I have to say I'm more of a Skate 
 fan now than Tony Hawk. Either way I'm glad something like this came out because to me Tony Hawk 
 started going a bit downhill after 3 And I was starting to get a little tired and craved something 
 new. EA, as much as I don't like you very much, and to the developers thank you for this game.

UserName: loogs
Rating: 10
Date: Sep 14, 2007 5:47 am PT
Review:  What do fight night round 3, def jam icon and a couple of other games have in common? They all 
 try to utilize the analog sticks for total control of a game, and fail miserably. What we have 
 here with skate is an excellent approach to the skating and video game chemistry. I, like everyone 
 else, have been playing tony hawk forever. Up until last years game when I said to myself, Im 
 done. Ive had enough of ollieing over buildings and grinding on telephone wires. I have been a 
 skater all my life and the hawk series is all we had. Not anymore.
  
  Skate is awesome. There are many reasons why this game is so good. Ill name a few. Well start with 
 graphics. Theyre sweet. What else would you expect from EA games on the 360. The characters look 
 good. The boards are cool and the town itself is nicely done. Nothing too surprising here.
  
  The sound is awesome. The effects of the board snapping off the ground, the wheels spinning 
 while in mid-air, the wheels scraping the pavement during a slide, the cracks in the sidewalk as 
 you roll over them and everything else about the sound effects are spot on. Im not a fan of the 
 soundtrack but thats irrelevant considering you can play music off of your hard drive, iPod or 
 console.
  
  What makes this game so special though are the controls. Every time I perform a trick it feels 
 right. I love what they did here. Approaching a set of stairs or a curb or anything and popping 
 that board is so gratifying. The other thing that makes this game great is its realism. Now, lets 
 not get crazy. Its still a game and there are tons of scenarios that are unrealistic but, what 
 makes them unrealistic is this. While doing a 360 kick flip over a hand rail on a set of stairs 
 15 feet high is possible, nobody in their right mind would try it because the worst result would 
 mean certain death in real life, thats the thing with this game. You could pull of most of the 
 tricks youll attempt, in real life, but if you made a mistake it would cost you your life. So 
 what it does is enable you to fantasize about what it would be like to pull off insane tricks that 
 you probably wouldnt try in real life. Your tricks can also vary from being ultra realistic to 
 not so realistic. Its up to you. The other thing is the open ended city. Like grand theft auto, 
 you could find yourself skating around for hours just popping tricks and trying to find sweet lines.
 
  
  Like most video games, this game has some glitches. The quirks in this game are a little different 
 from all other games and are actually very comical. Youll see some weird stuff but nothing that 
 will frustrate you. I see some reviews saying the rag doll effect on the bails are dumb, Ill tell 
 you right now they will have you in tears at some points. It does a great job at separating the 
 fantasy from the reality. When you see your skater do a 15 foot slide on his head it just doesnt 
 get any better than that.
  
  I dont really have anything bad to say about this game. I love it, and if you have any affection 
 for skateboarding, you will too. And its a fantastic alternative to what has become a drab and 
 boring series in the tony hawk games. The only thing bad I could think of is, if you are a hardcore 
 vert skater and you are looking for that in this game you will be disappointed. The large ramp 
 jump and the ramps at the x-games event are great but, there really isnt any hardcore vert skating 
 in the game. That doesnt bother me one bit but it might bother some. Street skaters rejoice. I 
 will own this game until its sequel comes out. This is one of those special games you will not 
 want to trade in. I got to go SKATE. 
::::::

::::::
UserName: SaladinSnake
Rating: 9.5
Date: Sep 12, 2007 8:31 am PT
Review:  This is my nice little review for the demo version of skate. I'll post a review for the real version 
 when it decides to come out. So here goes:
  
  Graphics: This game looks astounding. The small area your given in the demo is beautifully rendered, 
 and looks like a real public skatepark, (albiet a skatepark made by a town with a lot of free money.) 
 filled with rails, stairs, manny pads, and plenty of other goodies. However, it's the skater animations 
 that steal the show. From something as simple as pushing, to landing a frontside flip sketchy, 
 and watching your skater fight for balance, everything looks like it should. The bails look appropriately 
 painful, and my friends and I can find real creative ways to rack our nuts off of some interesting 
 obstacles. The other skaters that populate the world actually skate, and do more than just the 
 odd kickflip, though i've noticed they all skate mongo (push with their front foot instead of their 
 back foot) . It's also insanely fun to run into them. One minor quibble though, the skater's hands 
 seem a little blocky, but this is just nitpicking. Overall, the graphics do a real good job.
  
  Gameplay: Ah yes, the gameplay. To say Skate changes the usual control scheme is an understatement. 
 Skate invents a control scheme. As everyone probably already knows by now, Skate makes liberal 
 use of the right analog stick for it's tricks. This is genius. The amount of technical expertise 
 required to pull off a nollie flip to manual is incredible. To do tricks in this game, you've got 
 to think like a skater, and visualize how your feet would move to do a given trick. Now i'd think 
 that an actual skater might have an advantage here, but after a few hours, everyone can trick like 
 a pro. One of the best things about this game is the sense of accomplishment. Doing a 360 flip 
 to manual to kickflip out feels as amazing as it should. You'll feel proud of yourself for accomplishing 
 the smallest of tasks. The game also challenges you to come up with your own lines, and does not 
 give you the ability to grind from one end of the world to the other.
  
  Sound: The sound is topnotch. Everything from the wheels rolling on different surfaces, to the 
 bone jarring sounds of breaking your legs, the game sounds great. Overall: I can't wait for Skate. 
 With one day left, i'm losing sleep over the damn thing. I think this game will do very well, and 
 i'm looking forward to it.
